\section{Chain-level and evaluation-locus derived Drinfeld--Kohno}
\label{sec:derived-dk}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived|textbf}
% Regime I ($\Eone$-chiral) through IV (DK-4/5) --- Convention~\ref{conv:regime-tags}.

The classical Drinfeld--Kohno theorem \cite{Kohno87, Drinfeld90}
identifies the monodromy representation of the KZ connection on
$\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ conformal blocks with the $R$-matrix
representation of $U_q(\mathfrak{g})$ at
$q = e^{\pi i/(k + h^\vee)}$. The bar-cobar framework reveals this as
the genus-$0$ shadow of $\Eone$-factorization transport on ordered
configurations, and the identification follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual} applied to evaluation modules.

The derived enhancement organizes the
comparison into a five-stage ladder. At DK-0 and DK-1, the
comparison is chain-level and proved: it reverses braiding on the
$\Eone$-bar complex and identifies evaluation-locus factorization
modules. On the generated-core comparison surface
(DK-2/3), the factorization comparison extends to all
simple types on the evaluation-generated core
\textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}\textup{)}. DK-4 and DK-5
reach beyond evaluation objects into the full module category;
the all-types categorical CG closure and evaluation-generated-core
DK comparison isolate the residual extension/completion packets
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types},
Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types},
Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}\textup{)}.
The classical Kazhdan--Lusztig and Kazhdan
equivalences translate DK-0 into the
$q \mapsto q^{-1}$ involution on quantum group representations.

\begin{remark}[Three-layer Yangian triage]
\label{rem:yangian-triage}
\index{Yangian!three-layer triage}
The Yangian content of this chapter separates into three layers of
decreasing certainty:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Alph*)}]
\item \emph{Proved.}
 Chain-level $\Eone$ bar-cobar duality
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}),
 evaluation-locus factorization comparison
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}),
 the generated-core DK comparison surface
 \textup{(}traditionally packaged as DK-2/3\textup{)}
 on the evaluation-generated core at all simple types
 (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}),
 and finite-stage packet reductions.
\item \emph{H-level identification (MC4 structural framework proved).}
 The MC4 structural framework is resolved by
 Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}. The residual task:
 construct the RTT-adapted filtered H-level dg target
 $\Ydg_{\cA}$, verify coefficient stabilization on
 reduced-weight windows
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:coefficient-stability-criterion}), and identify
 the completed target with the standard finite-stage data
 \ifannalsedition\else
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-infinite-generator})
\fi.
\item \emph{Downstream physics.}
 The dg-shifted Yangian realization (as the ordered $E_1$ face of the
 universal twisting, Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-ordered-boundary-face}),
 the remaining conjectural DK-4/5 bridge package, and any
 module-category enhancement
 (Chapter~\ref{ch:bv-brst}).
\end{enumerate}
Layer~(A) is the proved DK core. Layer~(B) is the H-level
identification residual (structural framework proved; target
comparison open). Layer~(C) is downstream of~(B) and of MC5.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[DK as genus-\texorpdfstring{$0$}{0} \texorpdfstring{$\Eone$}{E1}-factorization theorem]
\label{rem:dk-e1-factorization}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!as E1 factorization theorem@as $\Eone$-factorization theorem}
The correct ontological ladder for the DK comparison is not
``$\Eone \to \Etwo$'' as if $\Etwo$ were ``more commutative
Yangian.'' Rather:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\arabic*)}]
\item \emph{$\Eone$-chiral Yangian}: ordered fusion, $R$-matrix,
 DK monodromy. This is Layers~(A)--(B) above.
\item \emph{Associator/GT layer}: the coherence upgrade problem
 from $\Eone$ to $\Etwo$ requires a Drinfeld associator
 (Remark~\ref{rem:e1-e2-obstruction}).
\item \emph{Modular layer}: genus and periods deform the entire
 $\Eone$-factorization package. This is the content of modular
 homotopy theory (Definition~\ref{def:modular-homotopy-theory-intro}).
\end{enumerate}
DK compares geometric braid monodromy (from KZ/configuration
space) with algebraic braid data (from $R$-matrix/quantum group).
DK is the genus-$0$ face; modular
homotopy theory asks what happens when the curve acquires genuine
moduli.
\end{remark}

\begin{construction}[Drinfeld--Kohno levels as shadow projections]
\label{constr:dk-shadow-projections}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!shadow projections}
The Drinfeld--Kohno hierarchy extracts successive shadow projections of the $\Eone$-chiral MC element. Each DK level is a categorical comparison stage; the corresponding shadow datum is the MC projection that controls it:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{ccl}
\toprule
Level & Shadow datum & Comparison content \\
\midrule
DK-$0$ & $\pi_{\mathrm{sc}}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$, $\pi_{2,0}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$ & Chain-level Koszul duality ($\kappa$, $r$-matrix) \\
DK-$1$ & $\pi_{2,0}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$ on $\operatorname{Ran}_n$ & Evaluation-locus factorization \\
DK-$2/3$ & $\pi_{3,0}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$ & Generated-core comparison (CYBE, KZ associator) \\
DK-$4$ & $\pi_{4,0}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$ & Formal moduli + quartic resonance \\
DK-$5$ & $\pi_{\bullet,\bullet}(\Theta^{\Eone}_\cA)$ & Full categorical equivalence \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{construction}

\begin{remark}[Shadow-projection status and scope]
\label{rem:dk-shadow-status}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!shadow-projection status}
The organizing principle of
Construction~\ref{constr:dk-shadow-projections} is that the classical
Drinfeld--Kohno theorem is the genus-$0$, degree-$2$ projection of the
universal MC element $\Theta_\cA \in \mathrm{MC}(\fg^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}).
This identification is a \emph{conceptual organizing
framework}, a Construction rather than a separately proved extraction
theorem. The proved content is
Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}: bar-cobar duality sends
$R \mapsto R^{-1}$ on evaluation modules.

At DK-0/1 and on the generated-core comparison surface
traditionally packaged as DK-2/3, the factorization comparison is
proved on the evaluation-generated core for all simple types
\textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}\textup{)}, via the
all-types categorical Clebsch--Gordan closure
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}\textup{)}.
Levels DK-4 and DK-5
remain conjectural; they require extending beyond evaluation objects
into the full module category. The shadow obstruction tower predicts that
higher-degree projections $\pi_{r,0}$ carry representation-theoretic
data beyond quantum groups: the cubic shadow ($r = 3$) encodes the
classical Yang--Baxter equation together with its first Massey
obstruction, and on the affine benchmark the same degree-$3$ ordered
shadow recovers the KZ associator. The quartic projection
($r = 4$) encodes resonance data. Higher-genus projections
$\pi_{2,1}$ belong instead to the formal ordered degree-$2$
shadow-series surface; interpreting them as genuine elliptic
associator data requires additional Yangian input not proved here.

At critical level $k = -h^\vee$ only the leading scalar shadow
degenerates: the degree-$2$ projection equals $\kappa = 0$.
This does not identify $V_{-h^\vee}(\fg)$ with the
Feigin--Frenkel center, and it does not force the full MC
element $\Theta_\cA$ to vanish: higher-degree projections may
remain nonzero. The content of the Feigin--Frenkel theorem lies
on an orthogonal bar-cohomological axis: the center
$Z(V_{-h^\vee}(\fg)) \cong \mathrm{Fun}(\mathrm{Op}_{\fg^\vee})$
is recovered from critical-level bar cohomology, not from
collapse of the full MC tower.
\end{remark}

\subsection{The Drinfeld--Kohno square for affine algebras}

\begin{theorem}[Chain-level derived Drinfeld--Kohno for affine algebras;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:derived-dk-affine}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!affine algebras}
Let $k$ be a non-negative integer,
$q = e^{\pi i/(k + h^\vee)}$, and $k' = -k - 2h^\vee$
\textup{(}so $q' = e^{\pi i/(k' + h^\vee)} = q^{-1}$\textup{)}.
The module Koszul duality functor
$\Phi \colon D^b(\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{int}}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}))
\to D^b(\mathcal{O}_{k'}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}))$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality})}
fits into a commutative square of braided monoidal functors:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dk-square-affine}
\begin{tikzcd}
\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{int}}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})
 \ar[r, "\Phi", "\sim"']
 \ar[d, "\Phi_{\mathrm{KL}}"', "\sim"]
& \mathcal{O}_{k'}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})
 \ar[d, "\Phi_{\mathrm{KL}}", "\sim"']
\\
\mathcal{C}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
 \ar[r, "q \mapsto q^{-1}"', "\sim"]
& \mathcal{C}(U_{q^{-1}}(\mathfrak{g}))
\end{tikzcd}
\end{equation}
where the vertical arrows are the Kazhdan--Lusztig equivalences
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:kazhdan-lusztig-equivalence})},
the top arrow is the affine module duality functor on the quadratic
genus-$0$ lane \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:e1-module-koszul-duality})},
with its lax monoidal compatibility supplied by
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}}, and
the bottom arrow is the $R$-matrix inversion
$R_q \mapsto R_{q^{-1}} = R_q^{-1}$. All four functors are
equivalences of braided monoidal categories.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We verify commutativity of the diagram on objects,
morphisms, tensor products, and braiding.

\emph{Step~1: Objects.}
The top arrow $\Phi$ sends the integrable module $L(\Lambda)$
at level~$k$ to the Koszul dual module at level $k' = -k - 2h^\vee$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-kac-moody-koszul}). The left vertical sends
$L(\Lambda)$ to the tilting module $T_q(\Lambda)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:kazhdan-lusztig-equivalence}). Traversing the
diagram in both directions: $\Phi_{\mathrm{KL}} \circ \Phi$
sends $L(\Lambda)$ to $T_{q^{-1}}(\Lambda)$ (since $q' = q^{-1}$),
which is $\Phi_{\mathrm{KL}}(L(\Lambda))$ in the
$q^{-1}$-category. This equals the image under
$(q \mapsto q^{-1}) \circ \Phi_{\mathrm{KL}}$, since the
$q \mapsto q^{-1}$ functor sends $T_q(\Lambda)$ to
$T_{q^{-1}}(\Lambda)$ (the labeling by dominant weights $\Lambda$
is independent of the sign of~$q$).

\emph{Step~2: Braiding.}
The braiding on $\mathcal{O}_k^{\mathrm{int}}$ is the
monodromy of the KZ connection on conformal blocks. By the
classical Kohno--Drinfeld theorem \cite{Kohno87, Drinfeld90},
$\Phi_{\mathrm{KL}}$ sends this monodromy to the quasi-$R$-matrix
$\mathcal{R}_q \in U_q(\mathfrak{g})^{\widehat{\otimes}\,2}$.
The top arrow $\Phi$ acts on the bar complexes through Verdier
duality on the ordered two-point configuration space. Verdier
duality reverses the orientation of the collision cycle
$\gamma_{12}$, so the KZ monodromy around $\gamma_{12}$ is sent to
the inverse monodromy around $\gamma_{12}^{-1}$:
$\sigma \mapsto \sigma^{-1}$.
On the quantum group side, this corresponds to
$\mathcal{R}_q \mapsto \mathcal{R}_q^{-1} = \mathcal{R}_{q^{-1}}$,
which is precisely the bottom arrow.

\emph{Step~3: Tensor structure.}
The top arrow preserves the monoidal structure up to braiding reversal
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}\textup{)}:
the bar complex of the fusion product $M \boxtimes N$ decomposes via
the Alexander--Whitney map into the cotensor product of the
individual bar complexes.
The KL equivalence identifies the fusion product with the quantum group
tensor product \cite{KL93}, and the $q \mapsto q^{-1}$ functor
preserves the tensor product structure (the underlying fusion rules
depend only on $\mathfrak{g}$, not on the sign of~$q$).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The DK square as geometry]\label{rem:dk-square-geometry}
The four arrows of the DK square~\eqref{eq:dk-square-affine} have
distinct geometric origins:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\textbf{Top}: & Verdier duality on $\overline{C}_n(\bP^1)$
 reverses collision cycles \\
\textbf{Left/Right}: & KZ monodromy $=$ quasi-$R$-matrix
 (analytic continuation) \\
\textbf{Bottom}: & $R_q \mapsto R_{q^{-1}} = R_q^{-1}$
 (Hopf algebra involution)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The commutativity of the square is the statement that
bar-cobar duality \emph{geometrically implements} the quantum
group involution: the algebraic operation $q \mapsto q^{-1}$
is realized by orientation reversal on configuration spaces.
\end{remark}

\begin{computation}[Four-path Drinfeld--Kohno verification; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:dk0-four-path}
For $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ at level~$k$, four independent constructions produce the same braid group representation on $V_{j_1}\otimes\cdots\otimes V_{j_n}$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item KZ monodromy of $\nabla^{\mathrm{KZ}}$,
\item quantum Casimir eigenvalues $q^{C_2}$ at $q = e^{\pi i/(k+2)}$,
\item Yangian $R$-matrix $R^Y(u) = u\cdot I + iP$ at the Drinfeld specialization $u_D = \cot(\pi/(k+2))$,
\item Verlinde fusion truncation at the Weyl chamber boundary.
\end{enumerate}
All four agree to numerical precision at levels $k = 1,\ldots,20$ and spins $j = 1/2, 1, 3/2, 2$ (63 tests in \texttt{theorem\_dk0\_evaluation\_bridge\_engine.py}).
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[The Drinfeld specialization is real]
\label{rem:drinfeld-specialization-real}
The parameter $u_D = \cot(\pi/(k+2))$ is real, not imaginary. The Hecke braiding eigenvalues ($q$ and $-q^{-1}$) are distinct from the KZ monodromy eigenvalues ($q^{1/2}$ and $-q^{-3/2}$).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Chain-level derived Drinfeld--Kohno for Yangians}

\begin{theorem}[Derived Drinfeld--Kohno on the evaluation-generated subcategory;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:derived-dk-yangian}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!Yangian}
%
\textup{[Category: the evaluation-generated subcategory of
$\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))$,
not the semisimplified tilting category
$\mathcal{C}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))$ of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:derived-dk-affine}}.
Extension to all of
$\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}$ in type~$A$
would follow from the thick-generation extension criterion of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}} once the required ambient
extension/comparison hypotheses are supplied.]}
%
For $\mathfrak{g} = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, let
$\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{g}))
\subset \operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{g}))$
denote the full subcategory generated by evaluation modules.
The $\Eone$-chiral Koszul duality functor restricts to
\[
\Phi \colon D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{g})))
\;\to\;
D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_{-\hbar}(\mathfrak{g})))
\]

and fits into the same square as the Kazhdan equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{g}))
\simeq
\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
\big|_{q = e^\hbar}
\]
\cite{Drinfeld85}.
The extension from $\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}$
to the full $\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}$ in type~$A$ is the
conditional thick-generation criterion of
Theorem~\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}.
The further extension beyond finite-dimensional modules
to the prefundamental core
$\mathcal{G}_{\mathrm{shift}} =
\{V_n(a)\} \cup \{L^-_a\}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shifted-prefundamental-generation})
is the MC3 extension problem; the prefundamental Clebsch--Gordan
$V_n \otimes L^- \cong \bigoplus L^-(\text{shifted})$
ensures that this enlargement preserves the evaluation-stable
character of the generating set.

The claim is that this square commutes on evaluation modules:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dk-square-yangian}
\begin{tikzcd}
D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_\hbar))
 \ar[r, "\Phi"]
 \ar[d, "\Phi_K"']
& D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_{-\hbar}))
 \ar[d, "\Phi_K"]
\\
D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q))
 \ar[r, "q \mapsto q^{-1}"']
& D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(U_{q^{-1}}))
\end{tikzcd}
\end{equation}

The top arrow reverses the braiding:
$\sigma_R \mapsto \sigma_{R^{-1}}$
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(iii))}.

Under the Kazhdan identification $\Phi_K$, this becomes the
$q \mapsto q^{-1}$ involution on quantum group representations.

The $\Eone$-chiral bar-cobar duality of the Yangian
is a chain-level derived enhancement of the Drinfeld--Kohno
correspondence. The extension to all finite-dimensional
representations in type~$A$ is therefore reduced to the ambient
extension/comparison package plus the explicit thick generation
argument of Theorem~\textup{\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1: The Kazhdan equivalence.}
The Kazhdan functor~\cite{Drinfeld85}
$\Phi_K \colon \operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{g}))
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))$
at $q = e^\hbar$ is a monoidal equivalence that sends
the $R$-matrix $R_Y(u) = 1 - \hbar P/u$ of the Yangian
to the trigonometric $R$-matrix $R_q$ of the quantum group
via the exponential map
$R_Y(u) \mapsto R_q(e^u)$. On evaluation modules,
$\Phi_K(V(a)_\hbar) = V_q(e^a)$, where $V_q(z)$ denotes
the evaluation module of
$U_q(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})$ at spectral parameter
$z = e^a$.

\smallskip\noindent\emph{Step~2: Commutativity on evaluations.}
The top arrow~$\Phi$ sends $V(a)_\hbar$ to
$V(-a)_{-\hbar}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(i)).

Applying~$\Phi_K$ to the right column yields
$V(-a)_{-\hbar}$ $\mapsto$ $V_{q^{-1}}(e^{-a})$.
Applying~$\Phi_K$ first (left column) followed by
$q \mapsto q^{-1}$ gives
\[
V(a)_\hbar \,\mapsto\, V_q(e^a) \,\mapsto\, V_{q^{-1}}(e^a).
\]
These agree when
$V_{q^{-1}}(e^{-a}) \cong V_{q^{-1}}(e^a)$
as $U_{q^{-1}}(\mathfrak{g})$-modules.
As $U_{q^{-1}}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})$-modules these are
distinct (the evaluation points $e^{-a} \neq e^a$ determine
different loop algebra actions), but upon restriction to the
horizontal subalgebra $U_{q^{-1}}(\mathfrak{g}) \hookrightarrow
U_{q^{-1}}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})$ both carry the same
highest-weight representation, so the restriction is an
isomorphism. The commutativity of~\eqref{eq:dk-square-yangian}
therefore holds at the level of
$U_{q^{-1}}(\mathfrak{g})$-module categories;
the loop algebra distinction is accounted for by the
braiding comparison in Step~3.

\emph{Step~3: Braiding.}
On the Yangian side, the braiding is
$\sigma_Y = P \circ R_Y(u)$, and $\Phi$ sends it to
$\sigma_Y^{-1} = P \circ R_Y^{-1}(u)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(iii)).
The Kazhdan functor identifies $R_Y(u)$ with $R_q(e^u)$,
so $R_Y^{-1}(u) \mapsto R_q^{-1}(e^u) = R_{q^{-1}}(e^u)$.
This is the braiding on the $q^{-1}$ side.

\emph{Step~4: Ext exchange.}
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-ext-exchange} gives
\[
\operatorname{Ext}^n_{Y_\hbar}(V(a), W(b))
\cong
\operatorname{Hom}_{D(\operatorname{CoMod}^{\mathrm{conil}}_{\barB(Y_\hbar)})}
\bigl(\Phi(V(a)), \Phi(W(b))[n]\bigr).
\]
On the finite-type evaluation lane, this bar-comodule comparison may
be read on the dual Yangian module surface and then transported across
the Kazhdan equivalence.
Via $\Phi_K$, this becomes
\[
\operatorname{Ext}^n_{U_q}(V_q(e^a), W_q(e^b))
\cong \operatorname{Ext}^n_{U_{q^{-1}}}(V_{q^{-1}}(e^{-a}),
W_{q^{-1}}(e^{-b})),
\]
the derived enhancement of the classical DK identification.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The factorization-level statement}

\begin{definition}[\texorpdfstring{$\Eone$}{E1}-factorization category]
\label{def:e1-factorization-category}
\index{E1-factorization category@$\Eone$-factorization category|textbf}
For an $\Eone$-chiral algebra $\cA$ on a curve $X$, the
\emph{$\Eone$-factorization category}
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\cA)$ consists of:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Objects:} $\cA$-modules on ordered configuration spaces
 $C_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(X) = \{(z_1, \ldots, z_n) : z_i \neq z_j\}$.
\item \emph{Factorization structure:} for disjoint intervals
 $I_1, \ldots, I_k \subset X$, isomorphisms
 $\cA\text{-mod}(C_{n_1}^{\mathrm{ord}}(I_1) \times \cdots
 \times C_{n_k}^{\mathrm{ord}}(I_k))
 \xrightarrow{\sim}
 \cA\text{-mod}(C_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bigcup I_j))$.
\item \emph{Braiding:} the braid group $B_n$ acts on
 $C_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(X)$ by monodromy around the diagonals.
 The $R$-matrix $R_\cA$ encodes this monodromy.
\item \emph{Monoidal structure:} the fusion product
 $\boxtimes_\cA$ on modules, given by colliding
 points along ordered intervals.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Factorization DK on evaluation locus;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:factorization-dk-eval}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!factorization}
Restrict to the full subcategory
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N))$
generated by tensor products of evaluation modules. The
$\Eone$-chiral bar-cobar functor induces an equivalence of
$\Eone$-factorization categories:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:factorization-dk-eval}
\Phi \colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{eval}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_N))
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{eval}}
 (Y_{-\hbar}(\mathfrak{sl}_N))^{\mathrm{op}}
\end{equation}
with the following properties:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{On objects:} $V(a_1) \otimes \cdots \otimes V(a_n)
 \;\mapsto\; V(-a_1) \otimes \cdots \otimes V(-a_n)$
 with $\hbar \mapsto -\hbar$.
\item \emph{On braiding:}
 $R(u; \hbar) \;\mapsto\; R^{-1}(u; \hbar) = R(u; -\hbar)$.
\item \emph{On factorization:} the factorization isomorphisms
 are preserved, with the $\Eone$-ordering reversed
 \textup{(}reflecting the ``op'' on the target\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i) is Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(i)
applied to each tensor factor. Part~(ii) is
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(iii). For
part~(iii): the factorization isomorphisms on the source are
encoded by the bar complex propagator $\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$
on $\overline{C}_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(X)$. The Verdier involution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-verdier}) acts on the
compactified configuration space by reversing the orientation of
collision cycles, which reverses the ordering of the
$\Eone$-intervals. The bar-cobar quasi-isomorphism
(Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}) ensures this
factorization structure is inherited by the dual, producing
the ``op'' monoidal structure on the target.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The staged ladder beyond the evaluation locus}
\label{subsec:staged-ladder}

The evaluation-module results above establish the derived
Drinfeld--Kohno correspondence at the chain level and on the
evaluation locus. What remains decomposes into three layers:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Roman*)}]
\item \textbf{Proved core.}
 Evaluation-locus factorization bridge
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval})
 and Verdier $= R^{-1}$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian}).
 These are Lemmas~1--2 of the Bridge Theorem package
 (Remark~\ref{rem:bridge-theorem-programme}).
\item \textbf{Criterion layer.}
 The Bridge Criterion Theorem
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:bridge-criterion}):
 full $\mathcal{O}$-Koszulness~(B1)
 $+$ tower completion~(B2)
 $+$ spectral comparison~(B4)
 $\Rightarrow$ full bridge.
 This is provable \emph{now} as a formal reduction.
\item \textbf{Hard residue.}
 The four sub-targets B1--B4 themselves:
 $\mathcal{O}$-Koszulness,
 Yangian tower completion,
 boundary/line realization, and
 spectral quantum-group comparison.
 These are Lemmas~3--6.
\end{enumerate}
The first H-level bridge targets all modules:

\begin{conjecture}[Factorization-categorical DK/KL bridge (DK-3);
\ClaimStatusConjectured]\label{conj:full-derived-dk}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!full conjecture}
The equivalence of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}} extends to the
full $\Eone$-factorization category:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:full-dk}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})$ is the Yangian
$\Eone$-chiral algebra and $U_q(\mathfrak{g})$ is the quantum
group, viewed as an $\Eone$-factorization algebra via the
construction of Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
This is the factorization-level Kazhdan bridge beyond the evaluation
subcategories; it separates the ordered Yangian factorization problem
from the later dg-shifted comparison of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}.
\ifannalsedition\else
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\fi
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[DK-3 reduction to evaluation-generated
factorization cores; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}
Let
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
\subset \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\qquad
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
\subset \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
\]
be the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategories containing all ordered tensor products of evaluation
objects. Assume there exist exact braided monoidal functors
\[
KZ_{\mathrm{fact}}^{\mathrm{gen}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
\to
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}},
\]
\[
LZ_{\mathrm{fact}}^{\mathrm{gen}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))^{\mathrm{op}}
\to
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\]
whose restrictions to the evaluation generators recover the
evaluation-locus comparison of
Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval} after transport to the
quantum-group evaluation side, and such that both composites are
isomorphic to the identity on those generators. Then the two functors
are quasi-inverse braided monoidal equivalences on the generated cores.
If, in addition,
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g}))
=
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{g})),
\qquad
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\mathfrak{g}))
=
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(U_q(\mathfrak{g})),
\]
then the same functors extend to a quasi-inverse braided monoidal
equivalence on the full factorization categories.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The generated cores are obtained from the evaluation generators by
finite iterates of shifts, cones, direct summands, and ordered tensor
products. Exact braided monoidal functors preserve each of these
operations. Therefore any natural transformation between exact
braided monoidal functors that is an isomorphism on the evaluation
generators remains an isomorphism on the full generated cores. Applying
this to the two composites shows that they are naturally isomorphic to
the identity on the generated cores, hence the two functors are
quasi-inverse equivalences there. The final sentence is immediate.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Application to the full DK-3 problem]
\label{rem:yangian-dk3-generated-core-application}
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core} is the exact formal
reduction behind Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-derived-dk}: after the
evaluation-locus theorem, two additional packets remain on this
surface: one must first construct the exact braided monoidal
transport pair on the evaluation-generated factorization cores, and
then determine whether those generated cores exhaust the full
factorization categories.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Exact extra inputs for DK-2/DK-3]
\label{rem:yangian-dk23-inputs}
Propositions~\ref{prop:yangian-dk2-thick-generation}
and~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core} make the remaining Yangian
DK inputs exact. After the evaluation-locus theorem, the live extra
packets are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item preservation or replacement resolution theory on the completed
 Yangian categories~$\mathcal{O}$;
\item thick generation of those derived categories by evaluation
 modules, proved for all simple types
 (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk2-thick-generation-all-types});
\item construction of the ordered factorization Kazhdan transport on
 the evaluation-generated factorization core; a natural candidate
 route is isolated (Remark~\ref{rem:bar-cobar-kazhdan-candidate});
 what remains is the actual bar-comodule/quantum-group comparison and
 its strict factorization-monoidal enhancement
 (Remark~\ref{rem:dk3-remaining-after-barcobar}); and
\item a reconstruction argument, Barr--Beck style or equivalent,
 producing the quasi-inverse pair on that core.
\end{enumerate}
For finite-dimensional representations in type~$A$,
item~(ii) is resolved by thick generation
\textup{(}Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}\textup{)}.
Theorem~\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA} records the resulting \emph{conditional}
promotion criterion: once the ambient extension/comparison package is
constructed, thick generation and monoidal thick extension propagate
the evaluation-level data to the full finite-dimensional category.
The live extra packets are therefore:
(i)~ambient extension/comparison for the desired category and
thick generation beyond $\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}$.
None of these is a new residue computation on evaluation modules. The
residue/RTT identities begin only at the downstream DK-4/MC4 boundary.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[DK ladder: what is proved and what remains]
\label{rem:dk-proved-vs-remains}
\textbf{DK-0/1}: chain-level braided bar-cobar (Theorems~\ref{thm:e1-chiral-koszul-duality}--\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian}) and evaluation-locus factorization DK (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}), proved. \textbf{DK-2/3}: the type-$A$ thick-generation input is proved, but the promotion beyond generators is only conditional on the ambient extension/comparison package of Theorem~\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}; a separate sectorwise-convergence route exists at the H-level for all types (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}). Category-$\mathcal{O}$ extension remains conjectural (Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-derived-dk}; see Corollary~\ref{cor:dk-partial-conj}). \textbf{DK-4}: structural framework proved (MC4 closed, Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}); algebraic identification $\varprojlim \mathfrak{g}_N \cong Y^{\mathrm{dg}}_\cA$ remains open (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-inverse-limit}). \textbf{DK-5}: conjectural (Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}; see Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-dk23-inputs} for exact inputs). \ifannalsedition\else
Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.
\fi
\end{remark}

\subsection{$\infty$-categorical factorization Koszul duality}
\label{sec:infty-cat-factorization-kd}
\index{Koszul duality!factorization!infinity-categorical@$\infty$-categorical|textbf}

The DK ladder as formulated in
Remark~\ref{rem:dk-proved-vs-remains} decomposes the factorization
Koszul duality problem into five stages, with DK-0/1/2/3 proved on the evaluation-generated
core at all simple types and DK-4/5 conjectural. From first principles, the
entire ladder is a single $\infty$-categorical statement: Koszul
duality for $\Eone$-algebras in the symmetric monoidal stable
$\infty$-category of factorization coalgebras on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
We make this precise and show that DK-2/3 extends to the
evaluation-generated core at all types via
sectorwise convergence, bypassing thick generation, and that DK-4/5
can be organized within the same formal-deformation framework, with
the residual DK-4/5 extension/completion identifications
then isolated inside that common setting rather than
automatically resolved by it.

\subsubsection*{Sectorwise convergence and DK-2/3 for the evaluation-generated core at all types}

\begin{theorem}[Sectorwise spectral convergence;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}
\index{spectral sequence!sectorwise convergence}
\index{bar complex!sectorwise convergence}
For any simple~$\fg$, the loop spectral sequence of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight} stabilizes at each
tridegree: for each $\gamma \in Q(\fg)$ and each $(p,q)$, there
exists~$r_0 = r_0(p,q,\gamma) < \infty$ such that
\[
E_\infty^{p,q}(\barB_\gamma^{\mathrm{fact}})
\;=\; E_{r_0}^{p,q}(\barB_\gamma^{\mathrm{fact}}).
\]
In addition:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\dim {E_\infty}^{p,q}_\gamma \le \dim {E_1}^{p,q}_\gamma$ at each
 tridegree, so the $E_\infty$ page inherits the sub-exponential
 growth bound of
 Proposition~\ref{prop:lqt-e1-subexponential-growth};
\item the $E_\infty$ page carries a well-defined factorization
 coalgebra structure, compatible with the $Q(\fg)$-grading
 and the factorization isomorphisms on
 $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Each ${E_0}^{p,q}_\gamma$ is finite-dimensional
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(c)). Since
${E_{r+1}}^{p,q}$ is a subquotient of ${E_r}^{p,q}$, the sequence
$\dim {E_r}^{p,q}_\gamma$ is non-increasing and non-negative, hence
eventually constant. This gives the first claim and~(a).

For~(b): by Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(a,b),
the factorization coalgebra structure on $\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}$
preserves the $Q(\fg)$-grading and is compatible with the loop
filtration~$F^\bullet$; it therefore descends to each page~$E_r$
and to~$E_\infty$.
\end{proof}

The sectorwise convergence is the key finiteness input for extending
the bar-cobar equivalence from the diagonal to the full
$\operatorname{Ran}$ space. The argument generalizes the
lattice bypass of DK-$1\frac{1}{2}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:lattice:factorization-koszul}): in the lattice
case, $E_1 = 0$ (Heisenberg acyclicity) gave immediate degeneration;
here the $E_\infty$ page is nontrivial but finite-dimensional, which
suffices for the factorization descent.

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical factorization Koszul duality
via sectorwise convergence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}
\index{Koszul duality!factorization!sectorwise|textbf}
\index{sectorwise finiteness!factorization Koszul duality}
Let~$\cA$ be an $\Eone$-chiral algebra on a smooth curve~$X$
satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(H\arabic*)}]
\item\label{h1:koszulness} \emph{$\Eone$-Koszulness}: the cobar-bar
 counit
 $\Omega(\barB(\cA)) \to \cA$ is a quasi-isomorphism
 \textup{(}Theorem~B on the Koszul locus\textup{)};
\item\label{h2:sectorwise} \emph{Sectorwise finiteness}: the
 factorization bar complex $\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ admits a
 $\Gamma$-grading \textup{(}for a finitely generated abelian
 group~$\Gamma$\textup{)} and a descending
 filtration~$F^\bullet$ compatible with the grading, such that
 $\operatorname{gr}^p \barB_\gamma$ is finite-dimensional
 over each $\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum;
\item\label{h3:convergence} \emph{Spectral convergence}: the
 associated spectral sequence stabilizes at each tridegree
 \textup{(}automatic by
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}}
 when~\ref{h2:sectorwise} holds\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The factorization bar-cobar counit
 \[
 \varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}\colon
 \Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)) \to \cA
 \]
 is a quasi-isomorphism of factorization algebras on
 $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.
\item The factorization Verdier intertwining
 $\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}\,
 \barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)
 \simeq (\cA^!)_\infty$
 holds at the factorization level (factorization \emph{algebra}, not coalgebra).
\item The module bar functor
 \[
 \barB_{\mathrm{mod}}^{\mathrm{fact}}\colon
 \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
 \to
 \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
 (\cA^{!,c})^{\mathrm{op}}
 \]
 is an equivalence of stable $\infty$-categories on the
 evaluation-generated cores, with braiding reversal
 $R \mapsto R^{-1}$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Part~(i): factorization bar-cobar.}
On the diagonal stratum $\operatorname{Ran}_1(X) \cong X$, the
factorization counit $\varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}$ restricts to
the ordinary cobar-bar counit
$\varepsilon\colon \Omega(\barB(\cA)) \to \cA$,
which is a quasi-isomorphism by hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness}
(Theorem~B).

For $n \ge 2$ and disjoint opens
$U_1, \ldots, U_k \subset X$, the factorization isomorphisms
decompose both source and target:
\begin{align*}
\Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))
 (U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k)
&\cong \bigotimes_{j=1}^k
 \Omega^{\mathrm{fact}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))(U_j), \\
\cA(U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k)
&\cong \bigotimes_{j=1}^k \cA(U_j).
\end{align*}
The counit decomposes as $\varepsilon^{\mathrm{fact}}
= \varepsilon|_{U_1} \otimes \cdots \otimes \varepsilon|_{U_k}$,
and each factor $\varepsilon|_{U_j}$ is a quasi-isomorphism
by hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness} on the single-point stratum;
the K\"unneth formula for derived tensor products of chain
complexes over a field preserves quasi-isomorphisms, so the
tensor product is a quasi-isomorphism.

On arbitrary opens (including overlapping configurations), the
factorization algebra is determined by descent: a factorization
algebra on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ is a cosheaf for the
factorization topology, whose basis consists of products of disjoint
opens. Sectorwise finiteness~\ref{h2:sectorwise} guarantees that
$\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ is a genuine factorization coalgebra
on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$ (not merely a formal pro-object), so
the cosheaf condition applies. A map of factorization cosheaves
that is a quasi-isomorphism on every basis open is a global
quasi-isomorphism, giving~(i).

\emph{Part~(ii): Verdier intertwining.}
The Verdier intertwining on~$\operatorname{Ran}_1$ is
Theorem~A\textsubscript{2}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-verdier}).
For disjoint opens
$U_1 \sqcup \cdots \sqcup U_k$, Verdier duality distributes as
$\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}
\simeq \mathbb{D}_{U_1} \boxtimes \cdots \boxtimes \mathbb{D}_{U_k}$,
so the factorization bar intertwining decomposes into a tensor
product of the $\operatorname{Ran}_1$ intertwining on each factor.
The same cosheaf descent as part~(i) extends from disjoint to
arbitrary opens.

\emph{Part~(iii): module equivalence.}
On evaluation objects, the module bar functor is an equivalence by
DK-1 (Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}). The
evaluation-generated core
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$ is the
smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategory
containing all evaluation objects. Since the module bar functor
is exact and braided monoidal with reversal
(Theorem~\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}), it preserves shifts,
cones, direct summands, and ordered tensor products. Therefore, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}, any natural
isomorphism between the identity and
$\Omega_{\mathrm{mod}} \circ \barB_{\mathrm{mod}}$ that holds on
evaluation generators extends to the full generated core.

The braiding reversal $R \mapsto R^{-1}$ is
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-module-koszul}(iii), extended to the
generated core by functoriality.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of ``unconditional'']
\label{rem:dk23-unconditional-scope}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!unconditional!scope}
The following corollary is ``unconditional'' in the sense that it
does not require thick generation: the sectorwise convergence
argument works for all simple types without identifying the
generated core with $D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$.
It does, however, depend on the classical Koszulness of the RTT
Yangian (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), whose proof
uses Molev's PBW theorem \cite{molev-yangians} as external input.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Evaluation-generated-core DK comparison for all
simple types via sectorwise convergence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:dk23-all-types}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!derived!all types}
\index{sectorwise finiteness!DK for all types}
For $\fg$ any simple Lie algebra, the factorization bar-cobar
functor induces an equivalence on the evaluation-generated cores:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:dk23-all-types}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
 (Y_\hbar(\fg))
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}
 (Y_{-\hbar}(\fg))^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
extending the evaluation-locus DK equivalence
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}}\textup{)}
to the full generated core at all types, without any
thick-generation argument.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} to
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h1:koszulness} is
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}: the RTT Yangian is
quadratic, pro-nilpotent, and Koszul
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), so
Theorem~\ref{thm:e1-chiral-koszul-duality} gives the
$\Eone$-chiral bar-cobar quasi-isomorphism for every
simple~$\fg$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h2:sectorwise} is
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}: the $Q(\fg)$-grading
and loop filtration give the required sectorwise-finite bifiltration
for every simple~$\fg$.
Hypothesis~\ref{h3:convergence} follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}.
Conclusion~(iii) gives~\eqref{eq:dk23-all-types}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[H/M/S semantic levels for DK-2/3]
\label{rem:dk23-hms}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!H/M/S levels}
\emph{Step~A} (H-level):
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} asserts an
equivalence of stable $\infty$-categories
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
\simeq
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA^!)^{\mathrm{op}}$
on the evaluation-generated cores, with braiding reversal
$R \mapsto R^{-1}$. This is the theorem.

\emph{Step~B} (M-level):
The proof is a dg chain-level argument: sectorwise convergence
of the bar spectral sequence on each
$\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum, extended to the full factorization
cosheaf by descent. Concretely, the module bar functor is exact
and braided monoidal
(Theorem~\ref{thm:monoidal-module-koszul}), and the
quasi-isomorphism on evaluation generators extends to the
generated core by functoriality
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}).

\emph{Reduction B$\to$A} (M-level $\to$ H-level):
The dg descent implies the $\infty$-categorical equivalence: a
map of factorization cosheaves that is a quasi-isomorphism on
every basis open is a global quasi-isomorphism in the
$\infty$-categorical sense
(Lurie~\cite[Proposition~5.5.2.2]{HA}). Thus the M-level
sectorwise quasi-isomorphisms determine the H-level equivalence
of stable $\infty$-categories.

\emph{Step~C} (S-level):
The shadow is the equality of graded dimensions
$\dim \operatorname{Ext}^i_{\cA}(V_\lambda, V_\mu)
= \dim \operatorname{Ext}^i_{\cA^!}(V_\lambda^!, V_\mu^!)$
across evaluation modules, together with the Kazhdan--Lusztig
multiplicity formula transported to the Koszul dual side.

\emph{Reduction B$\to$C} (M-level $\to$ S-level):
Taking cohomology of the M-level module bar complex
$\bar{B}_{\mathrm{mod}}(M)$ extracts the S-level Ext groups.
The sectorwise spectral sequence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence}) converges
at each tridegree, so the M-level quasi-isomorphism on
evaluation generators yields isomorphisms of Ext groups.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[A proved route and a conditional route in type~\texorpdfstring{$A$}{A}; scope comparison]
\label{rem:two-dk-proofs}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!route comparison}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, there are now two complementary routes on
the generated-core DK comparison surface
\textup{(}traditionally packaged as DK-2/3\textup{)} for the
evaluation-generated core:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Thick generation}
 \textup{(}Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}\textup{)}:
 uses the
 Drinfeld polynomial classification to show that evaluation modules
 generate all finite-dimensional simples, then the composition-length
 argument of Lemma~\ref{lem:composition-thick-generation}. Theorem~\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}
 then records the \emph{conditional} extension criterion: once the
 ambient extension/comparison package is supplied, thick generation
 propagates the evaluation-level equivalence. This route is
 representation-theoretic and specific to type~$A$.
\item \emph{Sectorwise convergence}
 \textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}\textup{)}: uses
 the root lattice grading and loop filtration to bypass thick
 generation entirely. The proof is
 operadic/factorization-theoretic and works for all types.
\end{enumerate}
Route~(b) is the actual proved generated-core DK comparison on the
evaluation-generated core, and it is strictly more general
(all types $A$--$G$). Route~(a) is more explicit on type~$A$:
it identifies the module-side thick target as
$D^b(\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ via the Drinfeld
classification and would propagate any supplied ambient
extension/comparison package beyond generators. The two routes are
compatible on type~$A$: thick generation by evaluation modules
\textup{(}Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}\textup{)}
identifies the type-$A$ module-side generated core with the
evaluation-generated core already resolved by route~(b).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Interaction with the four-conjecture package]
\label{rem:h-level-vs-four-conjectures}
\index{MC3!four-conjecture package!interaction with H-level}
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types} resolve the
evaluation-generated-core DK comparison surface
\textup{(}traditionally packaged as DK-2/3\textup{)} at all types.
The four conjectures of
Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b)
(Baxter exact triangles
(Conjecture~\ref{thm:baxter-exact-triangles}),
shifted-prefundamental generation
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shifted-prefundamental-generation}),
pro-Weyl recovery (Conjecture~\ref{thm:pro-weyl-recovery}), and
DK on compacts
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}))
concern the extension \emph{beyond} this core to
infinite-dimensional modules via a completed or coderived
enhancement.

The two projects are complementary:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The sectorwise convergence theorem gives the strongest
 factorization equivalence on the natural domain
 (evaluation-generated core) at all types.
\item The four-conjecture package enlarges the domain to include
 prefundamental and asymptotic modules, requiring new input
 (Baxter TQ-lifts, pro-Weyl limits) beyond Koszul duality.
\item The formal moduli framework below provides the categorical
 home for both projects: the evaluation-generated core is the
 compact part of the formal moduli problem, and the four-conjecture
 package extends to the completed/ind-completed part.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{DK-4/5 as formal moduli Koszul duality}

The passage from DK-3 to DK-4/5, beyond the evaluation-generated
core toward the full triple bridge, gains conceptual clarity when
viewed through the lens of formal moduli problems for
$\Eone$-algebras. The abstract framework exists
unconditionally (Lurie~\cite{LurieDAGX}); once the post-core DK-3
extension/completion packet is supplied, the DK-4 task is the
identification of the tangent Lie algebra with the dg-shifted
Yangian, while the DK-5 task is the exponential/PBW passage from
the tangent Lie algebra to its formal group together with the
further comparison to the spectral quantum-group side.

\begin{definition}[Factorization formal moduli problem]
\label{def:factorization-formal-moduli}
\index{formal moduli problem!factorization|textbf}
For an $\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\cA$ on~$X$, the
\emph{factorization formal moduli problem} is the functor
\[
\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}\colon
\mathrm{CAlg}^{\mathrm{aug}}_{k}
\to \mathcal{S},
\qquad
R \;\mapsto\;
\operatorname{Map}_{\mathrm{FAlg}_{\Eone}(X)}
 \bigl(\cA \otimes R,\, \cA \otimes R\bigr)^{\simeq}
\]
from augmented commutative $k$-algebras to spaces, where the mapping
space is taken in the $\infty$-category of
$\Eone$-factorization algebras on~$\operatorname{Ran}(X)$.

By Lurie's formal moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX},
$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ is controlled by a dg Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} := T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$,
the \emph{tangent Lie algebra} of the moduli problem.
The chain-level model is classified by the bar complex:
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \simeq
\operatorname{Der}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA))$,
the derivations of the factorization bar coalgebra.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Canonical Yangian H-level dg target from factorization
formal moduli; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-canonical-hlevel-target}
For every $\Eone$-chiral algebra $\cA$ on~$X$, the factorization
formal moduli problem $\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ of
Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli} has a tangent dg Lie
algebra
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}:=T_*\mathfrak{F}_{\cA},
\]
and hence a canonically attached completed module category
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}).
\]
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
\[
\cA=\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N),
\]
this gives an unconditional H-level dg target for DK-4/5.

Equivalently, the live Yangian MC4 problem is not the existence of an
H-level dg target. It is the identification of this canonical formal
moduli target with an RTT-adapted dg model whose finite quotients
recover the theorematic RTT stages and whose degree-$2$ twisting
morphism matches the ordered bar seed on the fundamental line.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Existence of the tangent dg Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ is exactly
the content of Lurie's formal moduli theorem, as recalled in
Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli}. The completed module
category $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ is
therefore canonically attached to $\cA$. Specializing to the Yangian
$\Eone$-chiral algebra gives the claimed H-level target.

The remaining sentence is a reformulation of the Yangian MC4 residual H-level identification (structural framework proved; Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}):
the unresolved step is to identify the canonical target
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ with an RTT-adapted dg model, not to construct the
target itself.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Canonical associative dg model of the Yangian
formal-moduli target; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-canonical-envelope}
Let
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}:=T_*\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}
\]
be the tangent dg Lie algebra of the factorization formal moduli
problem. Let
\[
U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\]
denote the completion of its universal enveloping dg algebra with
respect to the adic filtration defining complete
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$-modules. Then
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ is a canonically attached
separated complete dg algebra, and there is a canonical equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}\bigl(
 U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\bigr).
\]
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra, this gives an unconditional
canonical associative dg model of the H-level target.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The universal enveloping construction extends functorially to dg Lie
algebras. Completing with respect to the same adic filtration that
defines the completed module category of the formal moduli problem
produces a separated complete dg algebra
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$.

By the universal property of the enveloping algebra, an action of the
dg Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ on a complete dg module is
equivalent to an action of
$U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$ on the same object, and the
intertwining morphisms are identical on both sides. Hence the
completed module categories are canonically equivalent. Specializing
to the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra gives the claimed canonical
associative dg model.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-4 as tangent Lie algebra identification;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!formal moduli identification}
\index{dg-shifted Yangian!as tangent Lie algebra}
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The tangent Lie algebra
 $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} = T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
 is quasi-isomorphic, as a filtered complete dg Lie algebra, to the
 dg-shifted Yangian $\Ydg_{\cA}$ of
 Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}}.
\item Under this identification, the RTT-adapted filtration
 \textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}}\textup{)}
 corresponds to the canonical filtration on
 $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ by order of the formal parameter: the $N$-th
 quotient $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}/F^{N+1}$ is the tangent Lie algebra
 of the $N$-th infinitesimal neighborhood of the identity in the
 factorization group.
\item The module category equivalence
 $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA}) \simeq
 \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$
 is the linearization of the formal moduli problem:
 completed modules over the tangent Lie algebra classify
 infinitesimal deformations of factorization modules.
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Relation to existing DK-4 reductions]
\label{rem:dk4-formal-moduli-vs-rtt}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!formal moduli vs RTT}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli} provides a \emph{canonical}
construction of the dg-shifted Yangian, replacing the specific
RTT-adapted filtration of
Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} with the universal
construction from formal moduli theory. The two approaches are
related:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The tangent Lie algebra $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ exists
 unconditionally by Lurie's theorem; the content of
 Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}(a) is that it has the
 specific algebraic structure of the dg-shifted Yangian.
\item The residue reductions of
 Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier} are
 \emph{derived} from the formal moduli identification:
 the auxiliary-kernel identity $L_a(u) = R_{0a}(u-a)$ is
 the tangent-space computation of the moduli problem
 restricted to the fundamental evaluation line.
\item The RTT-adapted filtration of
 Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} is the
 \emph{coordinate expression} of the canonical formal-moduli
 filtration in the basis provided by the RTT generators.
\end{enumerate}
This reformulation clarifies the logical structure: the RTT
identities are not independent axioms but consequences of the
universal $\infty$-categorical framework applied to the specific
$\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-5 via \texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical PBW;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk5-infty-pbw}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!PBW argument}
\index{PBW theorem!infinity-categorical@$\infty$-categorical}
Assume Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}(a,b)}, and
assume that the DK-3 comparison has been extended from the
evaluation-generated core to the completed factorization domain
appearing in Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}}.
Then the remaining DK-5 step of the full triple bridge
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}}\textup{)}
reduces to a single input: the $\infty$-categorical
Poincar\'e--Birkhoff--Witt theorem for the factorization Lie
algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The formal group
 $G_{\cA} := \exp(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
 is a group object in $\Eone$-factorization coalgebras on
 $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$. Its representation category
 $\operatorname{Rep}(G_{\cA})$ is a braided monoidal stable
 $\infty$-category.
\item The $\infty$-categorical PBW theorem gives an equivalence
 \[
 \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
 \;\simeq\;
 \operatorname{Rep}(G_{\cA})
 \]
 between completed modules over the Lie algebra and
 representations of the formal group.
\item If $G_{\cA} \simeq \QGspec(R_{\cA})$
 \textup{(}the spectral quantum group of
 Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}\textup{)}, then the remaining bridge
 equivalence in~\eqref{eq:triple-equivalence} follows from the chain
 \begin{multline*}
 \Factord(X;\cA)
 \;\xleftarrow[\textup{DK-3}]{\sim}\;
 \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}(\cA^{!,c})^{\mathrm{op}}
 \\
 \;\xrightarrow[\textup{PBW}]{\sim}\;
 \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
 \;\xrightarrow[\exp]{\sim}\;
 \operatorname{Rep}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}.
 \end{multline*}
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[The DK ladder as successive approximation to
\texorpdfstring{$\infty$}{infinity}-categorical Koszul duality]
\label{rem:unified-dk-hierarchy}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!unified hierarchy}
The five DK levels are successive approximations to $\infty$-categorical Koszul duality for $\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Level} & \textbf{Content} & \textbf{Status} \\
\hline
DK-0 & Chain-level Koszul duality on $\operatorname{Ran}_1$
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-1 & Extension to $\operatorname{Ran}_n$ on evaluation objects
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-2/3 & Generated-core DK comparison (sectorwise convergence)
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
DK-4 & Tangent Lie algebra $=$ dg-shifted Yangian (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli})
 & Partial (ML proved, Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}; algebraic identification open, Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}) \\
DK-5 & $\infty$-PBW after post-core DK-3 extension (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw})
 & Open \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
DK-0/1: Drinfeld--Kohno $+$ Kazhdan--Lusztig. DK-2/3: Boardman convergence of the loop spectral sequence (Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}). DK-4: structural framework proved (MC4 closed, Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}); algebraic identification open (Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}). DK-5: once the post-core extension/completion packet beyond DK-2/3 is supplied, the remaining bridge step is the exponential/PBW passage $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \rightsquigarrow G_{\cA}$ together with the further identification of $G_{\cA}$ with Latyntsev's spectral quantum group~\cite{Latyntsev23}. \ifannalsedition\else Target: Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.\fi

\emph{CG constraint on DK-5.}
The prefundamental Clebsch--Gordan
(Proposition~\ref{prop:prefundamental-clebsch-gordan})
constrains DK-5 as follows: since
$V_n \otimes L^- \cong \bigoplus L^-(\text{shifted})$
shows that $L^-$ is evaluation-stable, the quantum group
representation $\operatorname{Rep}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))$ must
contain a corresponding family of objects that is closed under
tensoring with the fundamental. At the level of $q$-characters
(Frenkel--Reshetikhin), this forces the DK-5 functor to
intertwine the prefundamental TQ system
$[V_1] \cdot [L^-] = [L^-(+1)] + [L^-(-1)]$
with the QQ-system of the quantum group.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[DK-5 for $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ via FRT
reconstruction; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dk5-sl2-frt}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!sl2@$\mathfrak{sl}_2$ resolution|textbf}
\index{FRT construction!DK-5 resolution}
\index{quantum group!FRT reconstruction from bar complex}
For $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$ at generic~$q$, the
full Hopf algebra $U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ is uniquely
determined by the Yang $R$-matrix
$R(u) = uI + \hbar P$ arising from the bar complex
$\barB^{\mathrm{ord}}(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k})$
via the FRT construction.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The $R$-matrix satisfies the Yang--Baxter equation and
 strong unitarity $R_{12}(u)\,R_{21}(-u) = (u^2 - \hbar^2)I$.
\item The FRT relations $R\,T_1\,T_2 = T_2\,T_1\,R$
 produce the Drinfeld--Jimbo coproduct
 $\Delta(E) = E \otimes K + I \otimes E$,
 $\Delta(F) = F \otimes I + K^{-1} \otimes F$,
 $\Delta(K) = K \otimes K$.
\item Rigidity: $H^2(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2), \mathbb{k}) = 0$
 ensures the reconstruction is unique
 \textup{(}no deformation ambiguity\textup{)}.
\item At roots of unity $q = e^{2\pi i/(k+2)}$, the Verlinde
 truncation at spin $j = (k{+}1)/2$ is a direct consequence:
 the quantum dimension $[k{+}2]_q = 0$ forces vanishing
 of the trace on spin-$(k{+}1)/2$ representations.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Yang $R$-matrix is constructed from the bar complex
via the collision residue
(Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}). The FRT
procedure applied to $R(u) = uI + \hbar P$ yields
the RTT algebra; the standard Faddeev--Reshetikhin--Takhtajan
argument identifies this with $U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ at
$q = e^{i\hbar}$. Rigidity follows from the vanishing of the
second Hochschild--Kostant--Rosenberg cohomology of
$U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ at generic~$q$, which in turn follows
from the semisimplicity of the representation category.
The Verlinde truncation is immediate from the quantum
dimension formula $[n]_q = \sin(n\pi/(k{+}2))/\sin(\pi/(k{+}2))$.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Restricted DK-5: evaluation-generated triple bridge;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:restricted-dk5}%
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!restricted|textbf}%
\index{thick generation!restricted DK-5}%
\index{triple equivalence!evaluation-generated core}%
Let $\fg$ be a simple Lie algebra, and let
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\fg))
\subset \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}(\mathcal{Y}(\fg)),
\qquad
\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\fg))
\subset \operatorname{Rep}(U_q(\fg))
\]
be the full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategories
generated by evaluation modules
$\{V_{\omega_i}(a) : i \in \mathrm{vert}(\mathrm{Dyn}(\fg)),\;
a \in \mathbb{C}\}$. Let
${\Ydg_{\cA}}^{\mathrm{gen}}$ be the restriction of the dg-shifted
Yangian $\Ydg_{\cA}$ to the evaluation-generated sector. Then
there are equivalences of braided monoidal stable
$\infty$-categories
\begin{equation}\label{eq:restricted-dk5-triple}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathcal{Y}(\fg))
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\fg))^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
compatible with the DK-1 evaluation-locus equivalence
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}}\textup{)}
and the KZ monodromy package.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Inputs to the restricted DK-5]
\label{rem:restricted-dk5-inputs}
Two of the three ingredients are proved unconditionally for all
simple types.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Thick generation.}
 For every simple~$\fg$, the evaluation modules
 $\{V_{\omega_i}(a)\}$ thickly generate
 $D^b(\mathrm{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\fg)))$
 \textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:dk2-thick-generation-all-types}}\textup{)}.
 The subcategory
 $\operatorname{Rep}_{\mathrm{fd}}^{\mathrm{gen}}(U_q(\fg))$
 therefore contains every finite-dimensional irreducible.
\item \emph{Categorical Clebsch--Gordan.}
 The all-types CG closure
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}},
 via the multiplicity-free $\ell$-weight property of
 Chari--Moura~\cite{ChariMoura06}\textup{)} ensures that
 the evaluation-generated core is closed under the tensor
 operations needed for the factorization comparison.
\item \emph{DK-2/3 on the generated core.}
 The outer equivalence on the evaluation-generated core is
 proved
 \textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}}\textup{)}.
 What remains is the middle term: the dg-shifted Yangian
 identification~\textup{(}DK-4 restricted to the generated
 sector\textup{)} and the PBW/exponential
 passage~\textup{(}DK-5 on the generated core\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
The full DK-5 \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw}}\textup{)}
requires extending beyond the evaluation-generated core to the full
module category~$\mathcal{O}$. The restricted conjecture avoids
this extension entirely: the thick subcategory generated by
evaluation modules is the natural domain on which all proved inputs
\textup{(}MC3, thick generation, DK-2/3\textup{)} converge.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The RTT relation as Koszul duality datum]
\label{rem:rtt-is-the-duality-datum}
\index{Yangian!RTT as Koszul datum}
\index{Koszul duality!engine of DK ladder}
The common algebraic datum behind the proved DK ladder
\textup{(}DK-0 through DK-3 on the evaluation-generated core,
unconditional at all simple types\textup{)} is the RTT presentation.
But the proof is not a one-idea argument: quadratic duality,
PBW/Koszulness, and sectorwise spectral descent enter as
logically distinct inputs organized around that datum.
\smallskip
\begin{center}
\emph{The RTT relation
$R_{12}(u\!-\!v)\,T_1(u)\,T_2(v)
= T_2(v)\,T_1(u)\,R_{12}(u\!-\!v)$
is simultaneously the defining relation of the algebra
and the input to Koszul duality.}
\end{center}

\smallskip\noindent
Three consequences organize the proved surface:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Quadratic $\Rightarrow$ $R$-matrix inversion.}
 The RTT relation is quadratic in~$T$; the orthogonal complement
 $R^\perp$ of the $R(u)$-relations is the $R^{-1}(u)$-relations,
 so $Y(\fg)^! = Y_{-\hbar}(\fg)$
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}).

\item \emph{PBW $\Rightarrow$ Koszulness.}
 Molev's PBW basis gives a flat deformation to
 $\operatorname{Sym}(V)$; $\operatorname{Sym}$ is classically
 Koszul; flatness transfers Koszulness to~$Y(\fg)$, giving
 bar-cobar recovery for free
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul},
 Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}).

\item \emph{Root grading $\Rightarrow$ sectorwise convergence.}
 The root lattice $Q(\fg)$ decomposes the bar complex into sectors
 with $\dim V_r = (\dim V_0)^2$ uniformly; a non-increasing
 sequence of non-negative integers stabilizes; the factorization
 bar complex is therefore a genuine coalgebra on
 $\operatorname{Ran}(X)$, and K\"unneth $+$ cosheaf descent extend
 the diagonal quasi-isomorphism to all strata
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:sectorwise-spectral-convergence},
 Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}).
\end{enumerate}
These are logically independent inputs. Items~\textup{(a)} and
\textup{(b)} control the algebraic Koszul-dual surface, while
\textup{(c)} is the separate sectorwise-convergence/descent step
that upgrades the diagonal quasi-isomorphism to DK-2/3 for every
simple~$\fg$ without any thick-generation argument.

The deeper unity is organizational rather than eliminative:
\emph{the RTT presentation supplies the common algebraic source},
while PBW shows that the quadratic extraction is faithful and the
root grading makes the factorization descent converge. In that
sense, all three are built around
\emph{the RTT presentation expressing the Yangian as a quadratic
algebra whose defining relations encode the $R$-matrix}.
The bar construction extracts the $R$-matrix and inverts it;
PBW guarantees this extraction is lossless; the root grading
guarantees it converges sector by sector. Geometrically:
bar-cobar duality is Verdier duality on ordered configuration
spaces, and Verdier duality reverses the orientation of ordered
collisions, which inverts the $R$-matrix. The RTT presentation
is, in this precise sense, the Yangian \emph{presenting itself as
a Koszul duality problem}.

For the conjectural levels, the same RTT/PBW/root-grading package
continues to organize the \emph{bar-side} completion story, but it
does not by itself close DK-4 or DK-5.
It gives surjective
transition maps $\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N+1}^*) \twoheadrightarrow
\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N}^*)$ on the associated graded of bar
cohomology, hence Mittag-Leffler for the RTT tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}) and a well-behaved
completed bar-cobar equivalence
(Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}).
What remains at DK-4 is the separate structure identification:
$\varprojlim_N \fg_N \cong \Ydg_\cA$
(Maurer--Cartan element, translation, coproduct).
Downstream, DK-5 still sits beyond the post-core DK-3
extension/completion packet and then requires the
$\infty$-categorical PBW exponential
$\operatorname{Mod}(\fg_\cA) \simeq
\operatorname{Rep}(\exp(\fg_\cA))$.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Coderived factorization duality off the Koszul locus}

On the Koszul locus (generic levels, evaluation-generated core),
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd} provides an equivalence
in the ordinary derived sense. Off the Koszul locus (at admissible
affine levels, minimal-model central charges, or for infinite-dimensional
modules beyond the generated core), the bar-cobar object persists as a
\emph{curved} factorization coalgebra, and the correct framework is the
coderived/contraderived category of
Positselski~\cite{Positselski11}.

\begin{theorem}[Factorization Positselski equivalence on the bar-coalgebra surface; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:factorization-positselski}
\index{Positselski!factorization equivalence|textbf}
\index{coderived category!factorization|textbf}
\index{factorization co-contra comparison!off the Koszul locus}
Let~$\cA$ be an $\Eone$-chiral algebra on~$X$ satisfying
hypotheses~\ref{h2:sectorwise} and~\ref{h3:convergence} of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}}
\textup{(}sectorwise finiteness and spectral convergence\textup{)},
but not necessarily~\ref{h1:koszulness}
\textup{(}$\Eone$-Koszulness\textup{)}.
Let $C = \barB^{\mathrm{fact}}(\cA)$ denote the curved factorization
bar coalgebra. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The factorization coderived category
 $D^{\mathrm{co}}(C\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{conil}})$
 is a well-defined stable $\infty$-category: the sectorwise
 finiteness of~$C$ ensures that each $Q(\fg)$-sector is a
 genuine conilpotent coalgebra \textup{(}not a formal
 pro-object\textup{)}, so the coacyclicity localizing
 subcategory is well-defined.
 \item There is a triangulated equivalence
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:factorization-positselski}
 D^{\mathrm{co}}\bigl(
 C\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{conil}}
 \bigr)
 \;\simeq\;
 D^{\mathrm{ctr}}\bigl(
 C\text{-}\mathrm{ContraFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{comp}}
 \bigr),
 \end{equation}
 where the left side is the coderived category of conilpotent
 $\Eone$-factorization comodules over~$C$, and the right side is
 the contraderived category of complete \textup{(}pro-nilpotent\textup{)}
 $\Eone$-factorization contramodules over the same curved
 factorization coalgebra~$C$.
\item On the Koszul locus \textup{(}when~\ref{h1:koszulness}
 also holds\textup{)}, the coderived and ordinary derived categories
 coincide on compact objects. Together with the separate
 factorization Verdier/bar-dual identification of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(ii)}, the
 bar-coalgebra comparison~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski}
 is compatible with the generated-core equivalence of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Part~(i).}
Sectorwise finiteness (hypothesis~\ref{h2:sectorwise}) gives
$C = \bigoplus_{\gamma} C_\gamma$ with each $C_\gamma$
finite-dimensional over each $\operatorname{Ran}$-stratum.
The factorization structure on~$C$ preserves the
$Q(\fg)$-grading (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-bar-loop-weight}(a)),
so the coaugmentation filtration
$F_0 C \subset F_1 C \subset \cdots$ has each
$F_n C_\gamma$ finite-dimensional. The conilpotency condition
$C = \bigcup_n F_n C$ then holds sector-by-sector, and the
coacyclicity localizing subcategory (thick closure of totalizations
of exact triples, closed under coproducts) is well-defined
by the same argument as
Definition~\ref{def:chiral-coderived}, applied sectorwise.

\emph{Part~(ii).}
The chain-level comodule-contramodule correspondence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-co-contra-correspondence}) provides the
equivalence on
$\operatorname{Ran}_1(X) \cong X$. The factorization structure
propagates this to $\operatorname{Ran}_n$ by the same
K\"unneth--descent argument as
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(i):
on disjoint opens the equivalence decomposes as a tensor product
of chain-level equivalences, and the factorization cosheaf
condition extends to overlapping configurations. Sectorwise
finiteness ensures the tensor products are well-defined
(no infinite-dimensionality obstructions).

\emph{Part~(iii).}
On the Koszul locus, the curvature vanishes:
$h = m_0^{(g)} = 0$ at genus~$0$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion}(a)). When $h = 0$,
coacyclic = acyclic (Positselski~\cite[Thm~3.7]{Positselski11}),
so $D^{\mathrm{co}} = D^b$ on compact objects. The restriction
of~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski} to compact objects therefore
lives in the ordinary derived setting. The further identification of
that compact comparison with
Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii) uses the separate
Koszul-locus factorization Verdier/bar-dual statement
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(ii)}\textup{)},
which is not part of the off-Koszul Positselski proof itself.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The coderived category as the natural ambient]
\label{rem:coderived-natural-ambient}
\index{coderived category!as natural ambient for DK}
The equivalence~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski} is the
\emph{correct categorical context} for the remaining off-Koszul MC3
extension packets:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item On the Koszul locus (generic level), DK-0 through DK-3
 live in the ordinary derived category, and the coderived
 category adds nothing new. This is the domain of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}.
\item Off the Koszul locus (admissible levels, minimal-model central
 charges), the bar-cobar object~$\Omega(C)$ is curved:
 $d^2 = h \neq 0$. Ordinary cohomological derived methods no
 longer capture the curved bar-cobar object, but the coderived
 category retains the full categorical information.
 The four conjectures of
 Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b)
 naturally live here: Baxter exact triangles, shifted-prefundamental
 generation, pro-Weyl recovery, and DK on compacts are all
 most naturally formulated relative to the
 coderived/contraderived bar-coalgebra setting
 of~\eqref{eq:factorization-positselski}. What
 \eqref{eq:factorization-positselski} does \emph{not} by itself
 supply is the additional module-theoretic, compact-generation,
 or formal-neighborhood input appearing in those conjectures.
\item The passage from the evaluation-generated core (compact objects
 in $D^b$) to a presentable cocompletion is controlled by the
 ind-completion of that generated core: see
 Theorem~\ref{thm:ind-completed-extension} below. Identifying this
 cocompletion with the full category~$\mathcal{O}$ requires
 additional compact-generation/comparison input and is not part of
 that theorem.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Ind-completed factorization extension}

The passage from the evaluation-generated core to its formal
presentable cocompletion is a standard categorical construction once
the compact part is established. This should not be confused with a
theorematic identification of that cocompletion with the full Yangian
category~$\mathcal{O}$.

\begin{theorem}[Ind-completion of the generated-core DK equivalence; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:ind-completed-extension}
\index{ind-completion!factorization DK|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!ind-completed extension}
Under the hypotheses of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}},
the equivalence on evaluation-generated cores extends uniquely
to an exact colimit-preserving equivalence of ind-completed
categories:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ind-completed-dk}
\operatorname{Ind}\bigl(
 \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)
\bigr)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Ind}\bigl(
 \operatorname{CoFact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA^{!,c})
 ^{\mathrm{op}}
\bigr).
\end{equation}
In particular, both sides are presentable stable
$\infty$-categories.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The evaluation-generated core
$\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}}(\cA)$ is a small,
idempotent-complete, stable $\infty$-category
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}). The
equivalence of Theorem~\ref{thm:h-level-factorization-kd}(iii) is
an exact functor between small stable $\infty$-categories. By
the universal property of ind-completion
(Lurie~\cite[Prop.~5.3.5.10]{HTT}), any exact equivalence between
small stable $\infty$-categories extends uniquely to a
colimit-preserving equivalence between their ind-completions.
This gives~\eqref{eq:ind-completed-dk}.

Presentability follows from $\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})$
being presentable whenever $\mathcal{C}$ is small and
idempotent-complete (Lurie~\cite[Prop.~5.5.7.8]{HTT}).
Stability is preserved by ind-completion.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Ind-completion vs.\ pro-Weyl completion]
\label{rem:ind-vs-proweyl}
\index{pro-Weyl completion!vs.\ ind-completion}
The ind-completed category
$\operatorname{Ind}(\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{gen}})$
is the \emph{free cocompletion} of the generated core: it
formally adds all filtered colimits. This is a strictly larger
category than the generated core but a strictly smaller one than
the full coderived category
$D^{\mathrm{co}}(\barB^{\mathrm{fact}}\text{-}\mathrm{CoFact})$
of Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-positselski}.

The four conjectures of
Remark~\ref{rem:corrected-mc3-frontier}(b) concern modules
that lie in the ind-completion but not in the generated core:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Standard modules} $M(\Psi)$: by
 Conjecture~\ref{thm:pro-weyl-recovery}, these are
 pro-Weyl limits $R\varprojlim_m W_m$, where each~$W_m$ is
 compact (evaluation-generated). The pro-object
 $\{W_m\}$ defines an object of $\operatorname{Pro}(\mathcal{C})
 \hookrightarrow \operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})$
 via the canonical functor
 $\operatorname{Pro}(\mathcal{C}) \to
 \operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C})^{\mathrm{op}}$.
\item \emph{Prefundamental modules} $L^-_{i,a}$: by
 Theorem~\ref{thm:shifted-prefundamental-generation}, these
 are compact generators of the completed shifted category.
 In the ind-completed factorization category, $L^-_{i,a}$
 should be representable as a filtered colimit of evaluation
 objects (via the Baxter exact triangles of
 Conjecture~\ref{thm:baxter-exact-triangles}).
\end{enumerate}
The equivalence~\eqref{eq:ind-completed-dk} provides the
categorical framework in which both types of extensions live.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The four conjectures in the formal moduli framework}

The formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
(Definition~\ref{def:factorization-formal-moduli}) provides a
unified $\infty$-categorical formulation of the four MC3
conjectures. Each conjecture becomes a statement about the
tangent Lie algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ or the formal
group~$G_{\cA} = \exp(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$.

\begin{conjecture}[Formal moduli reformulation of MC3;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation}
\index{MC3!formal moduli reformulation}
\index{formal moduli problem!MC3}
The four MC3 components (with the all-types categorical CG and
evaluation-generated-core surfaces now separated from the remaining
completion packets) admit conjectural reformulations in terms
of the factorization formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$
and the tangent Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} = T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\Roman*)}]
\item \emph{Baxter
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{thm:baxter-exact-triangles}}\textup{)}
 as infinitesimal deformation exact triangles.}
 The Baxter TQ relations lift to distinguished triangles in
 the category $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
 of completed modules over the tangent Lie algebra. The
 companion module $M_{k,x}^{(i)}$ represents the tangent
 vector to the evaluation deformation at the point
 $(k, x) \in \mathbb{C}^2$, and the TQ triangle is the
