 fiber sequence of the tangent map
 $T_{(k,x)}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA} \to
 T_{(k',x')}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$.

\item \emph{Shifted-prefundamental generation
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:shifted-prefundamental-generation}}\textup{)}
 as compact generation of the tangent category.}
 The compact objects of
 $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})$
 are the thick closure of tangent representations at
 evaluation and prefundamental points. In the formal moduli
 picture, these are the tangent spaces to the evaluation
 locus (compact, by the proved DK-1) and the
 prefundamental locus (conjecturally compact).

\item \emph{Pro-Weyl recovery
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{thm:pro-weyl-recovery}}\textup{)}
 as completeness of the formal moduli problem.}
 For a rational $\ell$-weight~$\Psi$, the standard module
 $M(\Psi)$ is the derived global sections of the formal
 neighborhood of~$\Psi$ in the moduli of $\ell$-weights:
 \[
 M(\Psi)
 \;\simeq\;
 R\Gamma\bigl(\widehat{\mathrm{Spec}\,
 \mathcal{O}}_\Psi,\;
 \mathcal{V}_{\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}}\bigr)
 \;\simeq\;
 R\varprojlim_m\, W_m,
 \]
 where the Weyl modules~$W_m$ are the values of the moduli
 functor on the $m$-th infinitesimal neighborhood.

\item \emph{DK on compacts
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}}\textup{)}
 as formal GAGA.}
 The bar-cobar equivalence extends from the generic
 fiber (evaluation locus) to the formal neighborhood
 (completed category) by a formal GAGA principle for
 the factorization formal moduli problem:
 coherent sheaves on the formal completion agree with
 algebraic coherent sheaves on the Koszul locus.
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Tangent Lie algebra controls the extension package]
\label{rem:tangent-controls-extension}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!role in MC3 extension}
The formal moduli reformulation
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation})
reveals the organizing role of the tangent Lie
algebra~$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$: the remaining extension
conjectures beyond the proved MC3 evaluation-generated core can be organized over a common structural background,
namely that $\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}$ is \emph{algebraizable}:
that the formal moduli problem~$\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}$ is the
formal completion of a global (algebraic) moduli problem.

In the DK-4 framework
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}), algebraizability is the
content of the RTT-adapted filtration: the formal
group~$G_{\cA}$ admits a filtration whose finite quotients are
the finite RTT stages, and the transition maps are the RTT
truncations. If this filtration is Mittag-Leffler on cohomology
(the concrete form of algebraizability), the strong
completion-tower theorem
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}\textup{)}
supplies the bar-side completed Koszul framework relevant to the
remaining MC3 packets. What it does \emph{not} by itself prove is
the module-theoretic content of Baxter exact triangles,
shifted-prefundamental generation, pro-Weyl recovery, or DK on
compacts; those still require additional identifications on the
appropriate completed module/formal-neighborhood surfaces.

This suggests a staged alternative route: first establish the
Mittag--Leffler/completion framework on the RTT tower, then
separately identify how each remaining MC3 packet is encoded in
that common formal-moduli setting.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Factorization DK-4: tangent Lie algebra via
bar derivations}

Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli} identifies DK-4 with the
tangent Lie algebra computation
$\mathfrak{g}_{\cA} \simeq \Ydg_{\cA}$.
The following proposition provides the first constructive step:
the tangent Lie algebra at finite RTT stage is computable,
and the compatibility of these finite computations is the
content of DK-4.

\begin{proposition}[Finite-stage tangent Lie algebras;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:finite-stage-tangent}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!finite RTT stage}
\index{dg-shifted Yangian!finite-stage construction}
For the Yangian $\Eone$-chiral algebra
$\cA = \mathcal{Y}(\fg)$ and the $N$-th RTT truncation
$\cA_{\leq N}$, the tangent Lie algebra
$\mathfrak{g}_N := T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA_{\leq N}}$
satisfies:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\mathfrak{g}_N$ is a finite-dimensional dg Lie algebra
 with $N \cdot (\dim V_0)^2$ generators in degree~$0$
 \textup{(}one copy of $\operatorname{End}(V_0)$ per RTT
 level; for the reduced Yangian, $N \cdot \dim \fg$
 generators\textup{)}.
\item The differential on~$\mathfrak{g}_N$ is the derivation
 of $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$ induced by the bar differential:
 \[
 \mathfrak{g}_N
 \;\cong\;
 \operatorname{Der}^{\mathrm{cont}}\bigl(
 \barB(\cA_{\leq N}),\, \barB(\cA_{\leq N})
 \bigr)[1].
 \]
\item The truncation maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$
 induce surjective dg Lie algebra maps
 $\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \mathfrak{g}_N$,
 compatible with the bar construction.
\item At $N = 1$, $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$
 \textup{(}the RTT generators $T_{ij}^{(0)}$ at level~$0$ span
 $\operatorname{End}(V_0)$ with the commutator bracket\textup{)},
 concentrated in degree~$0$. For the reduced Yangian
 $Y(\fg)$ \textup{(}quantum determinant quotient\textup{)},
 $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \fg$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Part~(a):
$\cA_{\leq N}$ is the quotient of~$\cA$ by generators of
level $> N$. Each level contributes $(\dim V_0)^2$
generators (the RTT modes $T_{ij}^{(r)}$ for
$0 \leq r \leq N-1$), so $\mathfrak{g}_N$ has
$N \cdot (\dim V_0)^2$ generators in degree~$0$.
Since $\cA_{\leq N}$ is quadratic and Koszul
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), the tangent Lie
algebra $\mathfrak{g}_N \cong
\operatorname{Ext}^*_{\cA_{\leq N}}(\bC, \bC)[1]$ is
finite-dimensional (each degree of the Koszul dual
$\cA_{\leq N}^!$ is finite-dimensional by local finiteness).

Part~(b):
By Lurie's formal moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}, the tangent
Lie algebra is computed as the shifted derivations of the bar
coalgebra. For the finite-dimensional quotient~$\cA_{\leq N}$,
the bar coalgebra $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$ is finite-dimensional
(bounded bar degree by the quadratic relations), so
the derivation complex is finite-dimensional.

Part~(c):
The truncation map $\cA_{\leq N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cA_{\leq N}$
induces a surjection
$\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow \barB(\cA_{\leq N})$
of bar coalgebras (bar is covariant on algebra maps).

For the tangent Lie algebras, the map
$\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \to \mathfrak{g}_N$ is surjective by the
following Koszul dual argument: since $\cA_{\leq N}$ is Koszul,
the tangent Lie algebra in degree~$p$ is
$(\mathfrak{g}_N)_p \cong (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_{p+1}$.

The Koszul dual $\cA_{\leq N}^!$ has generators
$V_{\leq N}^*$ and relations $R_{\leq N}^\perp$.
Any element $f \in (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n
\subset (V_{\leq N}^*)^{\otimes n} \cap (R_{\leq N}^\perp)_n$
extends by zero on the $V_N^*$-components to an element
$\tilde{f} \in (\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n$
(since $\tilde{f}$ automatically annihilates all
relations involving level-$N$ generators).
Hence $(\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n \twoheadrightarrow (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n$
is surjective in every degree.

The identification
$(\mathfrak{g}_N)_p \cong (\cA_{\leq N}^!)_{p+1}$ is natural
in~$N$: it arises from Lurie's formal moduli theorem (Part~(b))
applied to each truncation, and the truncation-compatible maps of
bar coalgebras induce compatible maps on derivation complexes.
Thus the surjectivity of $(\cA_{\leq N+1}^!)_n \twoheadrightarrow
(\cA_{\leq N}^!)_n$ directly yields
$\mathfrak{g}_{N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \mathfrak{g}_N$ in every
internal degree.

Part~(d):
At $N = 1$, $\cA_{\leq 1} \cong U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0))$ (the
$T_{ij}^{(0)}$ for $1 \leq i,j \leq \dim V_0$ generate
$\operatorname{End}(V_0) = \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$ under the
commutator, and the RTT relation at level~$0$ reproduces the
$\mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$ bracket). The bar complex
$\barB(U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0)))$ is the Chevalley--Eilenberg complex,
and $\operatorname{Der}(\barB(U(\mathfrak{gl}(V_0))))[1]
\cong \mathfrak{gl}(V_0)$, concentrated in degree~$0$.
The quantum determinant condition at level~$0$ reduces the
identity component, giving $\mathfrak{g}_1 \cong \fg$ for
the reduced Yangian.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Mittag-Leffler for the RTT bar cohomology tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}
\index{Mittag-Leffler condition!RTT tower|textbf}
\index{bar complex!RTT tower!Mittag-Leffler}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!Mittag-Leffler}
For any simple Lie algebra~$\fg$, the transition maps on bar
cohomology in the RTT tower are surjective:
\[
H^n\bigl(\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1})\bigr)
\;\twoheadrightarrow\;
H^n\bigl(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})\bigr)
\qquad \text{for all } N \geq 1, \;\text{all } n \geq 0.
\]
In particular, the Mittag-Leffler condition holds and
$\varprojlim^1_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) = 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1: PBW filtration on truncated bar complexes.}
Each truncation $\cA_{\leq N} = Y(\fg)_{\leq N}$ inherits the
PBW filtration of Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}:
$F_p \cA_{\leq N}$ is spanned by ordered monomials of total
level $\leq p$ in the RTT generators $\{T_{ij}^{(r)}\}_{r < N}$.
The associated graded is the polynomial algebra:
\[
\operatorname{gr}_F \cA_{\leq N}
\;\cong\;
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N}),
\qquad
V_{\leq N} = \bigoplus_{r=0}^{N-1}
\operatorname{End}(\bC^{N_0})_r,
\]
where $N_0 = \dim V_0$. The truncation maps
$\cA_{\leq N+1} \twoheadrightarrow \cA_{\leq N}$ preserve the
PBW filtration and induce the projection
$\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$ on associated graded.

\emph{Step~2: PBW spectral sequence for bar cohomology.}
The PBW filtration induces a bounded-below, exhaustive filtration
on $\barB(\cA_{\leq N})$. By
Theorem~\ref{thm:pbw-koszulness-criterion} (``bar construction
commutes with taking associated graded for flat filtrations''),
the associated spectral sequence has $E_1$ page
\[
E_1^{p,q}(\cA_{\leq N})
= H^{p+q}\bigl(\barB(\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N}))\bigr).
\]
By Koszulness of $\cA_{\leq N}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul} applies to each truncation:
$\cA_{\leq N}$ is a quadratic algebra in finitely many generators
$\{T_{ij}^{(r)}\}_{r < N}$ with the restricted RTT relations, inherits
the PBW basis of Molev, and satisfies local finiteness a~fortiori),
the spectral sequence \emph{degenerates at $E_1$}:
$E_1 = E_\infty$. Indeed, Koszulness forces bar cohomology
onto the diagonal $p + q = n$, $p = n$ (homological = internal
degree), so all higher differentials $d_r$ for $r \geq 2$ have
zero source or target for bidegree reasons.

\emph{Step~3: Surjectivity on $E_1$.}
For the commutative algebra $\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$,
the Koszul dual is $\bigwedge(V_{\leq N}^*)$, and bar cohomology
in degree~$n$ is $\bigwedge^n(V_{\leq N}^*)$. The truncation
$\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N+1}) \twoheadrightarrow
\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\leq N})$ induces on bar cohomology the
projection
\[
\textstyle
\bigwedge\nolimits^n(V_{\leq N+1}^*)
\;\twoheadrightarrow\;
\bigwedge\nolimits^n(V_{\leq N}^*),
\]
which kills exactly the wedge products involving the factor
$\operatorname{End}(\bC^{N_0})_N^*$. This map is surjective
for all $N$ and $n$.

\emph{Step~4: Filtered surjectivity implies surjectivity.}
The truncation maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$ are
compatible with the PBW filtrations, hence induce a map of
spectral sequences. On the $E_1 = E_\infty$ page, this map
is the surjection of Step~3. Since the PBW filtration on
$H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$ is exhaustive and bounded below
(each bar degree and level contributes finitely), a standard
filtered-surjectivity argument gives: a filtered map
$f\colon M' \to M$ of filtered objects inducing a surjection
$\operatorname{gr}_p f$ on each graded piece is itself
surjective. (Proof: by induction on $p$, the image of
$f$ contains $F_p M$ for each~$p$; exhaustivity gives
$\operatorname{im}(f) = M$.)

Therefore $H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N+1}))
\twoheadrightarrow H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$
is surjective for all $N$ and~$n$. Surjective transition maps
trivially satisfy Mittag-Leffler, giving
$\varprojlim^1 = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Completed bar-cobar equivalence for Yangians;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}
\index{bar-cobar duality!completed Yangian|textbf}
\index{Yangian!completed bar-cobar}
For any simple~$\fg$, the completed reduced bar construction
\[
\widehat{\barB}\bigl(Y(\fg)\bigr)
\;:=\;
\varprojlim_N\, \barB\bigl(Y(\fg)_{\leq N}\bigr)
\]
exists as a separated complete conilpotent $\Eone$-chiral coalgebra,
and the completed cobar-bar counit is a quasi-isomorphism:
\[
\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}\bigl(
 \widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg))
\bigr)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\sim\;}\;
Y(\fg).
\]
This verifies
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}}
for the Yangian RTT tower.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The strong completion-tower axioms of
Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong} are verified:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Each truncation $\cA_{\leq N}$ is finite type and lies in
 the proved bar-cobar regime
 (Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-bar-cobar}).
\item The transition maps $\cA_{\leq N+1} \to \cA_{\leq N}$ are
 compatible with the finite-stage bar constructions
 (PBW filtration compatibility,
 Proposition~\ref{prop:finite-stage-tangent}(c)).
\item The inverse system on bar complexes satisfies Mittag-Leffler
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}): the transition maps
 on bar cohomology are surjective, so
 $\varprojlim^1_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) = 0$.
\end{enumerate}
The Mittag-Leffler condition gives
$H^n(\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg)))
\cong \varprojlim_N H^n(\barB(\cA_{\leq N}))$
(no $\varprojlim^1$ correction). The completed cobar differential
is continuous by
Proposition~\ref{prop:inverse-limit-differential-continuity}
(automatic for inverse systems of finite-stage curved dg
coalgebras). By the MC4 reduction principle
(Proposition~\ref{prop:mc4-reduction-principle},
now verified for this tower), the completed cobar-bar counit
restricts at each finite stage to the proved
quasi-isomorphism
$\Omega(\barB(\cA_{\leq N})) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA_{\leq N}$,
and the Mittag-Leffler condition ensures the inverse limit
of quasi-isomorphisms is a quasi-isomorphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-4: tangent Lie algebra identification;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk4-inverse-limit}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-4!inverse limit construction}
\index{tangent Lie algebra!inverse limit}
By Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler}}, the
inverse system $\{\mathfrak{g}_N\}_{N \geq 1}$ of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:finite-stage-tangent}} satisfies
Mittag-Leffler with surjective transition maps, and the tangent
Lie algebra of the factorization formal moduli problem is
\[
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}
\;=\;
T_{*}\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}
\;\cong\;
\varprojlim_N\, \mathfrak{g}_N.
\]
The remaining content of DK-4 is the identification of this
inverse limit with the dg-shifted Yangian:
\[
\varprojlim_N\, \mathfrak{g}_N
\;\cong\;
\Ydg_{\cA}.
\]
This identification is equivalent to showing that the derivation
complex $\operatorname{Der}(\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg)))$
carries the dg-shifted RTT structure
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}}\textup{)}:
the Maurer--Cartan element $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$, the
translation operator, and the twisted coproduct.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[DK-4 reduced to structure identification]
\label{rem:dk4-mittag-leffler}
\index{Mittag-Leffler condition!DK-4 reduction}
Theorem~\ref{thm:rtt-mittag-leffler} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian} resolve the
\emph{analytic} part of DK-4: the inverse limit exists, is
well-behaved ($\varprojlim^1 = 0$), and the completed bar-cobar
equivalence holds. What remains is the \emph{algebraic}
identification of $\varprojlim_N \mathfrak{g}_N$ with the
dg-shifted Yangian; specifically, the three structural
data:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item the Maurer--Cartan element $r(z)$ arises as the
 degree-$2$ part of the bar propagator~$\tau$;
\item the translation operator is the derivation induced by
 $T_{ij}^{(r)} \mapsto T_{ij}^{(r+1)}$;
\item the twisted coproduct on $\widehat{\barB}(Y(\fg))$
 decomposes as the Drinfeld coproduct on~$\Ydg$.
\end{enumerate}
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier} isolates the
finite-stage local shadow of~(a): on the standard type-$A$ tower,
the degree-$2$ packet is reduced to the auxiliary-kernel identity
$L_a(u) = R_{0a}(u - a)$ and its residue/mixed-tensor descendants,
which form the tangent-space computation of the moduli problem
restricted to the fundamental evaluation line
(Remark~\ref{rem:dk4-formal-moduli-vs-rtt}(ii)).

The completed bar-cobar equivalence
\textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}\textup{)}
also clarifies the bar-side setting for the remaining MC3 extension
conjectures
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:mc3-formal-moduli-reformulation}):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Pro-Weyl recovery}
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{thm:pro-weyl-recovery}\textup{)}:
 on the theorematic type-$A$ surface of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:pro-weyl-recovery}, the Weyl truncation tower
 $\{W_m\}$ can be viewed inside the completed bar/factorization
 setting supplied by Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian}.
 What the completed bar-cobar theorem does \emph{not} by itself prove
 is the existence of that pro-Weyl tower, the surjectivity/Mittag--Leffler
 statements, or the inverse-limit identification
 $M(\Psi) \simeq R\varprojlim_m W_m$ outside the separately proved
 type-$A$ lane.

\item \emph{DK on compacts}
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}\textup{)}:
 Theorem~\ref{thm:ind-completed-extension} gives the formal
 ind-completion of the evaluation-generated core. Comparing the
 Francis--Gaitsgory pro-nilpotent completion to that cocompletion,
 and then extending the completed bar-cobar equivalence across the
 desired compact generators, is additional input. What remains is
 the compact shifted-prefundamental generation input together with
 the extra compact-core extension/completion comparison package;
 even on the type-$A$ surface, these steps are not consequences of
 Corollary~\ref{cor:completed-bar-cobar-yangian} alone.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Ordered \texorpdfstring{$\Eone$}{E1}-factorization category]
\label{def:ordered-e1-factorization}
\index{factorization category!ordered $\Eone$-|textbf}
For an $\Eone$-chiral algebra~$\cA$ on a curve~$X$,
the \emph{ordered $\Eone$-factorization category}
$\Factord(X;\cA)$ is the stable $\infty$-category
of $\cA$-modules on ordered configuration spaces,
with the associative chiral tensor structure induced
by the $\Eone$-operad action
(Definition~\ref{def:e1-factorization-category}).
\ifannalsedition\else
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\fi
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Spectral quantum group]
\label{def:spectral-quantum-group}
\index{quantum group!spectral|textbf}
For a Koszul dual~$\cA^!$ with spectral $R$-matrix~$R_{\cA}$,
the \emph{spectral quantum group} $\QGspec(R_{\cA})$ is the
factorization quantum group whose representation category
is controlled by the spectral $R$-matrix, in the sense of
Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
\ifannalsedition\else
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\fi
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[dg-shifted Yangian]
\label{def:dg-shifted-yangian}
\index{Yangian!dg-shifted|textbf}
For a Koszul dual~$\cA^!$, the \emph{dg-shifted Yangian}
$\Ydg_{\cA}$ is the dg algebra with translation operator,
Maurer--Cartan element~$r(z)$, and twisted coproduct,
as constructed in the perturbative holomorphic-topological
setting of Costello--Yamazaki~\cite{costello-yamazaki} and
Costello--Gwilliam~\cite{CG17}.
\ifannalsedition\else
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\fi
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[RTT-adapted filtration on a dg-shifted Yangian]
\label{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}
Let $\Ydg_{\cA}$ be a dg-shifted Yangian. An
\emph{RTT-adapted filtration} on $\Ydg_{\cA}$ is a descending
filtration by closed dg ideals
\[
F^1\Ydg_{\cA} \supset F^2\Ydg_{\cA} \supset \cdots
\]
such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $\Ydg_{\cA} \cong
 \varprojlim_N \Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}$ as a complete dg algebra;
\item the differential, translation operator, Maurer--Cartan element
 $r(z)$, and twisted coproduct preserve the filtration;
\item each quotient
 $\Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}$ is dg quasi-isomorphic to the finite
 RTT stage $Y_{\le N}$; and
\item these quotient quasi-isomorphisms are compatible with the RTT
 truncation maps and the finite-stage bar-cobar data.
\end{enumerate}
This is the exact H-level input required by
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Formal quotient criterion for dg-shifted Yangians;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:dg-shifted-quotient-criterion}
Let $\Ydg_{\cA}$ be a dg algebra equipped with:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a translation operator;
\item a Maurer--Cartan element $r(z)$;
\item a twisted coproduct; and
\item a descending sequence of closed dg ideals
 \[
 F^1\Ydg_{\cA} \supset F^2\Ydg_{\cA} \supset \cdots
 \]
 preserved by the differential, translation operator,
 Maurer--Cartan element, and twisted coproduct.
\end{enumerate}
Then every finite quotient
\[
\Ydg_{\cA}/F^{N+1}\Ydg_{\cA}
\]
inherits the same dg-shifted Yangian type of structure, and the quotient
maps form an inverse system of dg-shifted objects.

If, in addition, these quotients are dg quasi-isomorphic to the finite
RTT stages $Y_{\le N}$ compatibly with RTT truncation, evaluation
modules, and the degree-$2$ twisting morphism, then
Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration} holds and
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} applies.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Preservation of the ideals by the differential descends the dg
structure to each quotient. Preservation by the translation operator,
Maurer--Cartan element, and twisted coproduct descends those data as
well, because each operation factors through the quotient by the same
ideal. Compatibility of the quotient maps with the preserved
operations makes the family of quotients an inverse system of
dg-shifted objects.

The additional compatibility hypotheses are exactly the remaining items
of Definition~\ref{def:rtt-adapted-filtration}. Once they are checked,
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} gives the
comparison with $\widehat Y_{\mathrm{RTT}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Full derived Drinfeld--Kohno bridge;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:full-dk-bridge}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!full bridge|textbf}
\index{triple equivalence!factorization--Yangian--quantum group}
For affine/Yangian-type modular Koszul $\Eone$-objects~$\cA$
satisfying:
\textup{(i)}~$\Eone$-Koszulness,
\textup{(ii)}~pro-nilpotent completion/convergence,
\textup{(iii)}~existence of spectral $R$-matrix data, and
\textup{(iv)}~extension of the evaluation-locus comparison to
the full category~$\mathcal{O}$,
there are equivalences of braided monoidal stable
$\infty$-categories
\begin{equation}\label{eq:triple-equivalence}
\Factord(X;\cA)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}},
\end{equation}
compatible with evaluation modules and the KZ monodromy package on the
evaluation locus.

\smallskip\noindent
\emph{Status.}
Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-derived-dk}} is the DK-3 outer
factorization equivalence; Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}}
proves DK-1 on the evaluation locus. The Yangian middle term and the
triple formulation are the DK-4/DK-5 completion.
\ifannalsedition\else
(Contributing to Conjecture~\ref{conj:master-dk-kl}.)
\fi
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[Formal reduction principle from DK-3 to
DK-4/DK-5; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction}
Fix an affine/Yangian-type modular Koszul $\Eone$-object~$\cA$.
Assume the DK-3 outer equivalence is established on the ordered
factorization model, namely that there is a braided monoidal
equivalence
\[
\Factord(X;\cA)
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
compatible with evaluation modules and extending the
evaluation-locus comparison of
Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}. Then the remaining task in
passing from this outer factorization comparison to a completed
H-level bridge is exactly the construction of a dg-shifted
Yangian~$\Ydg_{\cA}$ whose RTT-adapted filtration satisfies
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}, together with
the module-category enhancement
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}.
\]
In particular, once DK-3 is in hand, the genuinely new Yangian input is
the MC4 H-level comparison problem and its passage from completed
dg-algebra comparison to completed module-category equivalence; it is
not a second factorization comparison on the evaluation locus.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The ordered factorization term and the right-hand spectral quantum-group
term in~\eqref{eq:triple-equivalence} are fixed by the assumed DK-3
outer equivalence, so after DK-3 the only missing part of the desired
triple equivalence is the middle equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\simeq
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}.
\]
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion} shows that, once
$\Ydg_{\cA}$ carries a separated complete RTT-adapted filtration with
the theorematic finite RTT quotients, the underlying completed dg
algebra comparison with the standard RTT completion becomes formal.
Thus the remaining mathematical content is precisely the MC4
construction of that filtered H-level target together with the passage
from the dg comparison to the completed module-category equivalence
displayed above. This is exactly the DK-4/DK-5 remainder.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Application to the full bridge conjecture]
\label{rem:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction-application}
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction} isolates the Yangian
residue inside Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}: once the outer
factorization equivalence is supplied, what remains is the
RTT-adapted H-level realization and the completed
module-category equivalence.
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% The Bridge Theorem package
%% ================================================================
\begin{remark}[The Bridge Theorem package]
\label{rem:bridge-theorem-programme}
\index{Bridge Theorem!package|textbf}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!Bridge Theorem package}
We decompose
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge} (the \textbf{Bridge
Theorem} target) into four sub-targets and six lemmas.

\smallskip\noindent
The triple equivalence~\eqref{eq:triple-equivalence} asserts that
three deformation-theoretic presentations are matched:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the MC problem for the \emph{factorization convolution algebra}
 $\operatorname{Conv}_{\Eone}(\bar B(\cA), \cA^!)$ on ordered configuration
 spaces, presenting~$\Factord$;
\item the completed MC problem for the \emph{Yangian convolution algebra}
 $\widehat{\operatorname{Conv}}(\bar B(Y), Y^!)$, producing
 the dg-side category
 $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_\cA)$; and
\item the \emph{spectral quantum-group presentation}
 $\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_\cA))$.
\end{enumerate}
Each sub-target B1--B4 below is a specific extension, completion, or
identification problem. The proved core (Lemmas~1--2) establishes
the deformation-theoretic equivalence on the evaluation-generated
locus; the open targets extend it to the full highest-weight
category, complete the pronilpotent tower on the dg side, and
identify the spectral quantum-group presentation.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Four sub-targets.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{B\arabic*.}]
\item \label{item:B1}
 \emph{Full $\mathcal{O}$-Koszul extension.}
 The Yangian is Koszul on the full category~$\mathcal{O}$, not only
 on the evaluation locus. Then the bar spectral sequence collapses,
 minimal resolutions exist for all highest-weight objects, and
 the duality extends from evaluation modules to
 $D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}) \simeq D^b(\mathcal{O}_{Y_{-\hbar}})$.
 (Extends Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-dk23-inputs}.)

\item \label{item:B2}
 \emph{Yangian tower completion.}
 The four checks of Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-mc4-checklist}:
 (1)~finite RTT truncations in the proved $\Eone$-Koszul regime;
 (2)~compatible descent of finite-stage bar/cobar;
 (3)~Mittag--Leffler on $\{H^m(\bar B(Y_{\le N}))\}_N$;
 (4)~H-level comparison with an RTT-adapted dg model.
 Items~(1)--(3) are theorematic for the standard RTT tower; item~(4)
 is the genuine hard residue that upgrades the standard RTT
 completion to the desired H-level dg model.
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-tower-mc4-criterion}.)

\item \label{item:B3}
 \emph{Boundary/line realization.}
 There is a sufficiently rich holomorphic boundary condition~$b$
 with boundary chiral algebra~$V_b$, a line-to-boundary comparison
 functor
 $F_b \colon \mathcal{C}_T \to V_b\text{-mod}$,
 and a compatible line-side algebraic/spectral package controlled by
 a dg-shifted Yangian.
 The benchmark families provide only calibration and prototype
 evidence for this package, not a theorematic realization of
 $F_b$ in general.
 (Fresh input: Costello--Dimofte--Gaiotto~\cite{CDG2023},
 Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25}.)

\item \label{item:B4}
 \emph{Spectral quantum-group comparison.}
 The open spectral comparison is to identify the boundary spectral
 $R$-matrix data furnished by such a boundary/line package with
 Latyntsev's factorization quantum-group package
 \cite{Latyntsev23}; on that surface the middle category identifies with
 $\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))$.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Six-lemma architecture.}
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\textbf{Lemma} & \textbf{Content} & \textbf{Status} & \textbf{Input} \\
\hline
1 & Evaluation-locus factorization bridge
 & \textbf{Proved} & Thm~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval} \\
2 & Verdier $= R^{-1}$
 & \textbf{Proved} & Thm~\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian} \\
3 & Category~$\mathcal{O}$ extension
 & Open & Needs B1 \\
4 & Tower completion
 & Open & Needs B2 \\
5 & Boundary/line equivalence $F_b$
 & Open & Needs B3 \\
6 & Spectral quantum-group identification
 & Open & Needs B4 \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\emph{Lemmas~1--2 are proved. Lemmas~3--6 are the kill targets.}
Once all six close, the full Bridge Theorem
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}) is done.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Benchmark ladder} (fixed order, without skipping):
\[
\beta\gamma\text{/Heis}
\;\to\; \hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2
\;\to\; Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)
\;\to\; Y(\mathfrak{sl}_3)
\;\to\; Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)\text{ cat-}\mathcal{O}
\;\to\; \text{shifted Yangian tower.}
\]
Toroidal and elliptic extensions come only after the tower theorem
exists.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Bridge Criterion Theorem; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:bridge-criterion}
\index{Bridge Theorem!criterion theorem|textbf}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{B1}:
 the full category-$\mathcal{O}$ Koszul extension package on the
 Yangian side: the bar spectral sequence collapses for all
 highest-weight objects, minimal resolutions exist, and the resulting
 bar/cobar comparison extends from evaluation modules to the full
 highest-weight category;
\item \textup{B2}:
 theorematic finite RTT truncations in the proved $\Eone$-Koszul
 regime, compatible descent of finite-stage bar/cobar, Mittag--Leffler
 stabilization on $\{H^m(\bar B(Y_{\le N}))\}_N$, inverse-limit
 identification of the completed RTT tower, and the H-level
 realization/comparison packet identifying that standard completion
 with the dg-shifted Yangian~$\Ydg_{\cA}$; and
\item \textup{B4}:
 the spectral quantum-group comparison identifying the middle
 category with Latyntsev's factorization quantum-group
 category~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
\end{enumerate}
Then there are equivalences of braided monoidal stable
$\infty$-categories
\[
\Factord(X;\cA)
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\;\simeq\;
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}},
\]
compatible with evaluation modules and the KZ monodromy package on the
evaluation locus,
with Verdier duality acting by $R_{\cA} \mapsto R_{\cA}^{-1}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The argument combines the proved evaluation-locus factorization bridge
with the later dg-side completion and spectral-comparison stages.

\emph{Step~1: Evaluation-locus factorization bridge.}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval} (Lemma~1), the
bar-cobar functor induces an equivalence on the evaluation-generated
factorization subcategory:
the twisting morphism
$\tau \in \operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(\cA),\cA^!)$ restricts on evaluation objects
to the Kazhdan twisting morphism, and Verdier duality reverses
collision-cycle orientation, inverting $R_\cA$ (Lemma~2).
This establishes the bridge on the evaluation-generated
parameters.

\emph{Step~2: Extension beyond the evaluation-generated locus.}
Under B1 (the full category-$\mathcal{O}$ Koszul extension package),
the bar spectral sequence collapses for all highest-weight objects,
minimal resolutions exist, and the bar/cobar comparison extends from
the evaluation-generated subcategory to the full highest-weight
category (Lemma~3).

\emph{Step~3: Pronilpotent MC completion.}
Under B2 (tower completion), the pronilpotent MC tower
$\{\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(Y_{\le N}), Y_{\le N}^!)\}_N$ converges:
the inverse limit of finite RTT stages realizes the standard completed
bar object and the corresponding standard RTT completion
\textup{(}Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-tower-mc4-criterion},
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-standard-mc4-package}\textup{)}. The
H-level realization/comparison packet then identifies that standard
completion with the dg-shifted Yangian~$\Ydg_{\cA}$
\textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}\textup{)}, so
$\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})$ becomes an actual
completed dg-side category rather than formal target data (Lemma~4).

\emph{Step~4: Spectral comparison.}
Under B4 (the spectral quantum-group comparison), the resulting
completed dg-side category is identified with the spectral
quantum-group side attached to the compared spectral datum in the sense
of Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}, namely with
$\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}$
(Lemma~6).

The broader boundary/line route surrounding B3 provides an
independent route to B4 by
combining three separate ingredients on the boundary side: the
line-to-boundary comparison $F_b$, the derived-center recovery map
$\beta_{\mathrm{der}}$ back to the bulk algebra, and the additional
spectral $R$-matrix identification on $V_b$-mod.

The separate degree-$2$ shadow assertion
$r(z)=\tau|_{\deg 2}$ is not part of the present criterion theorem;
it remains the additional benchmark package isolated in
Remark~\ref{rem:r-from-tau}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Criterion form of the bridge conjecture]
\label{rem:bridge-criterion-application}
Theorem~\ref{thm:bridge-criterion} is the formal implication behind
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}: once the three named inputs B1,
B2, and B4 are verified, the triple equivalence follows without any
additional Yangian calculation. The separate propagator-shadow
benchmark $r(z)=\tau|_{\deg 2}$ remains the additional comparison
package isolated in Remark~\ref{rem:r-from-tau}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[B1 obstruction: thick generation does not imply
\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{O}$}{O}-Koszulness]
\label{rem:b1-obstruction-analysis}
\index{Bridge Theorem!B1 obstruction analysis}
\index{Koszulness!category O obstruction}
The homological core of B1
\textup{(}Yangian Koszulness on the full
category~$\mathcal{O}$\textup{)} does \emph{not} follow from thick generation by
evaluation modules (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk2-thick-generation-all-types}) combined
with evaluation-locus Koszulness
(Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-koszul}), for a precise structural reason.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{What MC3 gives.}
 Thick generation (Corollary~\ref{cor:dk2-thick-generation-all-types})
 says every object of
 $D^b(\mathcal{O}^{\mathrm{eval}})$
 is built from evaluation modules by cones and retracts. The DK
 equivalence extends to this thick subcategory (DK-2/3,
 Corollary~\ref{cor:dk23-all-types}) \emph{without} requiring bar
 spectral sequence collapse on non-evaluation objects. The argument
 uses sectorwise convergence and cosheaf descent, bypassing Ext
 concentration entirely.

\item \emph{What B1 asks.}
 Koszulness on the full category~$\mathcal{O}$ means: for every
 pair of highest-weight modules $M$, $N$ in~$\mathcal{O}_{Y_\hbar}$,
 the bar spectral sequence computing $\Ext^*_Y(M, N)$
 collapses at~$E_2$. This is an Ext diagonal concentration
 condition: the Ext algebra
 $\Ext^*_{\mathcal{O}}(S, S)$ (with $S$ the direct sum of simple
 objects) should be generated in degree~$1$.

\item \emph{The gap.}
 Thick-subcategory closure does not preserve Ext concentration.
 If $L$ is built as a cone $L = \operatorname{cone}(f\colon V_1 \to V_2)$
 of evaluation modules, the long exact Ext sequence gives
 $\Ext^i(L, M)$ as a sub-quotient of $\Ext^i(V_j, M)$,
 but the connecting maps may introduce nontrivial higher-Ext
 contributions even when $\Ext^*(V_j, M)$ is concentrated. In
 particular, infinite-dimensional highest-weight modules (Verma
 modules, prefundamental modules~$L^-$) can have Ext groups that
 fail to concentrate, despite lying in the thick closure of
 evaluation modules.

\item \emph{Francis--Gaitsgory completion.}
 The FG pro-nilpotent completion
 (Remark~\ref{rem:francis-gaitsgory-mc3}) extends a
 compact-generator equivalence to the ind-completion. This
 requires the equivalence \emph{on compacts} first, which is
 exactly DK-2/3 on the evaluation-generated core. The extension
 to all highest-weight objects on the module side is a different
 question: it requires B1 (Ext concentration on all of~$\mathcal{O}$).
 The boundary/line path
 (Remark~\ref{rem:boundary-line-bridge-path}) attacks the bridge from
 a different comparison surface rather than proving this
 category-$\mathcal{O}$ extension.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
\emph{Summary.} The proved DK-2/3 evaluation-generated-core package
closes Lemma~3 of the bridge criterion on that core, which suffices
for the compact-generator version of the bridge. B1 (full
$\mathcal{O}$-Koszulness together with its resulting module-side
extension package) remains the genuinely open input for extending the
equivalence to all highest-weight modules. The
boundary/line path (Remark~\ref{rem:boundary-line-bridge-path})
provides a different route to the spectral comparison side of the
bridge, but on the current theorem surface it complements rather than
replaces B1.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The boundary/line path to the bridge]
\label{rem:boundary-line-bridge-path}
\index{Bridge Theorem!boundary/line path}
\index{line operators!bridge path}
The HT literature offers an independent route to the
bridge. Suppose there is a rich boundary condition~$b$ with
boundary chiral algebra~$V_b$ such that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $F_b \colon \mathcal{C}_T \to V_b\text{-mod}$ is an equivalence
 (the line-side algebraic model is identified with boundary modules);
\item $\beta_{\mathrm{der}} \colon V \to Z(V_b)_{\mathrm{der}}$
 is an isomorphism (bulk data can be recovered from the derived
 center of the boundary algebra).
\end{enumerate}
Then proving the spectral quantum-group identification on
$V_b$-mod is sufficient for the missing comparison
side of the bridge. If $F_b$ is an equivalence, then the line
side algebraic model is already present on $V_b$-mod.
If $\beta_{\mathrm{der}}$ is an isomorphism, the bulk
algebra is recoverable on the derived-center side. Thus the
boundary-module picture supplies the line-side algebraic data together
with a route back to the bulk algebra, while the separate spectral
identification on $V_b$-mod handles the remaining factorization-side
comparison.

This path avoids a direct attack on the spectral comparison by instead
working through the line-side algebraic model, which may be better
behaved. On the current bridge-criterion surface it complements B1
and B2 rather than replacing the category-$\mathcal{O}$ extension.
See Costello--Dimofte--Gaiotto~\cite{CDG2023} and
Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25} for the foundational
boundary/line structure, and Zeng~\cite{KZ2025} for derived-center
evidence.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$ identification:
MC projection as candidate gluing law]
\label{rem:r-from-tau}
\index{propagator!$r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$}
\index{Chriss--Ginzburg!gluing law}
A natural candidate gluing law between the two sides of the bridge is
the projection of Maurer--Cartan elements between two convolution
algebras recorded below.

The universal MC element $\Theta_\cA \in
\MC(\mathfrak{g}_\cA^{\mathrm{mod}})$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:chriss-ginzburg-structure}) encodes the full
algebra structure of~$\cA$ as a graph sum over stable graphs with
propagator insertions on internal edges
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-bar-hamiltonian}).
Its genus-$0$, degree-$2$ projection is the bar-complex propagator
$\tau \in \operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(\cA), \cA^!)$ on ordered configuration
spaces, with kernel
$\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$.

The dg-shifted Yangian~$\Ydg_\cA$
(Definition~\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}) is governed by its own
MC element $r(z) \in \cA^! \otimes \cA^!(z^{-1})$.
The identification
\[
r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}
\]
is the assertion that \emph{the Yangian MC element is the
degree-$2$ shadow of the universal bar-complex MC element}.
In the language of the shadow obstruction tower
(\S\ref{sec:nms-shadow-calculus}), $r(z)$ is the
same-genus, degree-$2$ slice of~$\Theta_\cA$: the scalar
shadow~$\kappa(\cA)$ is the trace of this slice, and $r(z)$ is
the full tensorial content.

This is the single cleanest CG benchmark for the Bridge Theorem
package: compute $\tau|_{\deg 2}$ explicitly in each benchmark
family and verify it matches the known $r$-matrix.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[DK-4 reduction to the fundamental residue packet in
standard type~A; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction} and work with the
standard type-A RTT tower. Then the remaining DK-4 input is reduced to
the boundary-strip identities
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(N)=0
\qquad (0\le a\le N,\ N\ge 0)
\]
for the defects
\[
\Delta_{a,0}(N)
=\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,0}(N)
-\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,0}(N),
\]
together with the standard twisted-coproduct multiplication law on
fundamental evaluation modules. Equivalently, for the standard type-A
tower it is enough to prove the pairwise auxiliary-kernel identity
\[
L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)
\]
on the fundamental evaluation line.

If in addition the one-factor line operator is functorial for the
diagonal $\mathfrak{sl}_M$-action and normalized by
$L_a(u)\to 1$ as $u\to\infty$, then the same DK-4 input is further
reduced to transport of the standard residue formula
\[
\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P.
\]
For $M\ge 2$, this transport statement is further reduced to the
ordered mixed-tensor
identity
\[
\Xi_a(e_1\otimes e_2)=-\hbar(e_2\otimes e_1).
\]

By
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line},
this single ordered tensor-line computation already determines the full
residue operator $\Xi_a=-\hbar P$ uniformly in the rank.
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
shows that this residue formula already holds on the theorematic
standard RTT tower itself. Thus the genuinely live local input is to
identify the dg-shifted or factorization one-factor kernel with that
standard normalized residue, equivalently with the same mixed-tensor
matrix coefficient on the fundamental line.

Under one-loop exactness,
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-mixed-tensor-criterion}
reduces this transport problem further to the ordered mixed-tensor
coefficient of the degree-$2$ twisting morphism $r(z)=\tau|_{\deg 2}$.
Corollary~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-seed-normalized-coefficient}
shows that, in the standard logarithmic normalization, this is
equivalently the ordered mixed-tensor coefficient of the operator
$r_a^{\mathrm{fund}}(z)$ itself.

Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-scalar-normalization}
then removes the remaining one-loop matrix ambiguity: after
degree-$2$ scalar normalization, the only genuinely live datum is the
scalar coefficient of the permutation operator. In particular,
Corollary~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-casimir-normalization}
shows that the trace-zero convention
$P-\frac{1}{M}\id$ reduces to the same scalar packet, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-degree2-fundamental-casimir}
computes that scalar as $-1$ once the standard fundamental Casimir
insertion is identified.
Corollary~\ref{prop:factorization-fundamental-casimir-identity} proves
that the factorization side already satisfies this identity, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-factorization-shared-seed} shows that
any dg-shifted realization presented by the same ordered bar seed
inherits the same coefficient. Thus the genuinely live local step is
no longer a new coefficient computation, but the realization of the
dg-shifted target with that shared bar seed.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk-mc4-reduction}, once DK-3 is fixed
the remaining work is to construct a dg-shifted Yangian with an
RTT-adapted filtration satisfying
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}. The finite
quotient comparison required there is reduced by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-oneloop-kernel-criterion} to the
coefficient identities
$\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{line}}_{a,b}(N)
=\mathsf{K}^{\mathrm{RTT}}_{a,b}(N)$,
by Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-boundary-seed} to the boundary
strip $\Delta_{a,0}(N)$, and by
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-fundamental-propagation} to the
fundamental evaluation family together with the standard
twisted-coproduct multiplication law.

Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-auxiliary-kernel-criterion} then
reduces this boundary-strip packet to the pairwise kernel identity
$L_a(u)=R_{0a}(u-a)$ on the fundamental line. Under the symmetry and
normalization hypotheses,
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-residue-reduction} reduces that
identity to the residue formula
$\operatorname*{Res}_{u=a}L_a(u)=-\hbar P$, and
Corollary~\ref{cor:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-single-line} reduces the
transport-normalized residue formula further to the ordered
mixed-tensor check displayed in
the statement, while
Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-typea-uniform-single-line}
shows that this one check already determines the whole residue
operator uniformly in~$M$. Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
then identifies that residue explicitly on the theorematic standard
RTT side.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Remaining type-$A$ DK frontier]
After DK-3, the live analytic input on the standard type-$A$ tower is
the H-level dg-shifted realization together with the compact-core
DK-5 packet. Proposition~\ref{prop:dg-shifted-rtt-standard-typea-local-packet}
shows that no new residue coefficient remains to be computed inside
the standard RTT tower itself.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[DK-5 reduction to compact-generator comparison;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators}
Assume the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier}. Let
\[
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}
\subset \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA}),
\qquad
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\subset \operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategories generated by the completed images of finite
ordered tensor products of fundamental evaluation modules. Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item both ambient stable categories are compactly generated, and
 their compact objects are the thick idempotent-complete closures of
 $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ and
 $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$, respectively;
\item the DK-4 comparison supplies an exact colimit-preserving functor
 \[
 F_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
 \operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
 \longrightarrow
 \operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}\!
 \bigl(\QGspec(R_{\cA})\bigr)^{\mathrm{op}}
 \]
 compatible with the dg comparison
 $\Ydg_{\cA}\xrightarrow{\sim}\widehat Y_{\mathrm{RTT}}$ and with the
 DK-3 transport on the evaluation-generated packet; and
\item the restriction of $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ to
 $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ is an equivalence onto
 $\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$.
\end{enumerate}
Then $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence of stable categories. In
particular, after DK-4 the remaining DK-5 input is the compact-generator
comparison on the completed module categories; the passage from that
packet to the full completed equivalence is formal.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By assumption~\textup{(iii)}, the functor
$F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence on the chosen generator packet.
Because $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is exact, it preserves shifts, cones, and
direct summands, so it is an equivalence on the thick idempotent-complete
closures of that packet. Assumption~\textup{(i)} identifies those
closures with the compact objects in the two ambient categories.

Now both categories are compactly generated, and
$F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ preserves colimits by assumption~\textup{(ii)}.
Hence the same uniqueness-of-extension mechanism used in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-co-contra-correspondence} applies: an exact
colimit-preserving functor between compactly generated stable
categories is determined by its restriction to compact generators, and
an equivalence on those generators extends to an equivalence on the
whole categories. Therefore $F_{\mathrm{comp}}$ is an equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Compact-core comparison reduces to the completed
fundamental packet; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators}. Write
\[
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega
:=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}
\bigl(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}\bigr),
\qquad
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
:=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}
\bigl(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\bigr)
\]
for the compact cores of the two completed categories, and let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}\subset \mathcal{C}_Y^\omega,
\qquad
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\subset \mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
be the full subcategories spanned by the completed fundamental
evaluation modules themselves. Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item each compact core is the smallest full stable
 idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategory containing its
 completed fundamental packet;
\item there exist exact braided monoidal functors
 \[
 KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
 \mathcal{C}_Y^\omega \to \mathcal{C}_q^\omega,
 \qquad
 LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
 \mathcal{C}_q^\omega \to \mathcal{C}_Y^\omega;
 \]
\item the restrictions of these functors to
 $\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ and
 $\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$ recover the DK-3 transport on the
 completed fundamental evaluation packet; and
\item both composites
 \[
 LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}} \circ KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}},
 \qquad
 KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}} \circ LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}
 \]
 are naturally isomorphic to the identity on the completed
 fundamental packets.
\end{enumerate}
Then the two functors are quasi-inverse exact braided monoidal
equivalences
\[
KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{C}_q^\omega,
\qquad
LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}\colon
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{C}_Y^\omega.
\]

Equivalently, once the compact cores are generated by completed
fundamental evaluation modules, the compact-core DK-5 packet is forced
by transport on that completed fundamental packet.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
This is the compact-core analogue of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk3-generated-core}. By
assumption~\textup{(i)}, each compact core is obtained from its
completed fundamental packet by finite iterates of shifts, cones,
direct summands, and ordered tensor products. Exact braided monoidal
functors preserve each of these operations. Therefore any natural
transformation between exact braided monoidal functors that is an
isomorphism on the completed fundamental packet remains an isomorphism
on the full compact core.

Apply this to the two composites in assumption~\textup{(iv)}. Since
they are naturally isomorphic to the identity on the completed
fundamental packets, they are naturally isomorphic to the identity on
$\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega$ and $\mathcal{C}_q^\omega$. Hence
$KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}$ and $LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}$ are
quasi-inverse exact braided monoidal equivalences.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[DK-5 comparison functor is the ind-extension of the
compact core; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-ind-extension}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators}. Write
\[
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega
:=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}
\bigl(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}\bigr),
\qquad
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
:=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}
\bigl(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\bigr)
\]
for the compact cores of the two completed categories. Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the ambient categories
 $\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})$ and
 $\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}$
 are presentable, stable, and compactly generated, with compact
 objects exactly $\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega$ and $\mathcal{C}_q^\omega$;
\item there is an exact equivalence
 \[
 F^\omega\colon \mathcal{C}_Y^\omega \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{C}_q^\omega
 \]
 whose restriction to the completed fundamental evaluation packet
 agrees with the DK-3 transport on the evaluation-generated core.
\end{enumerate}
Then there exists a unique exact colimit-preserving equivalence
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(F^\omega)\colon
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
extending $F^\omega$.

In particular, once the compact-core equivalence is constructed, the
comparison functor appearing in
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators} and its
compatibility with DK-3 on the compact generator packet are formal.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By assumption~\textup{(i)}, each ambient category is the
ind-completion of its compact objects:
\[
\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})
\simeq
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega),
\qquad
\operatorname{Rep}^{\mathrm{spec}}(\QGspec(R_{\cA}))^{\mathrm{op}}
\simeq
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C}_q^\omega).
\]
This is the same compact-generation mechanism used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ind-completed-extension}: a presentable stable
compactly generated category is recovered from its compact part by
ind-completion.

Now apply the universal property of ind-completion to the exact
equivalence $F^\omega$. It extends uniquely to an exact
colimit-preserving functor
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(F^\omega)\colon
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega)
\longrightarrow
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathcal{C}_q^\omega),
\]
and because $F^\omega$ is already an equivalence, its ind-extension is
an equivalence as well. Transporting along the displayed
identifications of the ambient categories yields the claimed functor.

The final sentence is immediate: once the compact-core equivalence is
fixed, the completed comparison functor is forced to be this unique
ind-extension, so no separate completed-level functor construction
remains.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[DK-5 reduces to the compact-core equivalence;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-dk5-compact-core}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{prop:yangian-typea-dg-local-closure}. Assume further
that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the completed dg-shifted and spectral categories are presentable,
 stable, and compactly generated;
\item their compact objects are the thick idempotent-complete closures
 of the completed fundamental evaluation packets; and
\item those compact cores are exactly equivalent in a way compatible
 with DK-3 on the completed fundamental packet.
\end{enumerate}
Then the standard type-$A$ Yangian DK-5 packet closes.

Equivalently, after the local dg-shifted packet is closed, the
remaining DK-5 input is exactly the compact-core equivalence; the
completed comparison functor itself is formal.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Under
Corollary~\ref{prop:yangian-typea-dg-local-closure}, the local DK-4
packet is already closed, so only DK-5 remains. Assumptions
\textup{(i)}--\textup{(iii)} are precisely the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-ind-extension}, which produces the
unique exact colimit-preserving equivalence between the completed
categories. This is exactly the DK-5 conclusion.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[DK-5 reduces to compact generation plus completed
fundamental-packet transport; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{prop:yangian-typea-dg-local-closure}. Assume further
that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the completed dg-shifted and spectral categories are presentable,
 stable, and compactly generated;
\item their compact objects are the smallest full stable
 idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategories containing the
 completed fundamental evaluation packets; and
\item there exist exact braided monoidal functors between those compact
 cores whose restrictions to the completed fundamental evaluation
 packets recover the DK-3 transport and whose composites are the
 identity on that packet.
\end{enumerate}
Then the standard type-$A$ Yangian DK-5 packet closes.

Equivalently, once the local dg-shifted packet is closed, the remaining
categorical input is compact generation together with transport on the
completed fundamental evaluation packet; the compact-core equivalence
and the ambient completed comparison functor are then formal.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Assumption~\textup{(ii)} identifies the compact objects with the
compact cores appearing in
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}. By
assumption~\textup{(iii)}, that proposition yields an exact
equivalence between the compact cores. Now apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-ind-extension} to extend that
compact-core equivalence uniquely to an exact colimit-preserving
equivalence of the ambient completed categories. This is exactly the
DK-5 conclusion.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Compact-core DK-5 functors from realization of a
finite-dimensional factorization DK pair; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-core-realization}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}. Let
\[
KZ_{\mathrm{fd}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_M))
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
\[
LZ_{\mathrm{fd}}\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_M))
\]
be quasi-inverse exact braided monoidal equivalences whose restrictions
to the finite-dimensional fundamental evaluation packet recover the
standard type-$A$ DK transport on that packet. Assume there exist exact braided
monoidal equivalences
\[
\quad
J_Y^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_M))
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega,
\qquad
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
whose restrictions to the evaluation generators identify them with the
completed fundamental evaluation packets
$\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{Y}$ and
$\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}$.
Then
\[
KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}
:=
J_q^\omega \circ KZ_{\mathrm{fd}} \circ (J_Y^\omega)^{-1},
\qquad
LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}
:=
J_Y^\omega \circ LZ_{\mathrm{fd}} \circ (J_q^\omega)^{-1}
\]
are quasi-inverse exact braided monoidal equivalences
\[
\mathcal{C}_Y^\omega \xrightarrow{\sim} \mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
whose restrictions to the completed fundamental evaluation packets
recover the DK-3 transport. In particular, the packet hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet} are automatic.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed functors are composites of exact braided monoidal
equivalences, hence are themselves exact braided monoidal
equivalences. Because the completion equivalences
$J_Y^\omega$ and $J_q^\omega$ identify the evaluation generators with
the completed fundamental evaluation packets, the restrictions of
$KZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}$ and $LZ^\omega_{\mathrm{comp}}$ to those
packets are exactly the transported DK-3 packet and its inverse. Therefore the
composites are the identity on the completed fundamental packets, and
the final sentence follows immediately.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-dimensional Yangian factorization core is
generated by fundamental evaluation objects; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:yangian-fd-fundamental-generation}
For $\mathfrak{sl}_M$, the braided monoidal stable category
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_M))
\]
is the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategory containing the fundamental evaluation objects.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:dk2-thick-generation-typeA}, every
finite-dimensional irreducible Yangian module is a subquotient of a
tensor product of fundamental evaluation modules. Applying
Lemma~\ref{lem:composition-thick-generation} to the abelian category of
finite-dimensional Yangian modules shows that the bounded derived
category is the thick triangulated closure of those fundamental
evaluation modules. The factorization category
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_M))
\]
is this same finite-dimensional stable category equipped with the
ordered factorization tensor product, and ordered tensor products of
fundamental evaluation objects remain inside the same closure.
Therefore the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided
monoidal subcategory containing the fundamental evaluation objects is
the whole finite-dimensional Yangian factorization category.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Finite-dimensional quantum-group factorization core is
generated by fundamental evaluation objects; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:quantum-fd-fundamental-generation}
For $\mathfrak{sl}_M$, the braided monoidal stable category
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
is the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategory containing the fundamental evaluation objects.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Finite-dimensional irreducible type-$A$ quantum-loop modules are
classified by their Drinfeld polynomials / highest $\ell$-weights, and
factoring those polynomials into linear terms expresses every simple as
a subquotient of an ordered tensor product of fundamental evaluation
modules (\cite[Ch.~12]{ChariPressley94}, \cite[\S2]{Hernandez05}).
Applying Lemma~\ref{lem:composition-thick-generation} to the abelian
category of finite-dimensional quantum-loop modules shows that the
bounded derived category is the thick triangulated closure of the
fundamental evaluation modules. The factorization category
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
is this same finite-dimensional stable category equipped with the
ordered factorization tensor product, and ordered tensor products of
fundamental evaluation objects remain inside the same closure.
Therefore the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided
monoidal subcategory containing the fundamental evaluation objects is
the whole finite-dimensional quantum-group factorization category.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Spectral compact-core realization is formal from
generator transport; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-realization-formal}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-fundamental-packet}. Assume
\[
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
=
\operatorname{thick}^{\mathrm{idemp}}(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q})
\]
is the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategory containing the completed fundamental evaluation packet.
Let
\[
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\subset
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategory generated by finite ordered tensor products of
fundamental evaluation objects, and let
\[
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
be an exact braided monoidal functor whose restriction
\[
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\]
is an equivalence onto the completed generator packet. Then
\(J_q^\omega\) is an exact braided monoidal equivalence.

Equivalently, on the spectral side no additional comparison on the full
compact core remains once the generator-level completion transport is
constructed.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:quantum-fd-fundamental-generation}, the source is the
smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal subcategory
containing the fundamental evaluation objects. By hypothesis, the
target enjoys the same generation property for the completed
fundamental packet. Because \(J_q^\omega\) is exact and braided
monoidal, it preserves shifts, cones, direct summands, and ordered
tensor products. Since its restriction to
\(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}\) is already an equivalence onto
\(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\), the same thick-closure argument as
in Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-compact-generators} upgrades that
equivalence on the generator packet to an equivalence on the thick
idempotent-complete closures. Those closures are exactly the source
and target by Lemma~\ref{lem:quantum-fd-fundamental-generation} and the
displayed hypothesis on \(\mathcal{C}_q^\omega\). Thus \(J_q^\omega\)
is an exact braided monoidal equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[On the spectral side, ordered tensor-generator
transport is forced by the completed fundamental packet;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-fundamental-packet}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-realization-formal}. Let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\subset
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategory spanned by the fundamental evaluation objects
themselves, and let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\subset
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
be the full subcategory spanned by their completed spectral images.
Assume that the exact braided monoidal functor
\[
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
restricts to an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}.
\]
Then its restriction
\[
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\]
is automatically an equivalence onto the completed spectral
generator packet. Consequently, the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-realization-formal} are
already satisfied, so \(J_q^\omega\) is an exact braided monoidal
equivalence.

Equivalently, on the spectral side the genuinely non-formal packet is
not the whole ordered tensor-generator family: it is enough to place
the individual fundamental evaluation objects inside the completed
spectral category in an exact braided-monoidal way.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:quantum-fd-fundamental-generation}, the source
\[
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
is the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided monoidal
subcategory containing \(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}\). By the
standing hypothesis of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-realization-formal}, the
target \(\mathcal{C}_q^\omega\) enjoys the same generation property for
\(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\). Because \(J_q^\omega\) is exact
and braided monoidal, it preserves shifts, cones, direct summands, and
ordered tensor products. Since its restriction to
\(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}\) is already an equivalence onto
\(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\), the same thick-closure argument as
in Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-dg-realization-formal} upgrades
that equivalence on the completed fundamental packet to an exact
braided monoidal equivalence on the full finite-dimensional spectral
core.

In particular, the restriction of \(J_q^\omega\) to
\(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}\) is an equivalence onto
\(\mathcal{G}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}\), since those packets are the full
subcategories generated by finite ordered tensor products of the same
fundamental objects on the source and target sides. Therefore the
generator-packet hypothesis of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-realization-formal} is
automatic. The final sentence follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Type-\texorpdfstring{$A$}{A} quantum-group fundamental packet is generated
by the vector evaluation line; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:quantum-fd-vector-fundamental-generation}
Let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\subset
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategory spanned by the vector evaluation objects.
Then every fundamental evaluation object of
\(\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}\)
belongs to the smallest full stable idempotent-complete braided
monoidal subcategory containing
\(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\).

Equivalently, on the finite-dimensional spectral side the full
fundamental packet is generated by the vector evaluation line.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Each type-$A$ fundamental Kirillov--Reshetikhin module is the image of
the $q$-antisymmetrizer on an ordered tensor power of vector
evaluation modules (\cite[Ch.~12]{ChariPressley94},
\cite[\S2]{Hernandez05}), hence a direct summand. The closure
property follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[On the spectral side, the completed fundamental
packet is forced by the completed vector packet;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-packet}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-fundamental-packet}. Let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\subset
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\]
be the full subcategory generated by finite ordered tensor products of
the vector evaluation objects, and
let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}
\subset
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
be the full subcategory generated by the corresponding completed
spectral tensor packet.
Assume that the exact braided monoidal functor
\[
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
restricts to an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}.
\]
Let
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}
\subset
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
be the full subcategory spanned by the standard type-$A$
$q$-antisymmetric direct summands inside finite ordered tensor powers
of \(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}\), equivalently by the completed
spectral images of the source fundamental evaluation objects. Then
\(J_q^\omega\) restricts to an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund}}_{q}.
\]
Consequently the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-fundamental-packet} are
already satisfied, so \(J_q^\omega\) is an exact braided monoidal
equivalence.

\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:quantum-fd-vector-fundamental-generation}, every
source fundamental evaluation object is a $q$-antisymmetrizer summand
of an ordered tensor power of vector evaluation objects. Since
\(J_q^\omega\) is exact and braided monoidal, it preserves these
summands, giving the equivalence on
\(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{fund,fd}}_{q}\). Now apply
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-fundamental-packet}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[On the spectral side, ordered vector-packet
transport is forced by the completed vector line;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-line}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-packet}. Let
\(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) and
\(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}\) be the full subcategories
spanned by the vector evaluation objects and their completed spectral
images, respectively.
Assume that \(J_q^\omega\)
restricts to an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}.
\]
Then on every object of \(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) the
restriction of \(J_q^\omega\) is forced to be the ordered tensor
product of the corresponding completed vector objects, and on the
braid-group operators of the ordered vector packet it is forced to be
the trigonometric braiding of \(\mathcal{C}_q^\omega\)
(once the completed spectral vector line is fixed,
the transport on the whole ordered vector packet carries no additional freedom).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since \(\mathcal{P}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) consists of finite ordered
tensor products of objects of \(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\),
braided monoidality of \(J_q^\omega\) forces both the object-level and
braiding-level transport.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Standard quantum-loop vector seed and additive
log-spectral shifts; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:quantum-fd-vector-seed-shifts}
Let
\[
V(0)\in \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\]
be the vector evaluation object of the quantum loop algebra at
multiplicative spectral parameter \(1\), viewed on the additive
log-spectral line via the exponential coordinate \(z=e^u\). For every
\(a\in \mathbb{C}\), let
\[
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a\colon
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
\]
be the pullback along the loop-rotation automorphism \(z\mapsto e^a z\)
of the quantum loop algebra. Then each
\(\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a\) is an exact braided-monoidal
autoequivalence, and
\[
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a(V(0))\cong V(a),
\qquad
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_{a+b}\cong
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a\circ \mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_b,
\qquad
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_0\cong \id .
\]

\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Loop rotation \(z\mapsto e^a z\) is a Hopf algebra automorphism of the
quantum loop algebra (\cite[Ch.~12]{ChariPressley94},
\cite[\S2]{Hernandez05}), so pullback defines exact braided-monoidal
autoequivalences. The group law and unit follow from composition.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Quantum-loop vector seed is Schur-simple;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:quantum-fd-vector-seed-schur}
For every \(a\in\mathbb C\), the type-$A$ vector evaluation object
\(V(a)\in \operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}\)
is simple, so \(\End(V(a))\cong \mathbb C\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The vector evaluation object is the first fundamental
Kirillov--Reshetikhin module, hence simple (\cite[Ch.~12]{ChariPressley94}).
Schur's lemma gives \(\End(V(a))\cong\mathbb C\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[On the spectral side, the completed vector line is
forced by one completed vector seed together with spectral shifts;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-seed}
Work in the setting of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-line}. Fix one
source vector evaluation object \(V(0)\in
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) and one completed spectral vector
object \(V^\omega(0)\in \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}\). Assume
further that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item for every \(a\in \mathbb{C}\), the source vector evaluation line
 carries an exact braided-monoidal spectral-shift autoequivalence
 \[
 \mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a\colon
 \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\xrightarrow{\sim}
 \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}
 \]
 with \(\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a(V(0))\cong V(a)\);
\item for every \(a\in \mathbb{C}\), the completed spectral vector line
 carries an exact braided-monoidal spectral-shift autoequivalence
 \[
 \mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a\colon
 \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}\xrightarrow{\sim}
 \mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}
 \]
 with \(\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a(V^\omega(0))\cong V^\omega(a)\); and
\item the exact braided monoidal functor \(J_q^\omega\) intertwines
 these shift autoequivalences on the vector line:
 \[
 J_q^\omega\circ \mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a
 \cong
 \mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a\circ J_q^\omega
 \qquad (a\in \mathbb{C}),
 \]
 and identifies \(V(0)\) with \(V^\omega(0)\).
\end{enumerate}
Then the restriction of \(J_q^\omega\) to
\(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) is uniquely determined up to
unique natural isomorphism by the image of the single seed object
\(V(0)\) together with the compatible spectral-shift structure.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The intertwining relation~\textup{(iii)} forces \(J_q^\omega(V(a))
\cong V^\omega(a)\) for every \(a\), since every object of
\(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\) is obtained from the seed by
the shift autoequivalences~\textup{(i)}--\textup{(ii)}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[On the realized spectral vector-line locus, the
completed vector seed and spectral shifts are canonical;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-seed-shift-construction}
Work in the setting of
Propositions~\ref{prop:quantum-fd-vector-seed-shifts}
and~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-line}. Assume that the exact
braided monoidal functor
\[
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal{C}_q^\omega
\]
restricts to an equivalence
\[
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}.
\]
Define
\[
V^\omega(0):=J_q^\omega(V(0))
\]
and for each \(a\in\mathbb{C}\) define
\[
\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a
:=
\left.J_q^\omega\right|_{\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}}
\circ
\mathsf{T}^{\mathrm{fd}}_a
\circ
\left(\left.J_q^\omega\right|_{\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec,fd}}_{q}}\right)^{-1}.
\]
Then each \(\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a\) is an exact braided-monoidal
autoequivalence of \(\mathcal{L}^{\mathrm{vec}}_{q}\), and
\[
\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a(V^\omega(0))\cong V^\omega(a),
\qquad
\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_{a+b}\cong
\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_a\circ \mathsf{T}^{\omega}_b,
\qquad
\mathsf{T}^{\omega}_0\cong \id .
\]
