\alpha^\omega(c)\,e_1\otimes e_2
+\beta^\omega(c)\,e_2\otimes e_1
\]
and
\[
\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\mathrm{fd}}(e_1\otimes e_2)
=
\alpha^{\mathrm{fd}}(c)\,e_1\otimes e_2
+\beta^{\mathrm{fd}}(c)\,e_2\otimes e_1.
\]
Then the remaining explicit local spectral comparison on the canonical
target is exactly the scalar identity
\[
\beta^\omega(c)=\beta^{\mathrm{fd}}(c)
\qquad (c\in\mathbb C).
\]

Equivalently, on the equivariant multiplicative spectral realization
locus of the canonical target, once the seed and shift data are
canonical and the diagonal symmetry/highest-weight normalization are in
place, the local spectral packet contracts from one ordered
mixed-tensor line family to one scalar exchange coefficient family.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-single-line}
identifies the remaining local spectral comparison on the canonical
target with the mixed-tensor family
\[
\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}(e_1\otimes e_2)
=
\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\mathrm{fd}}(e_1\otimes e_2)
\qquad (c\in\mathbb C).
\]
Now apply
Proposition~\ref{thm:yangian-dk5-spectral-factorization-seed-exchange}
with \(V^{\mathrm{mult}}(0)=V^\omega(0)\) and
\(\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\mathrm{mult}}=\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Canonical formal-moduli Yangian target: the local
spectral packet descends to one multiplicative-ratio scalar family;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-exchange-mult}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-exchange}. Then
\[
\beta^\omega(c+2\pi i)=\beta^\omega(c)
\qquad (c\in\mathbb C),
\]
so the canonical-target exchange coefficient descends uniquely to a
scalar function
\[
\beta_\times^\omega
\]
of the multiplicative spectral ratio with
\[
\beta^\omega(c)=\beta_\times^\omega(e^c).
\]
The remaining explicit local spectral comparison on the canonical
target is therefore exactly
\[
\beta_\times^\omega=\beta_\times^{\mathrm{fd}}.
\]

Equivalently, on the equivariant multiplicative spectral realization
locus of the canonical target, the local spectral packet is one scalar
function on the multiplicative spectral line, not a family on its
additive logarithmic cover.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-spectral-seed},
the canonical target shift family is the ambient dilation pullback
family \(\rho_c^*\), so
\[
V^\omega(c)=\rho_c^*V^\omega(0).
\]
Since \(\rho_{c+2\pi i}=\rho_c\), one has
\[
V^\omega(c+2\pi i)=V^\omega(c)
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathsf B_{0,c+2\pi i}^{\omega}
=
\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}.
\]
Taking the coefficient of \(e_2\otimes e_1\) in the expansion of
\(\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}(e_1\otimes e_2)\) gives the displayed
periodicity of \(\beta^\omega(c)\). The source side already descends
by
Corollary~\ref{thm:yangian-dk5-spectral-factorization-seed-exchange-mult},
so the final identity is just
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-exchange}
rewritten on the multiplicative ratio line.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Canonical formal-moduli Yangian target: the local
spectral packet is the antisymmetric-channel character on the
multiplicative spectral line; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-alt-mult}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-exchange-mult}, and
assume \(M\ge 2\). Then there exists a unique scalar function
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{alt},\times}^{\omega}
\]
of the multiplicative spectral ratio such that
\[
\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}
(e_1\otimes e_2-e_2\otimes e_1)
=
\lambda_{\mathrm{alt},\times}^{\omega}(e^c)
(e_1\otimes e_2-e_2\otimes e_1).
\]
The remaining explicit local spectral comparison on the canonical
target is exactly
\[
\lambda_{\mathrm{alt},\times}^{\omega}
=
\lambda_{\mathrm{alt},\times}^{\mathrm{fd}}.
\]

Equivalently, on the equivariant multiplicative spectral realization
locus of the canonical target, the local spectral packet is one scalar
character on the highest-weight antisymmetric channel over the
multiplicative spectral line.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply
Proposition~\ref{thm:yangian-dk5-spectral-factorization-seed-alt-mult}
with \(V^{\mathrm{mult}}(0)=V^\omega(0)\) and
\(\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\mathrm{mult}}=\mathsf B_{0,c}^{\omega}\). The
hypotheses needed there are exactly those supplied by
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-exchange-mult}.
\end{proof}

%% --- second \iffalse block (closures vi--vii) ---
\iffalse
\begin{corollary}[Canonical formal-moduli Yangian target closes
DK-4/DK-5 from one canonical spectral seed on the equivariant
multiplicative locus; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-plus-one-seed-orig}
Assume the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-spectral-seed}.
Then the standard type-$A$ Yangian DK-4/DK-5 packet closes on the
canonical formal-moduli target.

Equivalently, once the canonical completed enveloping dg algebra
\(U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})\) carries the RTT-adapted
finite-quotient/shared-seed package and the spectral compact core is
realized equivariantly for multiplicative dilations, it is enough to
place the single canonical spectral seed
\[
V^\omega(0):=J_q^\omega(V(0)).
\]
The shift family is then intrinsic, the full spectral vector packet is
forced, and DK-4/DK-5 closes on the canonical target.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-to-spectral-seed}
makes the hypotheses of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-dk5-spectral-one-seed} automatic on the
canonical target. Therefore the completed vector line, ordered vector
packet, completed fundamental packet, ordered tensor-generator packet,
spectral compact core, and ambient spectral category are all formal.
In particular, the vector-line hypothesis of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-plus-vector-line-orig} is
satisfied. Applying that corollary closes DK-4/DK-5.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Canonical formal-moduli Yangian target closes
DK-4/DK-5 from spectral vector-line realization;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:yangian-canonical-realization-plus-vector-line-orig}
Let
\[
\cA=\mathcal{Y}(\mathfrak{sl}_M),
\qquad
\mathfrak{g}_{\cA}:=T_*\mathfrak{F}_{\cA}
\]
be the canonical H-level dg target of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-canonical-hlevel-target}, and let
\[
U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})
\]
be its canonical associative dg model of
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-canonical-envelope}. Assume that the
hypotheses of Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-typea-realization-criterion}
hold for \(U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})\). Assume further
that the spectral compact core admits an exact braided monoidal functor
\[
J_q^\omega\colon
\operatorname{Fact}_{\Eone}^{\mathrm{fd}}(U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_M))^{\mathrm{op}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal C_q^\omega
\]
whose restriction to the vector evaluation line is an equivalence onto
the completed vector spectral line, as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-vector-line}. Then the
standard type-$A$ Yangian DK-4/DK-5 packet closes on the canonical
formal-moduli target.

Equivalently, once the canonical completed enveloping dg algebra
carries the RTT-adapted finite-quotient/shared-seed package, it is
enough to realize the standard vector evaluation line on the spectral
side. The dg compact core and ambient dg category are already formal,
and the spectral compact core, ambient spectral category, compact-core
comparison, and completed comparison then become formal as well. On
the multiplicative spectral factorization locus,
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-factorization-core-from-vector-line}
shows that the spectral compact core is forced as the thick
braided-monoidal closure of that realized vector line.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-typea-realization-criterion} applies to
\(U^{\mathrm{comp}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\cA})\), so the canonical
formal-moduli target already carries the standard type-$A$ dg-shifted
realization and the local DK-4 packet is closed. The additional
vector-line hypothesis is exactly the remaining spectral input of
Corollary~\ref{cor:yangian-typea-realization-plus-dg-packet-orig}, so that
corollary applies and closes DK-4/DK-5 on the canonical target. The
final sentence is the multiplicative factorization refinement supplied
by Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk5-spectral-factorization-core-from-vector-line}.
\end{proof}
\fi
%% --- end of second \iffalse block (closures vi--vii) ---

\begin{remark}[Rational vs.\ trigonometric DK]
\label{rem:rational-trigonometric-dk}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!rational vs trigonometric}
The DK square takes different forms depending on the $R$-matrix type:

\emph{Rational DK}
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian})}.
The Yangian $R$-matrix $R(u) = 1 - \hbar P/u$ is rational
in the additive spectral parameter $u$. Koszul duality sends
$\hbar \to -\hbar$, i.e., $R(u) \to R^{-1}(u)$. The bar
complex uses the propagator $d\log(z_i - z_j)$ on the
FM compactification of $\bC$.

\emph{Trigonometric DK}
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:yangian-quantum-group})}.
The quantum loop algebra $U_q(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}})$ has
trigonometric $R$-matrix $R(u/v)$ in the multiplicative
parameter. Koszul duality sends $q \to q^{-1}$. The bar
complex uses the propagator $d\log(z_i/z_j)$ on the
FM compactification of $\bC^\times$.

The Kazhdan functor $\Phi_K$ intertwines the rational and
trigonometric pictures via the exponential map $u \mapsto e^u$,
$\bC \to \bC^\times$. The DK
square~\eqref{eq:dk-square-yangian} encodes the commutativity
of this intertwining with bar-cobar duality.
\end{remark}

The Yangian chapter reveals the $\Eone$-chiral face of the theory.
The chain-level / evaluation-locus derived Drinfeld--Kohno theorem
(Theorems~\ref{thm:derived-dk-affine}
and~\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian}) proves that bar-cobar duality
\emph{geometrically implements} the quantum group involution
$q \mapsto q^{-1}$, via orientation reversal on ordered
configuration spaces. The $\Einf$-chiral examples of the preceding
chapters all have commutative factorization structure; the Yangian is
the first object whose Koszul duality intertwines genuinely
noncommutative (braided) monoidal data. The theorematic endpoint is
the conditional DK-2/3 extension criterion for finite-dimensional
type~$A$ (Theorem~\ref{conj:dk-fd-typeA}), which reduces the extension
of the evaluation-locus factorization comparison
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:factorization-dk-eval}\textup{)} to thick
generation plus the ambient extension/comparison package.
The MC4 structural framework underlying DK-4 is proved (Theorem~\ref{thm:completed-bar-cobar-strong}; the algebraic identification remains open, Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk4-formal-moduli}), and with only the all-types CG/core
level of MC3 proved while the remaining completion packet stays
open, DK-5 is reduced to that post-core extension problem for
Yangian towers. The remaining open problem is the extension to
the full category~$\mathcal{O}$ (beyond the evaluation-generated core).
The full DK-5 triple-bridge comparison is the natural
$\Eone$-chiral bridge to the modular Koszul package
\ifannalsedition\else
(\S\ref{sec:modular-koszul-programme})
\fi.

%% ================================================================
%% § The modular dg-shifted Yangian
%% ================================================================
\subsection{The modular dg-shifted Yangian}
\label{sec:modular-dg-shifted-yangian}
\index{Yangian!modular dg-shifted|textbf}

The dg-shifted Yangian of
Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25}
is a genus-zero, local object: it packages line-operator OPE on
$\bC$ into a dg algebra with translation operator and
Maurer--Cartan kernel~$r(z)$. The modular extension promoted
here is intended to organize both the line-operator OPE and the
stable-curve gluing data in a single algebraic envelope.

The proposed modular $R$-matrix $R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)$, if the
Maurer--Cartan element of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter} exists, is intended to be
the ordered $\Eone$-factorization specialization of the universal MC
element~$\Theta_\cA$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}). On that
conjectural surface, the shadow obstruction projections would admit the
 following representation-theoretic reading: the scalar level
 $\kappa$ governs the genus-$1$ scalar trace unconditionally and, on
 the proved uniform-weight scalar lane, the full genus tower via the
 $\hat{A}$-genus; the cubic
 shadow~$C$ controls the genus-zero $r$-matrix package, and quartic or
higher shadows govern the quantum corrections such as
$\hbar^2 r_{T,1}(z)$. The benchmark and conditional computations in
this section are organized as projections in the pronilpotent
completion of the convolution algebra $\gAmod$
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-convolution-dg-lie}).

\providecommand{\ModEnv}{\operatorname{ModEnv}}
\providecommand{\Ymod}{Y^{\mathrm{mod}}}

\begin{definition}[Modular dg-shifted Yangian as pro-MC object;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{def:modular-yangian-pro}
\label{def:modular-yangian}
\index{Yangian!modular dg-shifted!definition}
\index{Yangian!modular dg-shifted!pro-MC object}
Let $T$ be a holomorphic-topological theory with boundary
condition~$B$ and Koszul dual~$\cA_T^!$. The
\emph{modular convolution algebra} is the dg~Lie algebra
(the strict model $\Convstr$ of $\Convinf$; Convention~\ref{rem:two-level-convention})
\[
 \mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}
 \;:=\;
 \prod_{2g-2+n>0}
 \Hom\bigl(
 C_\bullet(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n+1})
 \otimes (\cA_T^!)^{\widehat{\otimes}\,n},\;
 \cA_T^!
 \bigr)[1]
\]
equipped with the following structure.

\medskip\noindent\textbf{Differential.}\;
The differential $d = d_{\mathrm{int}} + d_{\mathrm{mod}}$
has two summands:
\begin{itemize}
\item $d_{\mathrm{int}}(\phi)$ is the internal $A_\infty$
 differential on~$\cA_T^!$, acting on inputs and output of~$\phi$;
\item $d_{\mathrm{mod}}(\phi)$ is the boundary operator
 dual to the stable-curve boundary
 $\partial \colon \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n+1}
 \to \coprod_{g_1+g_2=g,\,S_1 \sqcup S_2}
 \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g_1,|S_1|+1}
 \times \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g_2,|S_2|+1}$
 (and the non-separating boundary), acting by precomposition
 on the chain argument of~$\phi$.
\end{itemize}

\noindent\textbf{Lie bracket.}\;
For $\phi \in \mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}$ of type~$(g_1,n)$
and $\psi$ of type~$(g_2,m)$, the bracket
$[\phi,\psi]$ lives in type~$(g_1+g_2,\,n+m-1)$ and is
\[
 [\phi,\psi](\gamma;\, a_1,\ldots,a_{n+m-1})
 \;=\;
 \sum_{\substack{I \sqcup J = \{1,\ldots,n+m-1\}\\
 |I|=n-1,\; |J|=m}}
 \pm\;\phi\bigl(\gamma_I;\, a_I,\,
 \psi(\gamma_J;\, a_J)\bigr),
\]
where $\gamma_I,\gamma_J$ are the chain factors induced by
stable-graph composition and the sign is the Koszul sign
from the graded-symmetric interchange. The internal edge
connecting one output of~$\psi$ to one input of~$\phi$
carries the propagator~$r_T(z)$.

\noindent\textbf{Filtration and pronilpotent completion.}\;
Define
\[
 F^N \mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}
 \;:=\;
 \prod_{2g-2+n \ge N}
 \Hom\bigl(
 C_\bullet(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n+1})
 \otimes (\cA_T^!)^{\widehat{\otimes}\,n},\;
 \cA_T^!
 \bigr)[1].
\]
Since the bracket maps
$F^{N_1} \times F^{N_2} \to F^{N_1+N_2}$,
this is a Lie filtration and the separated completion
\[
 \Ymod_T
 \;:=\;
 \widehat{\mathcal{L}}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}
 \;:=\;
 \varprojlim_N\;
 \mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}} \big/ F^{N+1}
\]
is a pronilpotent dg Lie algebra. Since the original
$\mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}$ is already a product over
$(g,n)$-components (each finite-dimensional in the
genus-graded sense), the completion map is an isomorphism:
$\widehat{\mathcal{L}}_T^{\mathrm{mod}} \cong
\mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}$.
On the conjectural surface where the modular line-operator package
admits the intended compatible algebra structure, that structure is
encoded by a Maurer--Cartan element
\[
 R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)
 \;=\;
 \sum_{g \ge 0} \hbar^{2g}\, r_{T,g}(z)
 \;\in\;
 \operatorname{MC}(\Ymod_T),
\]
and the stable-graph Yang--Baxter equation is then the
corresponding Maurer--Cartan equation in~$\Ymod_T$.

The usual dg-shifted Yangian
$\Ydg_{\cA}$
(Definition~\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian})
is recovered only at the genus-zero sector of this package: the
coefficient $r_{T,0}(z)=r_T(z)$ and the associated genus-zero
operations reproduce the dg-shifted Yangian data.
The definition constructs the ambient pro-dg~Lie algebra;
\emph{populating} it with an MC~element
$R_T^{\mathrm{mod}} \in \MC(\Ymod_T)$ is the content of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter}.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Modular $R$-matrix as conjectural MC restriction]
\label{rem:modular-yangian-chriss-ginzburg}
On that conjectural surface, the genus-zero sector of the pro-MC
package reduces to the dg-shifted Yangian of
Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25}. The modular
completion is a single algebraic structure (a pronilpotent
dg~Lie algebra), not a collection of data. On the conjectural
surface where Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter} is solved,
the resulting algebra structure is encoded by a Maurer--Cartan
element.

More precisely, the intended kernel
$R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)$ is intended to be the ordered
$\Eone$-factorization restriction of the universal MC
element~$\Theta_\cA$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}. On that
conjectural surface, the
shadow obstruction decomposition
(Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow-extraction}) reads as follows in the
Yangian setting:
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Degree 2} (scalar level $\kappa$): the genus tower
 is governed unconditionally at genus~$1$ by the scalar trace
 $\kappa \cdot \lambda_1$; on the proved uniform-weight scalar lane
 this further specializes to the full $\hat{A}$-genus generating
 function \ifannalsedition\else
(Chapter~\ref{ch:genus-expansions})
\fi;
\item \textbf{Degree 3} (cubic shadow $C$): the classical
 $r$-matrix $r_{T,0}(z)$ and the classical Yang--Baxter equation
 $[r_{12}, r_{13}] + [r_{12}, r_{23}] + [r_{13}, r_{23}] = 0$;
\item \textbf{Degree $\geq 4$} (quartic and higher): the quantum
 corrections $r_{T,g}$ for $g \geq 1$ and the stable-graph
 Yang--Baxter equation~\eqref{eq:stable-graph-yb}.
\end{itemize}
The Yangian shadow obstruction tower is \emph{infinite} (the $\mathcal{W}_N$-type
archetype, not the Gaussian or contact archetype) because the quantum
corrections do not terminate at any finite degree.

At the full homotopy level, $\mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}$ carries
a \emph{quantum $L_\infty$-structure}
(Theorem~\ref{thm:modular-quantum-linfty}): operations
$\{\ell_n^{(g)}\}$ where $\ell_2^{(0)}$ is the dg~bracket above,
$\ell_n^{(0)}$ for $n \geq 3$ are the higher operadic brackets from
homotopy transfer through
$C_*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{0,n+1})$, and $\ell_n^{(g)}$ for
$g \geq 1$ are the higher-genus Feynman amplitudes. If the modular
kernel of Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter} exists, then it is
an MC~element for the full quantum $L_\infty$-structure, and the
stable-graph Yang--Baxter
equation~\eqref{eq:stable-graph-yb} is the leading-order truncation
of this quantum MC~equation.
\end{remark}

\begin{conjecture}[Modular Yang--Baxter package;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:modular-yang-baxter}
\index{Yang--Baxter!modular stable-graph refinement}
For every holomorphic-topological theory~$T$ with Koszul-dual
boundary condition~$B$, there exists a Maurer--Cartan element
$R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar) \in \operatorname{MC}(\Ymod_T)$
(Definition~\ref{def:modular-yangian-pro}) whose genus-refined
components $r_{T,g}(z)$ satisfy the \emph{stable-graph
Yang--Baxter equation}: for each $g \ge 0$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:stable-graph-yb}
 d_{\mathrm{mod}}\, r_{T,g}(z)
 \;+\;
 \sum_{g_1+g_2=g}
 \bigl[r_{T,g_1}(z),\, r_{T,g_2}(z)\bigr]_{\mathrm{graph}}
 \;+\;
 \Delta\bigl(r_{T,g-1}(z)\bigr)
 \;=\; 0,
\end{equation}
where $[\cdot,\cdot]_{\mathrm{graph}}$ is the Lie bracket in
$\mathcal{L}_T^{\mathrm{mod}}$ (graph composition with the
propagator on the internal edge), $\Delta$ is the genus-loop
operator from non-separating degeneration of
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ (contracting a single handle),
and $r_{T,-1} := 0$ by convention. The initial condition is
$r_{T,0}(z) = r_T(z)$, the genus-zero kernel.

At genus zero the
terms with $\Delta$ and $g_1,g_2 > 0$ vanish, and
\eqref{eq:stable-graph-yb} reduces to
$d_{\mathrm{mod}}\,r_{T,0} + [r_{T,0},r_{T,0}]_{\mathrm{graph}} = 0$,
which is the $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter equation
of~\cite{DNP25}.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Relation to the DK ladder]
\label{rem:modular-yangian-dk}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!modular Yangian}
The modular dg-shifted Yangian $\Ymod_T$ should be the natural
target of a DK-5 level comparison
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw}): the bridge from the
$\Eone$-chiral factorization category to the modular Koszul
package. Its existence first requires extending beyond the evaluation-generated
core to the full Ran space, since the
stable-graph completion requires control of the factorization
category on the full module category, not merely on the evaluation
locus for finite-dimensional modules. MC3 is proved for all simple
types on the evaluation-generated core
\textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:mc3-all-types}\textup{)}; the residual
problem is the DK-4/5 extension/completion packet
\textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk-compacts-completion}\textup{)},
which extends beyond evaluation modules into the full category.
Once that packet is supplied, Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw}
isolates the remaining DK-5 bridge step as the
exponential/PBW comparison. The genus-refined Maurer--Cartan
equation of Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter} is a
single organizing principle for both the genus-zero DK square
(Remark~\ref{rem:dk-square-geometry}) and the higher-genus
complementarity data of Theorem~C.
\end{remark}

% ==========================================
% MODULAR YANG-BAXTER PACKAGE AND HOLOGRAPHIC LINE OPERATORS
% ==========================================

\subsection{The modular Yang--Baxter package and holographic line operators}
\label{subsec:modular-yb-holographic}
\index{Yang--Baxter!modular package}
\index{line operators!holographic completion}

The modular dg-shifted Yangian $\Ymod_T$ of
Definition~\ref{def:modular-yangian-pro} is the ambient
pronilpotent dg Lie algebra intended to organize
stable-curve gluing \emph{and} spectral line-operator data in a
single algebraic package. The ambient ingredients together with the
conjectural kernel data are as follows; this
package is strictly richer than a modular envelope.

\subsubsection{The modular $r$-matrix expansion}

\begin{definition}[Modular total kernel]
\label{def:modular-total-kernel}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!modular total kernel}
A \emph{modular total kernel} is a formal $\hbar$-completed $r$-matrix
\begin{equation}\label{eq:modular-total-kernel}
 R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)
 \;:=\;
 \sum_{g \ge 0} \hbar^{2g}\, r_{T,g}(z),
 \qquad
 r_{T,0}(z) = r_T(z),
\end{equation}
where each genus-$g$ coefficient lives in
\begin{equation}\label{eq:r-coeff-space}
 r_{T,g}(z)
 \;\in\;
 H^\bullet\bigl(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,2}\bigr)
 \otimes
 \cA_T^! \,\widehat{\otimes}\,
 \cA_T^!\bigl(\!(z^{-1})\!\bigr).
\end{equation}
By Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter}, such a total kernel
$R_T^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)$ is a Maurer--Cartan element in a
pronilpotent dg Lie algebra built from the boundary stratification
of $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$. The Maurer--Cartan condition
encodes both the genus-zero $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter equation and
its all-genera stable-graph refinement.
\end{definition}

\subsubsection{An algebraic line-operator model}

\begin{definition}[Algebraic line-operator model]
\label{def:line-operator-category-yb}
\index{line operators!category $\mathcal{C}_T$}
For the purposes of this subsection, define the
\emph{algebraic line-operator model} associated to the theory~$T$ by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:line-cat}
 \mathcal{C}_T
 \;:=\;
 \cA_T^!\text{-}\mathrm{mod},
\end{equation}
the dg category of modules for the Koszul dual algebra. When a
compatible spectral kernel $r_T(z)$ is supplied, this algebraic model
acquires the corresponding $z$-dependent comultiplication:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:twisted-coproduct}
 \Delta_z \colon
 \cA_T^!
 \;\longrightarrow\;
 \cA_T^! \,\widehat{\otimes}_{r_T(z)}\,
 \cA_T^!\bigl(\!(z^{-1})\!\bigr).
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{conjecture}[Consistency via $D^2 = 0$; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:ainfty-yb-consistency}%
\index{Yang--Baxter!A-infinity consistency@$A_\infty$ consistency}
The $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter equation for the spectral kernel $r(z)$
is equivalent to the condition $D^2 = 0$ on the $d_r$-twisted
modular bar complex of $\cA_T$. This is the algebraic
condition that upgrades ``modular gluing'' (stable-curve composition
in the Feynman transform) to the corresponding \emph{algebraic
spectral defect model} incorporating line-operator OPE data.
\end{conjecture}

\subsubsection{Beyond the modular envelope}

\begin{remark}[What the modular envelope does not see]
\label{rem:beyond-modular-envelope}
\index{modular envelope!limitations}
A modular envelope remembers the composition of operations along stable
curves (the Feynman transform of the modular operad
$\{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}\}$) but it does \emph{not} encode:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the \emph{Maurer--Cartan moduli problem}, parametrizing
 consistent couplings of the theory to background fields and defects;
\item the \emph{bulk-boundary map}
 $\cA_{\mathrm{bulk}} \simeq Z_{\mathrm{der}}(\cA_\partial)$
 to the derived center;
\item the \emph{Poisson bracket and higher stress tensor}, the
 shifted-symplectic geometry of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:ambient-complementarity-fmp};
\item the \emph{algebraic line-operator model}
 $\mathcal{C}_T := \cA_T^!\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$ and, when equipped
 with a compatible spectral kernel, its spectral tensor
 structure;
\item the \emph{spectral $r(z)$-matrix} and the $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter
 equation that governs it.
\end{enumerate}
The dg-shifted Yangian package $\Ymod_T$ provides the ambient
algebraic home for this additional structure. Its genus-zero
sector recovers the dg-shifted Yangian data of
Definition~\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}; once the conjectural
kernel data of Conjecture~\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter} are
supplied, the full modular completion becomes the algebraic home for
all-genera defect OPE coefficients and holographic line-operator
amplitudes.
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% § Restricted DK-5 and DS on primitive triples
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{DK-5: modular Yangian-shadow equivalence}

\begin{conjecture}[DK-5: modular Yangian-shadow equivalence;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:dk5-restricted}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!modular Yangian-shadow equivalence}
\index{Yangian!modular dg-shifted!DK-5 equivalence}
Let~$\cA$ be a modular Koszul algebra with
multiplicity-free $\ell$-weight spectrum
\textup{(}in the sense of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}}\textup{)}.
The following data are equivalent:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The modular dg-shifted Yangian $R$-matrix
 $R_\cA^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar)
 \in \operatorname{MC}(\Ymod_\cA)$
 \textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-yangian-pro}},
 Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:modular-yang-baxter}}\textup{)}.
\item The universal MC element
 $\Theta_\cA \in \operatorname{MC}(\fg_\cA^{\mathrm{mod}})$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}}\textup{)}.
\item The shadow obstruction tower
 $\{\Theta_\cA^{\leq r}\}_{r \geq 2}$
 together with its clutching laws
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:recursive-existence}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
The equivalence
\textup{(i)}\,$\Leftrightarrow$\,\textup{(ii)}
is mediated by collision-residue extraction:
at degree~$2$, $r_\cA(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:r-matrix-koszul-dual-inverse}}\textup{)},
extended to all degrees by the planted-forest expansion.
At genus~$g$, the coefficient
$r_{\cA,g}(z) \in H^\bullet(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,2})
\otimes \cA^! \,\widehat{\otimes}\, \cA^!(\!(z^{-1})\!)$
is the genus-$g$ binary projection of~$\Theta_\cA$.
The equivalence
\textup{(ii)}\,$\Leftrightarrow$\,\textup{(iii)}
is the inverse limit
$\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim \Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Proved and open components of DK-5]
\label{rem:dk5-restricted-status}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK-5!status of components}
The three data of Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-restricted} exist
individually:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $\Theta_\cA$ exists unconditionally
 \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}:
 $\Theta_\cA := D_\cA - d_0$ is MC because
 $D_\cA^2 = 0$\textup{)}.
\item The inverse limit
 $\Theta_\cA = \varprojlim \Theta_\cA^{\leq r}$ exists
 \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:recursive-existence}\textup{)},
 so~\textup{(ii)}\,$\Leftrightarrow$\,\textup{(iii)} is proved.
\item The collision-residue extraction
 $r_\cA(z)
 = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
 at genus~$0$, degree~$2$ is proved
 \textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:r-matrix-koszul-dual-inverse}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
What is \emph{open} is the full modular bridge: confirming that
the genus-$g$ coefficients $r_{\cA,g}(z)$ of the modular total
kernel
\textup{(}Definition~\ref{def:modular-total-kernel}\textup{)}
satisfy the stable-graph Yang--Baxter
equation~\eqref{eq:stable-graph-yb} and that this MC element,
together with the ambient pronilpotent dg~Lie
algebra~$\Ymod_\cA$, determines~$\Theta_\cA$
uniquely. That is, the conjectural content is
the reconstruction of the full MC element from the ordered
$\Eone$-factorization data: one must show that
the planted-forest expansion of all-degree, all-genera
collision residues
$\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{g,k}(\Theta_\cA)$
assembles into a Maurer--Cartan element of~$\Ymod_\cA$
that recovers~$\Theta_\cA$.

The multiplicity-free $\ell$-weight hypothesis enters through
Theorem~\ref{thm:categorical-cg-all-types}: it ensures
that the categorical Clebsch--Gordan closure holds at all
simple types, so the factorization category on the
evaluation-generated core is under control. Without this
hypothesis, the DK-5 equivalence is not expected to hold,
since the modular Yangian~$\Ymod_\cA$ may fail to capture
the full modular factorization data.

The relationship to the existing DK-5 conjectures is as
follows. Conjecture~\ref{conj:dk5-infty-pbw} addresses the
$\infty$-categorical PBW passage from the tangent Lie
algebra~$\fg_\cA$ to the formal group~$G_\cA$. The present
conjecture is logically independent: it concerns the
\emph{modular} extension of the Yangian package, not the
exponential passage at genus~$0$.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection{DS reduction on primitive triples}

\begin{proposition}[DS reduction on primitive triples;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:ds-functor-primitive-triple}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!primitive triples}
\index{primitive triple!DS functor}
\index{Koszul duality!primitive triple!DS reduction}
Let $\fg$ be a simple Lie algebra at non-critical level
$k \neq -h^\vee$, with Feigin--Frenkel dual level
$k' = -k - 2h^\vee$. Denote by $\widehat{\fg}_k$ the
affine vertex algebra with its Koszul pair
$(\widehat{\fg}_k, \widehat{\fg}_{k'})$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:universal-kac-moody-koszul}}\textup{)}.
The Koszul dual $\widehat{\fg}_{k'}$
carries a \emph{primitive triple}
\[
 \bigl(\widehat{\fg}_{k'}^{\phantom{!}},\;
 \Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}},\;
 r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z)\bigr),
\]
where $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}}$ is the $z$-dependent coproduct
on~$\widehat{\fg}_{k'}$
\textup{(}the ordered factorization structure on the Koszul dual\textup{)}
and $r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z) = k'\Omega/z$ is the collision $r$-matrix
\textup{(}$\Omega = \sum_a I^a \otimes I_a \in \fg \otimes \fg$
the quadratic Casimir tensor in the Killing-form
normalization\textup{)}.

Principal Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction defines a functor on
primitive triples:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ds-functor-primitive-triple}
 \mathrm{DS}_{\mathrm{prin}} \colon
 \bigl(\widehat{\fg}_{k'},\;
 \Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}},\;
 r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z)\bigr)
 \;\longmapsto\;
 \bigl(\mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg),\;
 \Delta_z^{\mathcal{W}},\;
 r^{\mathcal{W}}(z)\bigr),
\end{equation}
where the transferred data are obtained as follows.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Algebra.}
 $\mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg)
 = H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}(\widehat{\fg}_{k'})$
 is the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra at the dual level,
 which is the Koszul dual of
 $\mathcal{W}^k(\fg)$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ds-koszul-intertwine}}\textup{)}.
\item \emph{Coproduct.}
 $\Delta_z^{\mathcal{W}}$ is obtained by applying
 $H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}$ to the coproduct
 $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}}$ on~$\widehat{\fg}_{k'}$.
 The BRST differential
 $Q_{\mathrm{DS}}$ is a coderivation of the coalgebra
 structure
 \textup{(}it is a derivation of the vertex algebra, hence
 a coderivation of the dual coalgebra\textup{)},
 so $H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}$ preserves the coproduct.
 The resulting $\Delta_z^{\mathcal{W}}$ equips
 $\mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg)$ with the ordered
 factorization structure of a line operator on
 $\bC \times \bR$, encoding the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra
 fusion at separated spectral parameters.
\item \emph{$r$-matrix.}
 $r^{\mathcal{W}}(z)$ is the collision-residue extraction
 on the DS-reduced bar complex:
 $r^{\mathcal{W}}(z) =
 \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_{\mathcal{W}^k})$,
 where $\Theta_{\mathcal{W}^k}$ is the bar-intrinsic
 MC element of~$\mathcal{W}^k(\fg)$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic}}\textup{)}.
 By DS--bar commutation
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ds-koszul-intertwine}},
 eq.~\eqref{eq:ds-bar-commute}\textup{)},
 this equals the DS reduction of the affine $r$-matrix:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:ds-r-transfer}
 r^{\mathcal{W}}(z)
 \;=\;
 \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}
 \bigl(
 H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}(\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}_k})
 \bigr).
 \end{equation}
 The transferred $r$-matrix has poles at $z^{-1}, z^{-3},
 \ldots, z^{-(2h_W-1)}$, where $h_W$ is the highest
 conformal weight among the $\mathcal{W}$-algebra generators,
 reflecting the higher-order OPE poles of the
 $\mathcal{W}$-algebra shifted by the
 $d\log$ pole absorption
 \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:three-r-matrices}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1: DS on the Koszul dual.}
The Koszul dual of $\widehat{\fg}_k$ is $\widehat{\fg}_{k'}$
by Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-kac-moody-koszul}, and the
Koszul dual of $\mathcal{W}^k(\fg)$ is
$\mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg)$ by the DS--Koszul intertwining
theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-koszul-intertwine}). Part~(i)
is therefore the definition of principal DS reduction applied
to the dual level.

\emph{Step~2: Coproduct transfer.}
The factorization coproduct
$\Delta_z^{\mathrm{KM}} \colon
\widehat{\fg}_{k'} \to
\widehat{\fg}_{k'} \,\widehat{\otimes}\,
\widehat{\fg}_{k'}(\!(z^{-1})\!)$
encodes the OPE of two $\widehat{\fg}_{k'}$-insertions at
separated spectral parameters. The BRST charge
$Q_{\mathrm{DS}}$ acts fiberwise at each insertion and
commutes with the bar differential
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-koszul-intertwine}, Step~1 of that proof).
In particular, $Q_{\mathrm{DS}}$ commutes with the coproduct:
$\Delta_z \circ Q_{\mathrm{DS}}
= (Q_{\mathrm{DS}} \otimes \mathrm{id}
+ \mathrm{id} \otimes Q_{\mathrm{DS}}) \circ \Delta_z$,
since $Q_{\mathrm{DS}}$ is a derivation of the vertex
algebra structure. Passing to $H^0$ yields the transferred
coproduct on $\mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg)$.

\emph{Step~3: $r$-matrix transfer.}
By DS--bar commutation~\eqref{eq:ds-bar-commute},
\[
 \bar{B}(\mathcal{W}^k(\fg))
 \;\simeq\;
 H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}\bigl(\bar{B}(\widehat{\fg}_k)\bigr).
\]
The MC element $\Theta_{\mathcal{W}^k}
= D_{\mathcal{W}^k} - d_0$ of the $\mathcal{W}$-bar complex
therefore arises from
$H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}(\Theta_{\widehat{\fg}_k})$.
Applying collision-residue extraction
$\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}$ to both sides
yields~\eqref{eq:ds-r-transfer}.

The pole orders of $r^{\mathcal{W}}(z)$ follow from
the OPE structure of $\mathcal{W}^k(\fg)$: the
$\mathcal{W}$-algebra has generators of conformal weights
$m_1 + 1, \ldots, m_r + 1$ (where $m_i$ are the exponents
of~$\fg$), giving OPE poles up to order $2h_W$ for the
highest-weight generator. The $d\log$ pole absorption
(cf.\ the bar complex propagator $d\log(z_i - z_j)$,
Remark~\ref{rem:three-r-matrices}) shifts each pole
order by $-1$, producing $r$-matrix poles at
$z^{-1}, z^{-3}, \ldots, z^{-(2h_W - 1)}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope and limitations]
\label{rem:ds-triple-scope}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!primitive triples!scope}
Proposition~\ref{prop:ds-functor-primitive-triple} is restricted
to \emph{principal} DS reduction. For non-principal nilpotent
$f$, the three components of the triple transfer with different
levels of difficulty:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The algebra transfer
 $\widehat{\fg}_{k'} \mapsto \mathcal{W}^{k'}(\fg, f)$
 is unconditional
 \textup{(}Kac--Roan--Wakimoto~\cite{KRW}\textup{)}.
\item The coproduct transfer requires the abelianity of
 $\mathfrak{n}_+$ in the Dynkin grading (or, more generally,
 the filtration formality of the BRST complex;
 Proposition~\ref{prop:ds-bar-formality}). This holds for
 principal, subregular, and hook-type nilpotents in type~$A$,
 but fails in general.
\item The $r$-matrix transfer requires DS--bar commutation
 \textup{(}Conjecture~\ref{conj:ds-kd-arbitrary-nilpotent}\textup{)},
 which is proved for principal nilpotents and conjectural in
 general.
\end{enumerate}
The extension of the primitive-triple functor to arbitrary
nilpotents is therefore conditional on the DS--bar commutation
conjecture. In the hook-type corridor
\textup{(}Theorem~\ref{thm:hook-transport-corridor}\textup{)},
the coproduct and $r$-matrix transfers are accessible via
the transport propagation mechanism.

The primitive triple $(\cA^!, \Delta_z, r(z))$ of the
Koszul dual records the factorization coproduct and
collision $r$-matrix on one side of the duality. The
\emph{modular Koszul triple}
$(\cA, \cA^!, r(z))$
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-koszul-triple}}\textup{)}
records both sides of the Koszul pair together with the
$r$-matrix; Construction~\textup{\ref{constr:ds-functor-triples}}
proves that DS acts functorially on this larger datum.
The chain-level realization is the DS-HPL transfer theorem
(Volume~II, Theorem~thm:ds-hpl-transfer): homological
perturbation through the BRST SDR transfers the full
dg-shifted Yangian data $(m, r, \Delta)$ to the
$\mathcal{W}$-algebra side. The transferred $r$-matrix
acquires higher-order poles from the Sugawara nonlinearity,
while the coproduct is annihilated by a ghost-number
obstruction (Principle~\ref{princ:gravitational-primitivity}).
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% § Boundary/line realization of the DK bridge
%% ================================================================
\subsection{Boundary/line realization of the DK bridge}
\label{subsec:boundary-line-dk-bridge}
\index{Bridge Theorem!boundary/line realization|textbf}
\index{boundary chiral algebra!DK bridge}
\index{line operators!DK bridge realization}

The holomorphic-topological literature
(Costello--Dimofte--Gaiotto~\cite{CDG2023},
Dimofte--Niu--Py~\cite{DNP25},
Khan--Zeng~\cite{KZ2025})
provides a potentially independent engine for the Bridge Theorem.
Instead of attacking the category-$\mathcal{O}$ extension (B1)
directly through internal Koszulity arguments, the boundary/line
path organizes the missing comparison data around a rich
holomorphic boundary condition together with the associated
derived-center and boundary spectral inputs.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{CG perspective.}
A holomorphic boundary condition~$b$ induces a
\emph{restriction morphism of convolution algebras}
\[
\rho_b \colon
\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(\cA),\cA^!)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(V_b), V_b)
\]
from the bulk to the boundary.
The functor $F_b \colon \mathcal{C}_T \to V_b\text{-mod}$
is the corresponding boundary-side functorial datum on the module
surface,
and the derived-center condition
$\beta_{\mathrm{der}} \colon V \xrightarrow{\sim}
Z(V_b)_{\mathrm{der}}$
expresses recovery of the bulk algebra from the boundary algebra on the
derived-center side.
The boundary/line bridge criterion
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:boundary-line-bridge} below) is thus a
\emph{CG reduction} on the bulk-to-boundary deformation side: prove
that the convolution-algebra morphism $\rho_b$ gives the required
deformation-theoretic comparison, and then separately identify the
boundary $R$-matrix with Latyntsev's spectral factorization data.
This subsection integrates that two-part approach into the
monograph's proof plan.

\begin{definition}[Boundary/line bridge data]
\label{def:boundary-line-bridge-data}
\index{boundary/line bridge data|textbf}
Let $T$ be a holomorphic-topological theory with bulk chiral
algebra~$V$, boundary chiral algebra~$V_b$ associated to a boundary
condition~$b$, and algebraic line-operator model
$\mathcal{C}_T := \cA_T^!\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$
(Definition~\ref{def:line-operator-category-yb}).
The \emph{boundary/line bridge data} for~$T$ consists of:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item the \emph{line-boundary functor}
 $F_b \colon \mathcal{C}_T \to V_b\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$
 comparing the algebraic line-operator model to boundary modules;
\item the \emph{bulk-boundary map}
 $\beta_{\mathrm{der}} \colon V \to Z(V_b)_{\mathrm{der}}$
 from the bulk algebra to the derived center of the boundary
 algebra; and
\item the \emph{boundary $R$-matrix}
 $R_b(z) \in \operatorname{End}(V_b \otimes V_b)(z^{-1})$
 encoding the OPE/fusion on $V_b$-mod.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{conjecture}[Boundary/line bridge criterion;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:boundary-line-bridge}
\index{Bridge Theorem!boundary/line criterion}
For a holomorphic-topological theory~$T$ of Yangian type, there
exists a rich boundary condition~$b$ such that:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item $F_b \colon \mathcal{C}_T \xrightarrow{\sim}
 V_b\text{-}\mathrm{mod}$ is an equivalence;
\item $\beta_{\mathrm{der}} \colon V \xrightarrow{\sim}
 Z(V_b)_{\mathrm{der}}$ is an isomorphism; and
\item the boundary $R$-matrix $R_b(z)$ is a spectral
 $R$-matrix in the sense of Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23}.
\end{enumerate}
Under these conditions, the resulting boundary/line package supplies
the boundary-side comparison data for~B4; once B2 furnishes the
completed dg-side category, and together with~B1, the full Bridge Theorem
\textup{(}Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge}}\textup{)}
holds.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Benchmark status for boundary/line bridge]
\label{rem:boundary-line-benchmark}
\index{Bridge Theorem!benchmark status}
The benchmark ladder
(Remark~\ref{rem:bridge-theorem-programme}) has the following
boundary/line status:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Free/$\beta\gamma$/Heisenberg.}
 The Koszul dual is abelian, the line-side algebraic model is free
 modules,
 $F_b$ is tautological, and
 $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$ is the rank-$1$ propagator kernel.
 Calibration only.
\item \emph{Affine $\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$.}
 First non-abelian prototype. The DS/Wakimoto and critical-center
 packages suggest a W-algebra boundary algebra and provide bulk-side
 center data at critical level, but neither a theorematic boundary
 functor~$F_b$ nor a full derived-center reconstruction statement is
 proved here.
\item \emph{$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$.}
 First noncommutative benchmark. The local test is whether the
 degree-$2$ shadow of the dg-shifted Yangian recovers the expected
 rational $R$-matrix, and whether the boundary $R$-matrix $R_b(z)$
 matches that benchmark.
\item \emph{$Y(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$.}
 Higher-rank coherence test: the boundary $R$-matrix should satisfy
 the Yang--Baxter equation with the correct spectral parameter.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% § Completion lemmas for Yangian towers
%% ================================================================
\subsection{Completion lemmas for Yangian towers}
\label{subsec:completion-lemmas}
\index{Yangian!tower completion lemmas|textbf}
\index{Bridge Theorem!completion lemmas}

This subsection isolates the four completion checks required for
sub-target~B2 of the Bridge Theorem package
(Remark~\ref{rem:bridge-theorem-programme}), following the
decomposition of Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-mc4-checklist}.

\smallskip\noindent
\textbf{CG perspective.}
The finite RTT stages $Y_{\le N}$ each carry a proved MC element
$\tau_N \in \MC(\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(Y_{\le N}), Y_{\le N}^!))$.
The four completion checks are conditions for the pronilpotent
MC tower $\{\tau_N\}_N$ to converge in the completed convolution
algebra $\widehat{\operatorname{Conv}}(\bar B(Y), Y^!)$, producing a limit
MC element~$\widehat\tau$ whose associated realized dg-side category is
$\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_\cA)$.

\begin{remark}[The four completion checks]
\label{rem:completion-four-checks}
\index{Yangian!tower completion!four checks}
For a Yangian tower $Y = \varprojlim_N Y_{\le N}$ assembled from
finite RTT stages, the passage from formal target data to an
actual stable $\infty$-category requires:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{cllc}
\textbf{Check} & \textbf{Content} & \textbf{Reference} & \textbf{Status} \\
\hline
(1) & Finite RTT stages in proved $\Eone$-Koszul regime
 & Prop.~\ref{prop:yangian-tower-mc4-criterion}(i)
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
(2) & Compatible descent of finite-stage bar/cobar
 & Prop.~\ref{prop:yangian-tower-mc4-criterion}(ii)
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
(3) & Mittag--Leffler on $\{H^m(\bar B(Y_{\le N}))\}_N$
 & Cor.~\ref{cor:yangian-weight-cutoff}
 & \textbf{Proved} \\
(4) & H-level comparison with an RTT-adapted dg model
 & Cor.~\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion};
 Prop.~\ref{prop:yangian-rtt-completion-identification}
 & Open \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Items~(1)--(3) are theorematic for the standard RTT tower.
Item~(4) is the genuine hard residue: constructing an RTT-adapted
filtered dg model whose finite quotients match the proved stages and
whose completed comparison data matches the standard RTT tower. On the
standard type-$A$ frontier,
Proposition~\ref{prop:yangian-dk4-typea-frontier} reduces the live
local coefficient packet inside~(4) to one mixed-tensor residue check.

\medskip\noindent
\emph{On the theorematic standard RTT side,
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:yangian-tower-mc4-criterion}} gives the
completed Yangian bar object
$\widehat{\bar B}(Y)=\varprojlim_N \bar B(Y_{\le N})$ as a separated
complete pro-nilpotent curved dg coalgebra together with
$\Omega(\widehat{\bar B}(Y)) \xrightarrow{\sim} Y$ for the inverse-limit
tower $Y=\varprojlim_N Y_{\le N}$. Supplying check~\textup{(4)} via
Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:yangian-hlevel-comparison-criterion}} then
identifies that standard RTT completion with the desired H-level dg
model. This combined M-level/H-level package is the content of B2.}
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What B2 does and does not give]
\label{rem:b2-scope}
\index{Bridge Theorem!B2 scope}
With B2 in hand, the middle term
$\operatorname{Mod}^{\mathrm{comp}}(\Ydg_{\cA})$ in
Conjecture~\ref{conj:full-dk-bridge} becomes an actual
completed module category over a realized dg algebra, not
formal target data. However, B2 alone does not give the
comparison functors to either the factorization side or
the spectral quantum-group side: those are the content of
B1 (for the category-$\mathcal{O}$ comparison) and B4
(for the spectral identification), and the
Bridge Criterion Theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bridge-criterion}) combines all three.

The reason for isolating B2 is that its four checks are
purely analytical/algebraic (inverse limits, Mittag--Leffler
conditions), involve no categorical or homotopical subtlety
beyond the bar-cobar formalism already in place, and three of
the four are already proved. The remaining open piece is the H-level
realization/comparison packet; on the standard type-$A$ frontier its
live local coefficient residue reduces to one mixed-tensor check, but
the full check~(4) still includes realizing the RTT-adapted dg model
with the required completed comparison data.
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% § From the bar propagator to r(z)
%% ================================================================
\subsection{From the bar propagator to \texorpdfstring{$r(z)$}{r(z)}}
\label{subsec:bar-propagator-to-rz}
\index{propagator!bar to $r(z)$|textbf}
\index{Bridge Theorem!propagator identification}

The benchmark shadow comparison between the chiral factorization side
and the dg-shifted Yangian side is the identification
$r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$, where $\tau$ is the propagator of the
$\Eone$-bar complex on ordered configuration spaces.
This subsection computes $r(z)$ explicitly in the first two
benchmark families.

\begin{proposition}[Free/Heisenberg propagator matching;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:free-propagator-matching}
\index{propagator!free/Heisenberg}
For the Heisenberg algebra $\cH_k$ at level~$k$, the
bar-complex propagator on $\overline{C}_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bC)$
is
\[
\eta_{12} = d\log(z_1 - z_2)
= \frac{dz_1 - dz_2}{z_1 - z_2},
\]
and the degree-$2$ collision residue gives
\[
r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}
= \frac{k}{z}
\;\in\;
\cA^! \otimes \cA^!(z^{-1}).
\]
This is the rank-$1$ meromorphic kernel with a simple pole at
$z = 0$, matching the $r$-matrix entry in the landscape table
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:rmatrix-pole-landscape})}.
For the free $\beta\gamma$ system, whose OPE
$\beta(z)\gamma(w) \sim 1/(z{-}w)$ has only a simple pole,
the $d\log$ absorption sends $z^{-1} \to z^0$ and
the collision $r$-matrix vanishes: $r^{\beta\gamma}(z) = 0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The CG apparatus (Proposition~\ref{prop:chriss-ginzburg-structure})
realizes the bar differential on
$\overline{C}_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bC)$ as $d_{\mathrm{bar}} =
d_{\mathrm{int}} + [\tau, -]$, where $\tau$ is the MC element in
the convolution algebra $\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(\cA), \cA^!)$ and the bracket
action is contraction with the propagator
$\eta_{12} = d\log(z_1 - z_2)$
on internal edges. For the Heisenberg algebra $\cH_k$, the OPE
$J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z{-}w)^2$ has a double pole. The $d\log$ kernel
absorbs one pole order: $z^{-2} \to z^{-1}$, giving
$r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2} = k/z$.
For the $\beta\gamma$ system, the mixed OPE
$\beta(z)\gamma(w) \sim 1/(z{-}w)$ has only a simple pole;
after $d\log$ absorption the result is regular, so
$r^{\beta\gamma}(z) = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Affine $\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ propagator
matching; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:affine-propagator-matching}
\index{propagator!affine $\mathfrak{sl}_2$}
For the affine $\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ chiral algebra at level~$k$,
the degree-$2$ bar propagator extracts
\[
r(z) = \frac{k\,\Omega}{z}
\;\in\;
\mathfrak{g} \otimes \mathfrak{g}(z^{-1})
\;\subset\;
\cA^! \otimes \cA^!(z^{-1}),
\]
where $\Omega = \sum_a I^a \otimes I_a$ is the quadratic Casimir
tensor. Under the Kazhdan equivalence, this is identified with
the classical $r$-matrix
$r_{\mathrm{KZ}}(z) = k\,\Omega/z$ of the KZ equation.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The CG structure on the bar complex of
$\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ at level~$k$ gives
$d_{\mathrm{bar}} = d_{\mathrm{int}} + [\tau, -]$ on
$\overline{C}_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bC)$, where the MC element~$\tau$
acts through the propagator $\eta_{12} = d\log(z_1 - z_2)$
tensored with the Lie-algebraic pairing.
The OPE
$J^a(z_1) J^b(z_2) \sim k\delta^{ab}/(z_1-z_2)^2
+ f^{ab}{}_{c} J^c(z_2)/(z_1-z_2)$
has a double pole (contributing to degree~$1$ / curvature) and
a simple pole (contributing to degree~$2$). The degree-$2$
MC projection extracts the double-pole coefficient after
$d\log$ absorption: the $k\delta^{ab}/(z_1-z_2)^2$ term shifts
to $k\delta^{ab}/(z_1-z_2)$ under the $d\log$ kernel,
giving $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2} = k\,\Omega/z$,
where $\Omega = \sum_a I^a \otimes I_a$ is the quadratic Casimir.
The simple-pole OPE term $f^{ab}{}_{c}J^c/(z_1-z_2)$ becomes
regular after $d\log$ absorption and drops.
Under the Kazhdan equivalence, this is precisely the classical KZ
$r$-matrix $r_{\mathrm{KZ}}(z) = k\,\Omega/z$, confirming the
CG identification $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$ in the affine benchmark.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Yangian benchmark: $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$]
\label{rem:yangian-propagator-benchmark}
\index{propagator!Yangian $\mathfrak{sl}_2$}
The first genuinely noncommutative benchmark is $Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$.
The rational $R$-matrix
\[
R(u) = \mathbb{1} - \frac{\hbar\, P}{u}
\]
(where $P$ is the permutation operator) should be recovered
from the degree-$2$ MC projection of the Yangian bar complex
as $r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2} = \hbar\, P / z$.

At the CG level, this is the assertion that the MC element
$\Theta_{Y(\mathfrak{sl}_2)}$ in the convolution algebra
$\operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(Y), Y^!)$ has degree-$2$ projection equal to
the Yang $r$-matrix. The Yang--Baxter equation
$[r_{12}, r_{13}] + [r_{12}, r_{23}] + [r_{13}, r_{23}] = 0$
should then follow from $D^2 = 0$ at the convolution level
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:ainfty-yb-consistency}): the MC equation
$D\tau + \tfrac{1}{2}[\tau,\tau] = 0$ projected to degree~$3$ gives
precisely the classical Yang--Baxter equation for $r(z) =
\tau|_{\deg 2}$.

This is the first nontrivial check: the bar-complex MC element must
encode the RTT relation as its degree-$2$ shadow. The Yangian
$R$-matrix is to the bar-complex propagator what $\kappa(\cA)$ is
to $\Theta_\cA$: a low-degree projection of a universal MC
element.
\end{remark}

%% =================================================================
%% § r-MATRIX POLE LANDSCAPE
%% =================================================================

\begin{proposition}[The collision-residue $r$-matrix across the standard landscape;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:rmatrix-pole-landscape}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!pole landscape|textbf}
}
\index{pole absorption!standard landscape}
For each standard family, the collision residue
$r^{\mathrm{coll}}_\cA(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
has pole orders exactly one less than the corresponding OPE, by the
$d\log$ absorption rule
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:three-r-matrices})}:
$z^{-n}$ in the OPE becomes $z^{-(n-1)}$ in the $r$-matrix, and
$z^{-1}$ terms become regular and drop.
The explicit formulas are:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lccl}
\toprule
\textbf{Family}
& \textbf{OPE max pole}
& \textbf{$r$-matrix max pole}
& \textbf{$r^{\mathrm{coll}}_\cA(z)$} \\
\midrule
$\cH_k$ (Heisenberg)
 & $z^{-2}$ & $z^{-1}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{H}}(z) = k/z$ \\[3pt]
$\hat\fg_k$ (affine $\mathfrak{sl}_2$)
 & $z^{-2}$ & $z^{-1}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z) = k\Omega/z$ \\[3pt]
$\hat\fg_k$ (affine $\mathfrak{sl}_3$)
 & $z^{-2}$ & $z^{-1}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z) = k\Omega/z$ \\[3pt]
$\mathrm{Vir}_c$
 & $z^{-4}$ & $z^{-3}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{Vir}}(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ \\[3pt]
$\cW_3$ ($TT$ channel)
 & $z^{-4}$ & $z^{-3}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{W}_3}_{TT}(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ \\[3pt]
$\cW_3$ ($WW$ channel)
 & $z^{-6}$ & $z^{-5}$
 & $r^{\mathrm{W}_3}_{WW}(z)
 = (c/3)/z^5 + 2T/z^3 + \partial T/z^2 + \cdots$ \\[3pt]
$\beta\gamma$
 & $z^{-1}$ & $0$ (regular)
 & $r^{\beta\gamma}(z) = 0$ \\[3pt]
$bc$ (free fermion)
 & $z^{-1}$ & $0$ (regular)
 & $r^{bc}(z) = 0$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
For the affine families, the off-diagonal channels
$J^a J^b$ ($a \neq b$) have at most a simple OPE pole
$f^{ab}{}_{c}J^c/(z{-}w)$, which becomes regular and drops:
only the Casimir (metric) part survives in~$r(z)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each entry is verified by applying the pole-shift rule
$z^{-n} \mapsto z^{-(n-1)}$ to the known OPE.

\emph{Heisenberg.}
The OPE $J(z)J(w) \sim k/(z{-}w)^2$ has a single double pole.
After $d\log$ absorption: $z^{-2} \to z^{-1}$, giving
$r^{\mathrm{H}}(z) = k/z$.

\emph{Affine Kac--Moody.}
The OPE has $k\delta^{ab}/(z{-}w)^2 + f^{ab}{}_{c}J^c/(z{-}w)$.
The double pole shifts to $z^{-1}$; the simple pole shifts to
$z^0$ (regular) and drops. Therefore $r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z) = k\Omega/z$
where $\Omega = \sum_a I^a \otimes I_a$ is the quadratic Casimir.
This holds for all $\fg$ by the same argument.

\emph{Virasoro.}
The OPE $T(z)T(w) \sim (c/2)/(z{-}w)^4 + 2T/(z{-}w)^2
+ \partial T/(z{-}w)$ has poles at orders $4$, $2$, $1$.
After shifting: $z^{-4} \to z^{-3}$, $z^{-2} \to z^{-1}$,
$z^{-1} \to z^0$ (drops). Hence
$r^{\mathrm{Vir}}(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$
with poles at $z^{-3}$ and $z^{-1}$ only (both odd order).

\emph{$\cW_3$, $TT$ channel.}
Identical to the Virasoro.

\emph{$\cW_3$, $WW$ channel.}
The $W(z)W(w)$ OPE has poles at orders $6, 4, 3, 2, 1$.
After shifting: $z^{-6} \to z^{-5}$, $z^{-4} \to z^{-3}$,
$z^{-3} \to z^{-2}$, $z^{-2} \to z^{-1}$,
$z^{-1} \to z^0$ (drops).
The $r$-matrix has four nonzero pole orders: $5, 3, 2, 1$.
The even-order pole $z^{-2}$ is present because $W$ has
conformal weight~$3$ (odd), so the OPE includes odd-order poles
$z^{-3}$ which shift to even-order poles in the $r$-matrix.
This is not a violation of bosonic parity
(Proposition~\ref{prop:bosonic-parity-constraint} below).

\emph{$\beta\gamma$ and $bc$.}
The mixed OPE $\beta(z)\gamma(w) \sim 1/(z{-}w)$ has only a simple pole.
After $d\log$ absorption: $z^{-1} \to z^0$ (regular).
All diagonal channels ($\beta\beta$, $\gamma\gamma$, $\psi\psi$)
have no singular OPE. Therefore $r(z) = 0$ in all channels.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Bosonic parity constraint on $r$-matrix poles;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:bosonic-parity-constraint}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!bosonic parity constraint|textbf}
\index{bosonic parity|textbf}
For a single bosonic generator of integer conformal weight~$h$,
the same-generator $r$-matrix
$r^{\mathrm{coll}}_{\cA\cA}(z)$
has only odd-order poles.
More precisely, the OPE has poles at even orders
$z^{-2h}, z^{-(2h-2)}, \ldots, z^{-2}$ and the descendant
$z^{-1}$; after $d\log$ absorption, the surviving poles are at
odd orders $z^{-(2h-1)}, z^{-(2h-3)}, \ldots, z^{-1}$.
In particular:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $h = 1$ \textup{(}Kac--Moody\textup{)}: $r$-matrix pole at $z^{-1}$,
\item $h = 2$ \textup{(}Virasoro\textup{)}: poles at $z^{-3}$, $z^{-1}$,
\item $h = 3$ \textup{(}$W_3$, same-generator $WW$\textup{)}: max pole at $z^{-5}$.
\end{enumerate}
The pattern is: $\max$ pole order of $r^{\mathrm{coll}}(z) = 2h - 1$.

For multi-generator algebras, different-generator channels
\textup{(}$TW$, $WT$\textup{)} can have even-order $r$-matrix
poles because the OPE between generators of different weights
includes odd-order poles that shift to even-order.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The OPE $\Phi_h(z)\Phi_h(w)$ between two copies of a bosonic
primary of weight~$h$ has poles at even orders
$z^{-2h}, z^{-(2h-2)}, \ldots, z^{-2}$
(from conformal Ward identities and the Sugawara structure)
plus the descendant contribution at $z^{-1}$.
The $d\log(z_1 - z_2)$ measure absorbs one pole order:
$z^{-2j} \to z^{-(2j-1)}$ for $j = 1, \ldots, h$ (all odd),
$z^{-1} \to z^0$ (drops).
The resulting $r$-matrix poles are at odd orders
$z^{-(2h-1)}, z^{-(2h-3)}, \ldots, z^{-1}$, as claimed.
Computations \texttt{test\_rmatrix\_landscape.py}
and \texttt{test\_rmatrix\_poles\_comprehensive.py}
verify this for all eight standard families ($205$ tests).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[CYBE from bar-complex MC equation;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:cybe-from-mc}
\index{CYBE!from MC equation|textbf}
\index{classical Yang--Baxter equation|see{CYBE}}
\index{infinitesimal braid relation|see{CYBE}}
For affine $\hat\fg_k$ with $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$,
the collision residue $r^{\mathrm{KM}}(z) = k\Omega/z$
satisfies the classical Yang--Baxter equation
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cybe-casimir}
[r_{12}(z_{12}),\, r_{13}(z_{13})]
+ [r_{12}(z_{12}),\, r_{23}(z_{23})]
+ [r_{13}(z_{13}),\, r_{23}(z_{23})]
= 0
\end{equation}
where $z_{ij} = z_i - z_j$.
Equation~\eqref{eq:cybe-casimir} reduces via partial fractions
to the infinitesimal braid relation
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ibr}
[\Omega_{ij},\, \Omega_{ik} + \Omega_{jk}] = 0
\end{equation}
for all distinct triples $(i,j,k)$, which holds because $\Omega$
is the quadratic Casimir.

\medskip\noindent
The skew-symmetry $r_{12}(z) + r_{21}(-z) = 0$ holds because the
Casimir is symmetric under permutation
($P \cdot \Omega \cdot P = \Omega$) and
$r(z) = k\Omega/z$ is an odd function of~$z$.
For the Virasoro, $r^{\mathrm{Vir}}(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$
is odd because it has only odd-order poles
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:bosonic-parity-constraint})},
so the skew-symmetry holds automatically.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The CYBE is the degree-$3$ projection of the MC equation
$D\Theta + \frac{1}{2}[\Theta, \Theta] = 0$
(Remark~\ref{rem:yangian-propagator-benchmark}).
For $r(z) = k\Omega/z$, the commutator
$[r_{12}(z_{12}), r_{13}(z_{13})] = k^2[\Omega_{12}, \Omega_{13}]/(z_{12}\cdot z_{13})$.
By partial fractions $1/(z_{12}\cdot z_{13}) + \text{cyc} = 0$,
the CYBE reduces to the infinitesimal braid relation~\eqref{eq:ibr}.

The IBR for $\Omega = \sum_a T^a \otimes T_a$ is a standard identity:
it follows from $[T^a, T^b] = f^{ab}{}_c T^c$ and the invariance of the
Killing form $\kappa(T^a, T_b) = \delta^a_b$.
Numerical verification in the fundamental representations of
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$ ($4\times 4$ matrices) and $\mathfrak{sl}_3$
($9\times 9$ matrices) confirms all three IBR identities to machine
precision ($<10^{-10}$); see \texttt{test\_rmatrix\_landscape.py},
classes \texttt{TestCYBESl2} and \texttt{TestCYBESl3}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The pole hierarchy and conformal weight]
\label{rem:pole-hierarchy-conformal-weight}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!pole hierarchy}
The $r$-matrix pole landscape reveals a hierarchy indexed by
conformal weight:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.1}
\begin{tabular}{cll}
$h$ & family & max $r$-matrix pole \\
\midrule
$0$ (or $1/2$) & $\beta\gamma$, $bc$ & $0$ (regular) \\
$1$ & Heisenberg, $\hat\fg_k$ & $z^{-1}$ \\
$2$ & Virasoro & $z^{-3}$ \\
$3$ & $\cW_3$ ($WW$) & $z^{-5}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The pattern $\max\text{pole}(r) = 2h - 1$ is
Proposition~\ref{prop:bosonic-parity-constraint}.
Physically, higher-spin generators produce longer-range correlations
in the $r$-matrix, reflected in higher-order poles. The shadow depth
classification (G/L/C/M) is orthogonal to this hierarchy: shadow depth
classifies complexity within the Koszul world, while pole order
classifies the binary collision structure.
\end{remark}

%% =================================================================
%% § INTEGRABLE STRUCTURES FROM THE BAR COMPLEX
%% =================================================================

\subsection{Integrable structures from the bar complex}
\label{subsec:integrable-structures-bar-complex}
\index{integrable systems!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{Bethe ansatz!from shadow connection|textbf}
\index{KZ equation!from shadow connection|textbf}
\index{Verlinde formula!from shadow complex|textbf}

The preceding subsections established that the collision residue
$r_\cA(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
recovers the classical $r$-matrix for each standard family,
and that the CYBE follows from the MC equation at degree~$3$.
This analysis extends in five directions: the quantum
$R$-matrix from the bar coproduct, the elliptic deformation on
$E_\tau$, the Bethe ansatz from the shadow potential, the KZ
equation as the restriction of the shadow connection to
configuration space, and the Verlinde formula from the shadow
complex at genus~$g$. Throughout, $\hat\fg_k$ denotes affine
$\fg$ at positive integer level $k$, and $h^\vee$ is the dual
Coxeter number.

\begin{proposition}[Quantum $R$-matrix from the bar coproduct;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:rmatrix-from-bar-coproduct}
\index{R-matrix@$R$-matrix!from bar coproduct|textbf}
\index{quantum Yang--Baxter equation!from coassociativity|textbf}
Let $\cA = \hat\fg_k$ be an affine Kac--Moody chiral algebra and
$\bar B(\cA)$ its bar complex. The bar coproduct
\[
\Delta_{\bar B}\colon \bar B(\cA) \to
\bar B(\cA) \hat\otimes \bar B(\cA)
\]
is the factorization coproduct induced by the diagonal embedding
$\Delta_{1,2}\colon X \hookrightarrow X \times X$. Restriction to the
ordered configuration locus $C_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\mathbb{C}) \subset
\mathrm{Ran}^2(X)$ and passage to the degree-$2$ component yields
the quantum $R$-matrix
\begin{equation}\label{eq:quantum-R-from-bar-coproduct}
R(u) = \mathbb{1} + \frac{\hbar\, \Omega}{u}
+ \sum_{n \ge 2} \hbar^n\, r_n(u)
\;\in\;
\operatorname{End}(V \otimes V)[\![{\hbar}]\!][u^{-1}],
\end{equation}
where $V$ is any finite-dimensional $\fg$-module,
$\hbar = \pi i/(k + h^\vee)$,
$\Omega = \sum_a T^a \otimes T_a$ is the quadratic Casimir,
and $r_n(u)$ are rational functions of~$u$ determined by higher
bar-tree contractions. In the fundamental representation of
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$, $R(u)$ coincides with the Jimbo
$R$-matrix~\cite{Jimbo85}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:jimbo-R-matrix}
R^{\mathrm{fund}}_{\mathfrak{sl}_N}
= q \sum_i e_{ii} \otimes e_{ii}
+ \sum_{i \neq j} e_{ii} \otimes e_{jj}
+ (q - q^{-1}) \sum_{i > j} e_{ij} \otimes e_{ji},
\quad q = e^{\hbar}.
\end{equation}
The quantum Yang--Baxter equation \textup{(}QYBE\textup{)}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:qybe-from-bar}
R_{12}(u_{12})\, R_{13}(u_{13})\, R_{23}(u_{23})
= R_{23}(u_{23})\, R_{13}(u_{13})\, R_{12}(u_{12})
\end{equation}
holds as a formal consequence of the coassociativity
$(\Delta \otimes \operatorname{id}) \circ \Delta
= (\operatorname{id} \otimes \Delta) \circ \Delta$
of the bar coproduct.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The bar complex $\bar B(\cA)$ carries a natural factorization
coalgebra structure (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-modular-operad}): for
every finite subset $I = I_1 \sqcup I_2$ of distinct points in~$X$,
the factorization isomorphism provides
$\bar B(\cA)_I \simeq
\bar B(\cA)_{I_1} \hat\otimes \bar B(\cA)_{I_2}$,
and the coproduct $\Delta_{\bar B}$ is the structure map for the
partition $\{1\} \sqcup \{2\}$ of a two-element set.

Restrict to $C_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\mathbb{C})$ with coordinates
$(z_1, z_2)$ and set $u = z_1 - z_2$. The bar propagator is
$\eta_{12} = d\log(z_1 - z_2) = du/u$
(Remark~\ref{rem:three-r-matrices}). The degree-$2$ component of the
coproduct, expanded in the $\hbar$-deformation parameter
$\hbar = \pi i/(k + h^\vee)$, produces the series
\eqref{eq:quantum-R-from-bar-coproduct}. The leading term
$\mathbb{1} + \hbar\, \Omega/u$ is the classical $r$-matrix
(Proposition~\ref{prop:cybe-from-mc}). Higher-order terms $r_n(u)$
arise from contractions of $n$-fold iterated bar-tree graphs with
$n$ internal propagator edges, each contributing a factor of~$\hbar$.

The QYBE~\eqref{eq:qybe-from-bar} follows from coassociativity.
Consider three points $z_1, z_2, z_3 \in C_3^{\mathrm{ord}}(\mathbb{C})$.
The factorization coproduct applied to
$\bar B(\cA)_{\{1,2,3\}}$ factors through either of the two
iterated coproductions
$(\Delta_{12} \otimes \operatorname{id}) \circ \Delta_{12,3}$ or
$(\operatorname{id} \otimes \Delta_{23}) \circ \Delta_{1,23}$.
Their equality is the coassociativity axiom. Projecting both sides
to the degree-$2$ component in each tensor factor and reading off the
$u$-dependence yields~\eqref{eq:qybe-from-bar}. In the fundamental
representation of $\mathfrak{sl}_N$, the explicit matrix
\eqref{eq:jimbo-R-matrix} is verified numerically for
$\mathfrak{sl}_2$ ($4\times 4$) and $\mathfrak{sl}_3$ ($9\times 9$)
in \texttt{quantum\_rmatrix\_barcomplex.py}, classes
\texttt{verify\_qybe\_sl2} and \texttt{verify\_qybe\_sl3}:
the QYBE residual is $< 10^{-10}$ for all tested values of
$q \in \{e^{i\pi/3}, e^{i\pi/4}, e^{i\pi/5}\}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Elliptic $R$-matrix from the genus-$1$ shadow;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:elliptic-rmatrix-shadow}
\index{R-matrix@$R$-matrix!elliptic|textbf}
\index{Belavin r-matrix@Belavin $r$-matrix|textbf}
\index{shadow connection!genus-1 deformation}
Let $E_\tau = \mathbb{C}/(\mathbb{Z} + \mathbb{Z}\tau)$ be an
elliptic curve with $\operatorname{Im}(\tau) > 0$. The bar
propagator on $E_\tau$ is
\[
\eta_{12}^{E_\tau}
= d\log E(z_1, z_2)
= \zeta_\tau(z_1 - z_2)\, d(z_1 - z_2),
\]
where $E(z,w)$ is the prime form on $E_\tau$ and $\zeta_\tau$ is
the Weierstrass zeta function for periods $(1, \tau)$.
For affine $\hat\fg_k$ with $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_N$, the collision
residue on $E_\tau$ produces the Belavin classical elliptic
$r$-matrix~\cite{Belavin81, BelavinDrinfeld82}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:elliptic-rmatrix}
r^{\mathrm{ell}}_\cA(z, \tau)
= \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{1,2}(\Theta_\cA)\big|_{E_\tau}
= k \Bigl(
 \zeta_\tau(z) \cdot \frac{H \otimes H}{2}
 + \phi_+(z, \tau)\, E \otimes F
 + \phi_-(z, \tau)\, F \otimes E
\Bigr)
\end{equation}
for $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$, where
$\phi_\pm(z, \tau) = \theta_1'(0|\tau)\, \theta_1(z \pm \tfrac{1}{2}|\tau)
/\bigl(\theta_1(z|\tau)\, \theta_1(\pm\tfrac{1}{2}|\tau)\bigr)$,
and the Weierstrass $\wp$-function
$\wp(z, \tau) = -\zeta_\tau'(z)$ appears as the
shadow metric on the genus-$1$ moduli component:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-metric-wp}
Q^{(1)}_{\hat\fg_k}(z, \tau)
= \wp(z, \tau).
\end{equation}
The shadow connection at genus~$1$ restricts to the KZB
connection~\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:kz-from-shadow})}:
\[
\nabla^{\mathrm{KZB}}_\tau
= \partial_\tau
 - \frac{1}{2\pi i(k + h^\vee)}\,
 \wp(z, \tau)\, \Omega.
\]
The degeneration chain
\[
r^{\mathrm{ell}}(z, \tau)
\xrightarrow{\;\operatorname{Im}(\tau) \to \infty\;}
r^{\mathrm{trig}}(z)
\xrightarrow{\;L \to \infty\;}
r^{\mathrm{rat}}(z)
= k\Omega/z
\]
recovers the trigonometric and rational $r$-matrices as successive
limits.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
On $E_\tau$, the prime form is
$E(z) = \theta_1(z|\tau)/\theta_1'(0|\tau)$
(Mumford's Tata Lectures, \S IIIa), so
$d\log E(z) = (\theta_1'(z|\tau)/\theta_1(z|\tau))\, dz$.
Adding the quasi-period correction $2\eta_1 z$ (where
$\eta_1 = -\theta_1'''(0|\tau)/(6\theta_1'(0|\tau))$ is the
first quasi-period) gives the Weierstrass zeta function
$\zeta_\tau(z) = \theta_1'(z|\tau)/\theta_1(z|\tau) + 2\eta_1 z$.

The collision residue on $E_\tau$ proceeds exactly as in the
genus-$0$ case (Proposition~\ref{prop:affine-propagator-matching}),
except that $1/(z_1 - z_2)$ is replaced by $\zeta_\tau(z_1 - z_2)$.
For the Cartan channel $J^a \otimes J^b$ with $a = b \in \mathfrak{h}$,
the residue extracts $\zeta_\tau(z) \cdot H \otimes H/2$. For the
root channels $E \otimes F$ and $F \otimes E$, the twisted boundary
conditions on the torus introduce the theta-function ratio
$\phi_\pm(z, \tau)$ (Belavin~\cite{Belavin81}). The overall
level factor $k$ arises from the OPE normalization.

The degeneration: as $\operatorname{Im}(\tau) \to \infty$,
$q = e^{2\pi i \tau} \to 0$, and
$\zeta_\tau(z) \to \pi \cot(\pi z) + O(q)$,
$\phi_\pm(z, \tau) \to \pi/\sin(\pi z) + O(q)$.
Therefore $r^{\mathrm{ell}} \to r^{\mathrm{trig}}$.
The further limit $L \to \infty$ with $z \mapsto z/L$ sends
$\pi \cot(\pi z/L) \to L/z$, recovering
$r^{\mathrm{rat}}(z) = k\Omega/z$.
Both limits are verified numerically in
\texttt{elliptic\_rmatrix\_shadow.py}:
the relative error $\|r^{\mathrm{ell}} - r^{\mathrm{trig}}\|/\|r^{\mathrm{trig}}\|$
decreases monotonically with
$\operatorname{Im}(\tau)$ and is $< 10^{-6}$ at
$\operatorname{Im}(\tau) = 12$ (function
\texttt{elliptic\_to\_trigonometric\_limit}).

The identification~\eqref{eq:shadow-metric-wp}: the shadow metric
$Q^{(g)}_\cA$ at genus~$g$ is the curvature of the shadow connection
on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$. At genus~$1$, the moduli space
$\mathcal{M}_{1,1}$ is parametrized by $(z, \tau)$. The $z$-dependence of
the connection involves $\zeta_\tau(z)$; its derivative
$-\zeta_\tau'(z) = \wp(z, \tau)$ is the curvature in the
$z$-direction, which is the shadow metric component.

The classical YBE for $r^{\mathrm{ell}}$ is verified numerically
in \texttt{elliptic\_rmatrix\_shadow.py}, function
\texttt{verify\_ybe\_elliptic\_sl2}: the residual is $< 10^{-6}$
for generic $(z_1, z_2, z_3, \tau)$. This provides independent
confirmation that the genus-$1$ shadow data satisfies the integrability
constraint.
\end{proof}


\begin{theorem}[Bethe ansatz equations from the MC stationarity;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:bae-from-mc-stationarity}
\index{Bethe ansatz!from MC stationarity|textbf}
\index{shadow potential!Bethe ansatz}
\index{Nekrasov--Shatashvili!gauge/Bethe correspondence}
Let $\cA = \hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k$ at positive integer level~$k$
and let $\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$ be the shadow connection
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:shadow-connection})}. Consider a
spin chain of length~$L$ with~$M$ magnon excitations coupled to the
genus-$0$ shadow connection on $\mathrm{Conf}_L(\mathbb{P}^1)$.
Define the shadow Yang--Yang potential
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-yang-yang}
\mathcal{Y}(u_1, \ldots, u_M)
= \sum_{i=1}^{M}
 L \cdot \phi_1(u_i)
 - \sum_{1 \le i < j \le M}
 \phi_2(u_i - u_j),
\end{equation}
where $\phi_1(u) = \int^u \log\bigl((t + i/2)/(t - i/2)\bigr)\, dt$
is the driving phase and $\phi_2(u) = \int^u \log\bigl((t+i)/(t-i)\bigr)\, dt$
is the scattering phase, both determined by the $r$-matrix
$r(z) = k\Omega/z$ via the Nekrasov--Shatashvili
limit~\cite{NekrasovShatashvili09} of the genus-$0$ shadow amplitude.
Then the Bethe ansatz equations
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bae-xxx}
\prod_{j \neq i}
\frac{u_i - u_j + i}{u_i - u_j - i}
= \biggl(\frac{u_i + i/2}{u_i - i/2}\biggr)^{\!L},
\qquad i = 1, \ldots, M,
\end{equation}
are equivalent to the stationarity condition
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mc-stationarity}
\frac{\partial \mathcal{Y}}{\partial u_i} = 2\pi n_i,
\qquad n_i \in \mathbb{Z},
\end{equation}
and the Bethe roots $\{u_i\}$ at stationarity determine the
eigenvalues of the transfer matrix
$T(u) = \operatorname{Tr}_0[R_{0L}(u) \cdots R_{01}(u)]$
constructed from the quantum $R$-matrix of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:rmatrix-from-bar-coproduct}}. The
transfer matrices commute at distinct spectral parameters:
$[T(u), T(v)] = 0$,
as a consequence of the QYBE.

The energy eigenvalues of the Heisenberg XXX Hamiltonian
$H = J \sum_{i=1}^{L} \vec{S}_i \cdot \vec{S}_{i+1}$ are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bethe-energy}
E = \frac{JL}{4}
 - \frac{J}{2} \sum_{a=1}^{M}
 \frac{1}{u_a^2 + 1/4}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof proceeds in three steps.

\emph{Step~1: the shadow potential from the $r$-matrix.}
The genus-$0$ shadow connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} = d - (1/\kappa) \sum_{i<j} \Omega_{ij}\, d\log(z_i - z_j)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:kz-from-shadow} below) acts on
sections over $\mathrm{Conf}_n(\mathbb{P}^1)$. In the
Nekrasov--Shatashvili limit, the flat-section equation
$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}} \Psi = 0$ is solved by the WKB ansatz
$\Psi = \exp(\mathcal{Y}/\hbar)$ where $\hbar = 1/(k + h^\vee)$.
The stationarity condition
$\partial \mathcal{Y}/\partial u_i = 2\pi n_i$ for this WKB
approximation is the logarithmic form of the BAE.

\emph{Step~2: equivalence with the product-form BAE.}
Take the exponential of~\eqref{eq:mc-stationarity}. The derivative
$\partial \phi_1/\partial u = \log((u + i/2)/(u - i/2))$, so
$\exp(\partial_{u_i} \mathcal{Y}) = ((u_i + i/2)/(u_i - i/2))^L
\cdot \prod_{j \neq i} (u_i - u_j - i)/(u_i - u_j + i)$.
Setting this equal to $e^{2\pi i n_i} = 1$ gives
exactly~\eqref{eq:bae-xxx}.

\emph{Step~3: transfer matrix commutativity and energy.}
The transfer matrix
$T(u) = \operatorname{Tr}_0[R_{0L}(u) \cdots R_{01}(u)]$ is
built from the quantum $R$-matrix $R(u) = u \cdot \mathbb{1} + P$
(the Yang $R$-matrix for the XXX chain), where $P$ is the
permutation operator on $\mathbb{C}^2 \otimes \mathbb{C}^2$.
The QYBE~\eqref{eq:qybe-from-bar} implies
$R_{12}(u-v)\, T_1(u)\, T_2(v) = T_2(v)\, T_1(u)\, R_{12}(u-v)$
(the RTT relation). Taking the trace over the first auxiliary space:
$\operatorname{Tr}_1[R_{12}(u-v)\, T_1(u)\, T_2(v)]
= \operatorname{Tr}_1[T_2(v)\, T_1(u)\, R_{12}(u-v)]$.
Using the cyclic property of the trace and $R$-matrix regularity
($R(0) \propto P$), this yields $[T(u), T(v)] = 0$.

The Hamiltonian is extracted as
$H \propto \partial_u \log T(u)\big|_{u=0}$,
and the Bethe ansatz diagonalizes $T(u)$ simultaneously for all~$u$.
On a Bethe state $|\{u_a\}\rangle$, the energy
eigenvalue~\eqref{eq:bethe-energy} follows from the dispersion
relation $\varepsilon(u) = -J/(2(u^2 + 1/4))$ for each magnon.
Numerical verification in \texttt{bethe\_ansatz\_shadow.py}:
for chain lengths $L = 4, 6, 8$ with $M = L/2$ (half-filling),
the BAE roots from \texttt{solve\_xxx\_bae} yield energies
agreeing with exact diagonalization to $< 10^{-8}$
(\texttt{heisenberg\_xxx\_hamiltonian}). Transfer-matrix
commutativity $\|[T(u), T(v)]\| < 10^{-10}$ is confirmed by
\texttt{xxx\_verify\_transfer\_commuting}.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[KZ equation from the shadow connection;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:kz-from-shadow}
\index{KZ equation!from shadow connection|textbf}
\index{shadow connection!KZ restriction}
\index{Knizhnik--Zamolodchikov!from bar complex}
Let $\cA = \hat\fg_k$ with $\fg$ simple and
$\kappa = \kappa(\hat\fg_k) = \dim(\fg) \cdot (k + h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$
the modular characteristic. The genus-$0$ shadow connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{sh}}$ on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{0,n}$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:shadow-connection})} restricts to
the open stratum $\mathrm{Conf}_n(\mathbb{P}^1) \subset
\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{0,n}$ as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:kz-from-shadow}
\nabla^{\mathrm{KZ}}
= d - \frac{1}{k + h^\vee}
 \sum_{1 \le i < j \le n}
 \Omega_{ij}\, d\log(z_i - z_j)
\end{equation}
after choosing an affine coordinate on $\mathbb{P}^1$ and
fixing $z_n = \infty$. Here $\Omega_{ij} = \sum_a T^a_i \otimes (T_a)_j$
is the Casimir operator acting on the $i$-th and $j$-th tensor factors
of $V_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes V_{n-1}$.

The KZ equation $\nabla^{\mathrm{KZ}} F = 0$ is therefore the
genus-$0$ flat-section equation of the shadow connection,
restricted to configuration space and evaluated in the representation
$V_1 \otimes \cdots \otimes V_n$ of $\fg^{\oplus n}$.

For $n = 4$ with all external legs in the fundamental representation
$V_{1/2}$ of $\mathfrak{sl}_2$, the KZ equation reduces to the
hypergeometric ODE
\[
z(1-z) F'' + (c_h - (a + b + 1)z) F' - ab\, F = 0
\]
with $a = -1/(k+2)$, $b = (k+1)/(k+2)$, $c_h = k/(k+2)$. The
two independent solutions
\begin{align}
\label{eq:kz-singlet}
F_0(z) &= {}_2F_1\bigl(-\tfrac{1}{k+2},\,
 \tfrac{k+1}{k+2};\,\tfrac{k}{k+2};\, z\bigr)
\quad\textup{(singlet channel)}, \\
\label{eq:kz-triplet}
F_1(z) &= z^{2/(k+2)}\,
{}_2F_1\bigl(\tfrac{1}{k+2},\,
 \tfrac{k+3}{k+2};\,\tfrac{k+4}{k+2};\, z\bigr)
\quad\textup{(triplet channel)},
\end{align}
are the $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ conformal blocks in the $s$-channel.
Their monodromy around $z = 0$ is
$\operatorname{diag}(1, e^{4\pi i/(k+2)})$, and the braiding
eigenvalues in the singlet and triplet channels are
$R_0 = -q^{-3/2}$ and $R_1 = q^{1/2}$ respectively, where
$q = e^{i\pi/(k+2)}$. This is the Drinfeld--Kohno identification:
the monodromy representation of $\nabla^{\mathrm{KZ}}$ coincides
with the $R$-matrix representation of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:rmatrix-from-bar-coproduct}} at the level of
