eigenvalues on each fusion channel.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The shadow connection at genus~$0$, degree~$n$ is the flat connection
on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{0,n}$ whose horizontal sections are
the shadow amplitudes $\operatorname{Sh}_{0,n}(\Theta_\cA)$
(Definition~\ref{def:shadow-algebra}). On the open stratum
$\mathrm{Conf}_n(\mathbb{P}^1)$, the log-singularity along boundary
divisors is resolved, and the connection takes the form
$\nabla = d - A$ where $A = \sum_{i<j} A_{ij}\, d\log(z_i - z_j)$
and $A_{ij}$ is the Lie-algebraic pairing
$A_{ij} = \Omega_{ij}/(k + h^\vee)$.

The factor $1/(k + h^\vee)$ arises as follows. The bar propagator
$\eta_{ij} = d\log(z_i - z_j)$ enters the MC element $\Theta_\cA$
at degree~$2$, and the collision residue
$r(z) = k\Omega/z$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:affine-propagator-matching})
carries a factor of~$k$. The shadow connection divides by the
modular characteristic $\kappa = \dim(\fg)(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$ to
normalize to a flat connection; for the KZ connection the
conventional normalization is $1/(k + h^\vee)$, which follows from
the relation $r(z)/\kappa = \Omega/(z(k+h^\vee))$ after
accounting for the $\dim(\fg)/(2h^\vee)$ factor in the Casimir
normalization.

For the four-point function of $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ fundamentals:
the Casimir $\Omega$ acts on $V_{1/2} \otimes V_{1/2}$ with
eigenvalue $+1/4$ on the symmetric (triplet, $j=1$) component
and $-3/4$ on the antisymmetric (singlet, $j=0$) component.
The KZ equation on $\mathrm{Conf}_4(\mathbb{P}^1)$, after
M\"obius reduction to $(z_1, z_2, z_3, z_4) = (0, z, 1, \infty)$,
becomes the hypergeometric ODE with the stated parameters
(Etingof--Frenkel--Kirillov~\cite{EFK98}).
The two solutions~\eqref{eq:kz-singlet}--\eqref{eq:kz-triplet} are
verified numerically in \texttt{kz\_conformal\_blocks.py},
function \texttt{verify\_kz\_ode\_4point}: the ODE residual is
$< 10^{-4}$ for $k = 1, 2, 3, 4$ at generic $z$.
The braiding eigenvalues are computed in
\texttt{braiding\_eigenvalues\_sl2} and match the quantum-group
prediction $R_0 = -q^{-3/2}$, $R_1 = q^{1/2}$, confirming the
Drinfeld--Kohno theorem at the eigenvalue level. The braid relation
$B_s B_t B_s = B_t B_s B_t$ is verified numerically in
\texttt{monodromy\_matrices\_4point} with error $< 10^{-10}$.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[Verlinde formula from the shadow complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:verlinde-from-shadow}
\index{Verlinde formula!from shadow complex|textbf}
\index{shadow complex!Verlinde dimension}
\index{modular tensor category!from shadow data}
For $\cA = \hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k$ at positive integer level~$k$,
the genus-$g$ shadow complex
$Q_g(\cA) = H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g}, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))$
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:complementarity})} has dimension
\begin{equation}\label{eq:verlinde-from-shadow}
\dim Q_g(\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k)
= \sum_{j=0}^{k}
 \bigl(S_{0j}\bigr)^{2-2g}
= \sum_{j=0}^{k}
 \biggl(
 \sqrt{\frac{2}{k+2}}\,
 \sin\frac{\pi(j+1)}{k+2}
 \biggr)^{\!2-2g},
\end{equation}
where $S_{jl} = \sqrt{2/(k+2)} \cdot \sin(\pi(j+1)(l+1)/(k+2))$ is
the modular $S$-matrix. This is the Verlinde
formula~\cite{Verlinde} for the dimension of the space of genus-$g$
conformal blocks of $\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ at level~$k$.

At genus~$1$:
$\dim Q_1(\hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k)
= |\{j : 0 \le j \le k\}| = k + 1$,
the number of integrable representations.

The quantum dimensions
$d_j = S_{0j}/S_{00} = \sin(\pi(j+1)/(k+2))/\sin(\pi/(k+2))$
and the total quantum dimension
$\mathcal{D}^2 = \sum_j d_j^2 = 1/S_{00}^2
= (k+2)/(2\sin^2(\pi/(k+2)))$
are extracted from the genus-$1$ shadow datum via the $S$-matrix,
and the fusion coefficients
\begin{equation}\label{eq:verlinde-fusion}
N_{ij}^{\;m}
= \sum_{l=0}^{k}
 \frac{S_{il}\, S_{jl}\, \overline{S_{ml}}}{S_{0l}}
\end{equation}
are nonnegative integers satisfying the truncated
Clebsch--Gordan rule: $N_{ij}^{\;m} = 1$ if
$|i-j| \le m \le \min(i+j, 2k-i-j)$ and $i+j+m$ even, and
$N_{ij}^{\;m} = 0$ otherwise.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The shadow complex $Q_g(\cA) = H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))$
computes the factorization homology of $\bar B(\cA)$ over a
genus-$g$ surface (Theorem~\ref{thm:complementarity}). For
$\cA = \hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k$, the factorization homology over
$\Sigma_g$ coincides with the space of conformal blocks of the WZW
model on $\Sigma_g$, whose dimension is given by the Verlinde
formula.

The derivation from shadow data: the $T$-matrix
$T_{jl} = \delta_{jl} \exp(2\pi i (h_j - c/24))$ with
$h_j = j(j+2)/(4(k+2))$ and $c = 3k/(k+2)$ encodes the
genus-$1$ twist ($\tau \to \tau + 1$).
The $S$-matrix encodes the modular inversion ($\tau \to -1/\tau$).
Together $(S, T)$ generate an $\mathrm{SL}(2, \mathbb{Z})$
representation on the space of characters, which is the
genus-$1$ shadow datum. The genus-$g$ shadow dimension
$\dim Q_g = \sum_j S_{0j}^{2-2g}$ is the trace of the identity
on the TQFT state space associated to $\Sigma_g$, computed by
cutting $\Sigma_g$ into $2g - 2$ pairs of pants (for $g \ge 2$)
and contracting the fusion matrices along the gluing curves.
The computation reduces to the stated formula by the
diagonalization property of the $S$-matrix (Verlinde's
argument~\cite{Verlinde}).

At genus~$1$: $\sum_j S_{0j}^0 = \sum_j 1 = k+1$.

At genus~$0$: $\sum_j S_{0j}^2 = 1$ (unitarity of $S$).

At genus~$2$: $S_{0j} = d_j \cdot S_{00}$, so
$\sum_j S_{0j}^{-2} = S_{00}^{-2} \sum_j d_j^{-2}
= \mathcal{D}^2 \sum_j d_j^{-2}$
(an interesting rationality check).

The fusion coefficients~\eqref{eq:verlinde-fusion} are verified to
be nonnegative integers in \texttt{verlinde\_shadow\_algebra.py},
function \texttt{sl2\_fusion\_coefficients}: for $k = 1, \ldots, 10$,
every $N_{ij}^{\;m}$ rounds to an integer within $10^{-10}$ and
matches the explicit truncated Clebsch--Gordan formula
(\texttt{sl2\_fusion\_rules\_explicit}). The MTC consistency
checks (unitarity $SS^\dagger = I$, $(ST)^3 \propto I$,
quantum dimension positivity $d_j > 0$) are confirmed in
\texttt{shadow\_S\_T\_from\_genus1}. The Verlinde dimension for
$g = 2, 3$ is confirmed to be a positive integer for all
$k \le 20$, and the Reshetikhin--Turaev trefoil invariant
(\texttt{sl2\_RT\_trefoil}) matches the expected quantum Jones
polynomial.
\end{proof}


\begin{remark}[$L_\infty$ brackets and the Yangian deformation]
\label{rem:linfty-yangian-deformation}
\index{L-infinity@$L_\infty$!Yangian deformation}
\index{Yangian!L-infinity structure@$L_\infty$ structure}
\index{shadow depth!Yangian}
The modular convolution algebra
$\fg^{\mathrm{mod}}_\cA = \operatorname{hom}_\alpha(C^!_{\mathrm{ch}},
P^{\mathrm{ch}})$
carries an $L_\infty$ structure with brackets $\ell_k$
(Construction~\ref{constr:explicit-convolution-linfty}). For the
dg-shifted Yangian $\Ydg(\fg)$, these brackets have a transparent
integrable-systems interpretation:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\ell_2$ is the dg Lie bracket, encoding the classical
 $r$-matrix $r(z) = k\Omega/z$
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:cybe-from-mc}). The CYBE is the
 $\ell_2$-Jacobi identity projected to degree~$3$.
\item $\ell_3$ encodes the Drinfeld associator $\Phi_{\mathrm{KZ}}$:
 the homotopy-Jacobi relation
 $\ell_2(\ell_2(x,y),z) \pm \text{cyc} = \ell_1(\ell_3(x,y,z))
 + \ell_3(\ell_1(x), y, z) + \cdots$
 captures the failure of strict Jacobi for the $r$-matrix,
 which is measured by the Drinfeld associator at the quantum
 level. For affine $\hat\fg_k$, this bracket is nonzero
 (class~L: shadow depth $r_{\max} = 3$; see
 Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-archetype-classification}), encoding
 the tree-level cubic shadow $C(\cA)$.
\item $\ell_4$ and higher brackets encode the quartic and
 higher-degree obstructions in the shadow obstruction tower
 $\Theta_\cA^{\le r}$. For the Yangian, the RTT relation
 \[
 R_{12}(u - v)\, T_1(u)\, T_2(v)
 = T_2(v)\, T_1(u)\, R_{12}(u - v)
 \]
 is the \emph{all-degree} MC equation for the monodromy matrix
 $T(u)$, which packages all $\ell_k$ brackets into a single
 generating relation.
\item The depth classification from the $L_\infty$ perspective:
 class~G algebras (Heisenberg) have $\ell_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$
 (strict dg Lie); class~L algebras (affine KM, and hence the
 Yangian) have $\ell_k = 0$ for $k \ge 4$; class~C algebras
 ($\beta\gamma$) terminate at $k = 4$; class~M (Virasoro, $W_N$)
 have all $\ell_k \neq 0$. The Yangian $Y(\fg)$ sits in
 class~L, meaning that the $L_\infty$ structure on its convolution
 algebra is governed by $\ell_2$ and $\ell_3$ alone.
 The vanishing $\ell_k = 0$ for $k \ge 4$
 (Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow-formality-low-degree}) is equivalent
 to the statement that the shadow obstruction tower of $\hat\fg_k$ terminates
 at degree~$3$ (cubic shadow).
\end{enumerate}
These identifications are verified computationally in
\texttt{linf\_modular\_higher.py}: the scalar MC equation at each
degree closes with the binary bracket alone at genus~$0$
(\texttt{scalar\_mc\_binary}); the depth termination is confirmed
for all four archetype classes (\texttt{HigherVectorBracket}); and
the Catalan tree counts $C_k = 1, 2, 5, 14, 42, 132$ for
$\ell_2, \ldots, \ell_7$ match the vertex counts of the
associahedra $K_4, \ldots, K_8$
(\texttt{associahedron\_f\_vector}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Baxter $Q$-operator from MC projection]
\label{rem:baxter-q-from-mc}
\index{Baxter Q-operator@Baxter $Q$-operator!from MC projection|textbf}
\index{transfer matrix!from bar coproduct}
\index{TQ relation!from shadow connection}
The complete XXX integrable structure descends from
$\Theta_\cA$ through genus-$0$ projections.
The classical $r$-matrix
$r(z) = \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:cybe-from-mc})
gives the binary collision data.
The quantum $R$-matrix $R(u)$ of
Proposition~\ref{prop:rmatrix-from-bar-coproduct}
gives the iterated product
$T(u) = \operatorname{Tr}_0 \prod_{i=1}^L R_{0i}(u - a_i)$
(the transfer matrix), and the commutativity
$[T(u), T(v)] = 0$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bethe-from-mc})
follows from coassociativity of the bar coproduct.
The Baxter $Q$-operator is determined by the TQ relation
\[
\Lambda(u)\,Q(u) = a(u)\,Q(u - 1) + d(u)\,Q(u + 1),
\]
where $\Lambda(u)$ is the transfer-matrix eigenvalue and
$a(u)$, $d(u)$ encode the boundary vacuum eigenvalues.
The Bethe ansatz equations are the condition that the
zeros of $Q(u)$ cancel the poles introduced by
the shifts $u \pm 1$.

The chain of projections is:
$\Theta_\cA \xrightarrow{\mathrm{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}} r(z)
\xrightarrow{\text{quantize}} R(u)
\xrightarrow{\mathrm{Tr}_0\prod} T(u)
\xrightarrow{\text{TQ}} Q(u)$.
Each arrow is a successive genus-$0$, degree-$2$ projection
of the MC element, with the quantization step supplied by
the bar coproduct (Proposition~\ref{prop:rmatrix-from-bar-coproduct}).
Verified for $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$ and $\mathfrak{sl}_3$
at chain lengths $L = 2, 3, 4$ in
\texttt{baxter\_q\_from\_mc.py} (45 tests):
the TQ relation holds to numerical precision $< 10^{-10}$
for all Bethe roots.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Ordered chiral center and Bethe wavefunctions]
\label{rem:ordered-center-bethe}
\index{Bethe ansatz!ordered chiral center|textbf}
\index{ordered chiral center!Bethe wavefunctions}
\index{Bethe ansatz!wavefunction from ker(av)}
\index{transfer matrix!from symmetric shadow}
The integrable structures of the preceding results admit a
precise restatement in terms of the ordered chiral center
$Z_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{der,ord}}(\cA)$ and its averaging
map $\av$.

\textbf{1.\@ Degree decomposition = magnon-sector decomposition.}
For $\cA = \hat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2{}_k$ and a spin chain of
length~$L$ on $V = \mathbb{C}^2$, the degree-$L$ ordered
chiral center at genus~$0$ carries the Hilbert space
$V^{\otimes L}$ with the full $PB_L$-monodromy of the KZ
system. The magnon-number decomposition
$V^{\otimes L}
= \bigoplus_{M=0}^{L}
\bigl(\mathbb{C}^2\bigr)^{\otimes L}_{S^z = L/2 - M}$
into sectors of $M$ down spins coincides with the
$\mathfrak{h}$-weight decomposition of the degree-$L$
ordered datum under the Cartan subalgebra $\mathfrak{h}
\subset \mathfrak{sl}_2$.

\textbf{2.\@ Symmetric shadow = transfer-matrix eigenvalues.}
The averaging map $\av_L \colon V^{\otimes L}
\to \operatorname{Sym}^L(V)$ projects the full
$PB_L$-monodromy to its $\Sigma_L$-coinvariant shadow.
The image $\operatorname{Sym}^L(V)$ carries only the scalar
traces of the monodromy matrices: these are the transfer-matrix
eigenvalues $\Lambda(u)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bae-from-mc-stationarity}),
the quantum determinant $\operatorname{qdet}\,T(u)$
(a central element, sitting in the degree-$0$ shadow), and the
energy eigenvalues~\eqref{eq:bethe-energy}.
In the notation of Computation~\ref{comp:bethe-exact},
the TQ relation
$\Lambda(u)\,Q(u) = a(u)\,Q(u-1) + d(u)\,Q(u+1)$
is a relation in the symmetric shadow:
$\Lambda(u)$ is determined by the Baxter polynomial
$Q(u) = \prod_{a=1}^{M}(u - u_a)$ whose roots are the Bethe
roots, and both $\Lambda(u)$ and $Q(u)$ are symmetric functions
of the Bethe roots.

\textbf{3.\@ Kernel of averaging = Bethe wavefunctions.}
The kernel $\ker(\av_L)$ at degree~$L$ has dimension
$2^L - (L + 1)$.
It carries the matrix-valued $PB_L$-monodromy: the Bethe
\emph{wavefunctions}
$|\{u_a\}\rangle = B(u_1) \cdots B(u_M)\,|\Omega\rangle
\in V^{\otimes L}$
(Faddeev~\cite{Faddeev96}), where $B(u)$ is the off-diagonal
entry of the monodromy matrix
$T(u) = \bigl[\begin{smallmatrix} A & B \\ C & D
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr]$.
The wavefunction $|\{u_a\}\rangle$ is a specific
vector in $V^{\otimes L}$ that projects under $\av_L$
to the scalar eigenvalue $\Lambda(u)$; the full
vector-valued datum (the amplitudes on each site of the
chain) is the genuinely $E_1$ content invisible to the
symmetric theory. For distinct Bethe roots, the wavefunctions
span a $\binom{L}{\lfloor L/2 \rfloor}$-dimensional subspace
of $V^{\otimes L}$ (the completeness of the Bethe ansatz),
and this subspace lies in $V^{\otimes L}$, not in its
$\Sigma_L$-coinvariant quotient.

\textbf{4.\@ At integrable level: ordered chiral homology
recovers conformal blocks.}
At positive integer level $k$, the genus-$g$ symmetric shadow
$(\int_{\Sigma_g}^{\mathrm{ord}} \cA)_{\Sigma_n}$ has
dimension given by the Verlinde formula
(Proposition~\ref{prop:verlinde-from-shadow}):
$\dim Q_g = \sum_{j=0}^{k} S_{0j}^{2-2g}$.
The ordered chiral homology
$\int_{\Sigma_g}^{\mathrm{ord}} \cA$ at each degree retains
the full monodromy representation of the mapping class group
$\Gamma_{g,n}$, not merely its character. At genus~$1$, the
$k+1$ integrable representations $V_0, \ldots, V_k$ of
$U_q(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$ with $q = e^{2\pi i/(k+2)}$
provide the basis for the space of conformal blocks; the
ordered theory sees the individual blocks as vectors, while
the symmetric theory sees only the dimension $k+1$.
The genus-$0$ version of this statement is the Drinfeld--Kohno
theorem (Proposition~\ref{prop:kz-from-shadow}): the KZ monodromy
on $V^{\otimes n}$ is the ordered datum, and the braiding
eigenvalues are the symmetric shadow.

The chain of projections
\[
\underbrace{\Theta_\cA}_{\text{MC element}}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\mathrm{degree}\;L\;}
\underbrace{V^{\otimes L},\; PB_L\text{-monodromy}}_{\text{ordered
center: wavefunctions}}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\av_L\;}
\underbrace{\Lambda(u),\; Q(u)}_{\text{symmetric shadow:
eigenvalues, BAE}}
\]
is the bar-complex refinement of the algebraic Bethe ansatz:
the ordered center is the habitat of the full spin-chain Hilbert
space, and the symmetric shadow extracts the integrable
Hamiltonian's spectral data.
\end{remark}

%% =================================================================
%% § THE r-MATRIX AS KOSZUL-DUAL INVERSE
%% =================================================================

\subsection{The \texorpdfstring{$r$}{r}-matrix as Koszul-dual inverse}
\label{subsec:r-matrix-koszul-dual-inverse}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!Koszul-dual inverse|textbf}

The preceding subsection computed the collision residue
$r_\cA(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$ for the standard families. The following
state the categorical content of this identification: the collision
residue is the binary inverse of the bar functor at the level of
twisting morphisms. The spectral $r$-matrix recovers the defining
relations of~$\cA^!$ from the bar coalgebra of~$\cA$; the bar
functor, conversely, encodes those relations as a factorization
coalgebra. This reciprocity is the mechanism by which the RTT
presentation simultaneously defines the algebra and supplies its
Koszul dual.

\begin{theorem}[Collision residue as binary Koszul inverse;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:rmatrix-koszul-inverse}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!binary Koszul inverse|textbf}
\index{Koszul duality!binary inverse via collision residue}
\index{twisting morphism!binary inverse}
\index{collision residue!binary Koszul inverse}
Let~$\cA$ be a modular Koszul chiral algebra on a smooth projective
curve~$X$, with bar coalgebra $\barBch(\cA)$ and Koszul dual
$\cA^! = H^*(\barBch(\cA))^\vee$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{The collision residue determines the universal twisting
 morphism.} The genus-zero binary collision residue of the
 bar-intrinsic MC element~$\Theta_\cA$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})}
 recovers the universal twisting morphism:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:rmatrix-koszul-inverse-twisting}
 r_\cA(z)
 \;=\;
 \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)
 \;=\;
 \pi_\cA|_{\mathrm{degree}\,2}
 \;\in\;
 \mathrm{Tw}(\barBch(\cA),\, \cA).
 \end{equation}
 This is the content of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:collision-residue-twisting}}.
 Under the three bijections
 \textup{(}Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:three-bijections})},
 the twisting morphism $\pi_\cA$ corresponds bijectively to
 the coalgebra structure map $\barBch(\cA) \to \barBch(\cA)$
 \textup{(}the identity\textup{)} and to the algebra morphism
 $\varepsilon\colon \Omegach(\barBch(\cA))
 \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
 \textup{(}the bar-cobar counit\textup{)}.

\item \emph{The $r$-matrix inverts the bar functor at degree~$2$.}
 The bar functor sends the binary chiral bracket
 $\mu^{\mathrm{ch}}\colon \cA \otimes \cA \to \cA$
 to a codifferential on the degree-$2$ component of the bar
 coalgebra. The collision residue reverses this:
 \begin{equation}\label{eq:bar-inverse-degree2}
 \mu^{\mathrm{ch}}(a, b)
 \;=\;
 \operatorname{Res}_{w = z}\,
 r_\cA(a, b)(z, w) \cdot \eta(z, w),
 \end{equation}
 where $\eta(z,w) = d\log(z - w)$ is the logarithmic propagator.
 The bar functor encodes $\mu^{\mathrm{ch}}$ as the codifferential
 $d_{\barB}\colon \barB^1(\cA) \to \barB^2(\cA)$; the collision
 residue extracts $\mu^{\mathrm{ch}}$ from $d_{\barB}$.

\item \emph{RTT self-encoding.}
 For a Yangian $Y(\fg)$, the RTT relation
 $R_{12}(u{-}v)\, T_1(u)\, T_2(v)
 = T_2(v)\, T_1(u)\, R_{12}(u{-}v)$
 is the binary component of the bar codifferential: the
 quadratic relations defining $Y(\fg)$ are exactly the
 degree-$2$ bar relations, and $R(u) \mapsto R^{-1}(u)$ is
 the passage from bar to Koszul dual
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}},
 Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:rtt-is-the-duality-datum})}.
 In this sense, the RTT presentation encodes $Y(\fg)$ as its
 own Koszul duality problem: the collision residue
 extracts~$R(u)$, and the orthogonal complement of the
 $R(u)$-relations gives the $R^{-1}(u)$-relations
 defining $Y(\fg)^! = Y_{-\hbar}(\fg)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i) is the collision-residue theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:collision-residue-twisting}):
the genus-zero binary collision residue of~$\Theta_\cA$ extracts
the universal twisting morphism
$\pi_\cA \in \Tw(\barBch(\cA), \cA)$
via the logarithmic propagator
(Proposition~\ref{prop:twisting-morphism-propagator}).
The three bijections of Corollary~\ref{cor:three-bijections}
give the equivalence with the identity coalgebra map and the
bar-cobar counit.

Part~(ii): the bar differential on the degree-$2$ component
$\barB^2(\cA) = (s^{-1}\cA)^{\otimes 2}$ is
$d_{\barB}([s^{-1}a \mid s^{-1}b])
= s^{-1}(a_{(0)}b) \cdot \eta_{12}$,
where $a_{(0)}b$ is the zeroth OPE product.
The collision residue at degree~$2$ extracts
$\Rescoll_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)(a,b) = a_{(0)}b$
(Construction~\ref{constr:thqg-V-binary-extraction}),
which is the chiral bracket. The composition
$\Rescoll_{0,2} \circ d_{\barB}$ recovers
$\mu^{\mathrm{ch}}$ on the nose.

Part~(iii): for the Yangian $Y(\fg)$ with RTT presentation,
the quadratic relations $\{R_{12}T_1T_2 - T_2T_1R_{12} = 0\}$
are the bar relations at degree~$2$. The orthogonal complement
under the Koszul duality pairing gives the relations of~$Y(\fg)^!$,
which are the $R^{-1}$-relations: $Y(\fg)^! = Y_{-\hbar}(\fg)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:yangian-koszul-dual}). The collision residue
extracts~$R(u)$ from the bar differential, and inversion
$R \mapsto R^{-1}$ is exactly the passage from the bar coalgebra
to the Koszul dual algebra.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The binary inverse as leading term]
\label{rem:rmatrix-koszul-inverse-leading}
\index{Koszul duality!binary inverse as leading term}
Theorem~\ref{thm:rmatrix-koszul-inverse} is a genus-zero,
degree-$2$ statement. The full inverse of the bar functor is
the bar-cobar counit $\varepsilon\colon
\Omegach(\barBch(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
(Theorem~B), which uses collision residues at all degrees.
Higher-degree collision residues
$\Rescoll_{0,k}(\Theta_\cA)$ for $k \geq 3$ encode the
$A_\infty$ corrections: the cubic shadow $\mathfrak{C}$ at
degree~$3$, the quartic resonance class $\mathfrak{Q}$ at
degree~$4$, and so on
(Proposition~\ref{prop:e1-shadow-r-matrix}).
The $r$-matrix inversion is the leading term of this all-degree
inverse; the full content is Verdier intertwining (Theorem~A).
\end{remark}

Theorem~\ref{thm:rmatrix-koszul-inverse} isolates the binary
mechanism. The following theorem relates the $r$-matrix to the $\lambda$-bracket
of~$\cA^!$ under the full bar-cobar adjunction.

\begin{theorem}[The $r$-matrix as Koszul-dual inverse;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:r-matrix-koszul-dual-inverse}
\index{r-matrix@$r$-matrix!Koszul-dual inverse|textbf}
\index{twisting morphism!Koszul-dual inverse}
\index{Koszul duality!r-matrix as inverse@$r$-matrix as inverse}
Let~$\cA$ be a modular Koszul chiral algebra with Koszul dual
$\cA^! = H^*(\barBch(\cA))^\vee$. The collision $r$-matrix
\begin{equation}\label{eq:r-matrix-koszul-inverse-def}
 r_\cA(z)
 \;=\;
 \operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,2}(\Theta_\cA)
 \;\in\;
 \cA^! \,\widehat{\otimes}\, \cA^!\bigl[\![z^{-1}]\!\bigr]
\end{equation}
and the $\lambda$-bracket
$\{a_\lambda b\}_{\cA^!}$ of~$\cA^!$ are functionally inverse
in the following precise sense.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Twisting morphism from $r_\cA(z)$.}
 The $r$-matrix determines a twisting morphism
 $\tau_r \colon \barBch(\cA) \to \cA^!$
 by extracting the degree-$2$ collision data of the
 universal MC element. This twisting morphism encodes
 the binary factorization coupling between $\barBch(\cA)$
 and~$\cA^!$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:thqg-V-collision-twisting}}\textup{)}.

\item \emph{Co-twisting morphism from $\{a_\lambda b\}_{\cA^!}$.}
 The $\lambda$-bracket of~$\cA^!$ determines a co-twisting
 morphism
 $\sigma_\lambda \colon \cA \to \Omegach(\barBch(\cA^!))$
 by embedding the binary OPE data of~$\cA^!$ into the
 cobar construction on the bar complex of~$\cA^!$.
 In the Koszul pair $(\cA, \cA^!)$, the Verdier intertwining
 $\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}(\barBch(\cA)) \simeq
 \barBch(\cA^!)$
 \textup{(}Theorem~A\textup{)} identifies
 $\barBch(\cA^!)$ with the Verdier dual of~$\barBch(\cA)$,
 so $\sigma_\lambda$ is equivalently a map
 $\cA \to \Omegach(\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}(\barBch(\cA)))$.

\item \emph{Inversion.}
 The compositions
 \[
 \Omegach(\barBch(\cA))
 \;\xrightarrow[\varepsilon]{\;\sim\;}\;
 \cA
 \;\xrightarrow{\;\sigma_\lambda\;}\;
 \Omegach(\barBch(\cA^!))
 \]
 and
 \[
 \barBch(\cA)
 \;\xrightarrow{\;\tau_r\;}\;
 \cA^!
 \;\xrightarrow{\;\eta\;}\;
 \Omegach(\barBch(\cA^!))
 \;\xrightarrow[\varepsilon']{\;\sim\;}\;
 \cA^!
 \]
 are quasi-isomorphisms. Here $\varepsilon$ and
 $\varepsilon'$ are the bar-cobar counits
 \textup{(}Theorem~B\textup{)}, and $\eta$ is the
 bar-cobar unit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i) is Theorem~\ref{thm:thqg-V-collision-twisting}:
the genus-zero binary collision residue of~$\Theta_\cA$ is the
universal twisting morphism
$\pi_\cA \in \Tw(\barBch(\cA), \cA)$, and $\tau_r$ is its
projection to the Koszul dual via the identification
$H^*(\barBch(\cA)) \cong (\cA^!)^\vee$.

Part~(ii): the $\lambda$-bracket of any chiral algebra~$\cB$
determines a canonical map
$\cB \to \Omegach(\barBch(\cB))$
as the bar-cobar unit. Apply this to $\cB = \cA^!$.
The Verdier intertwining
$\mathbb{D}_{\mathrm{Ran}}(\barBch(\cA)) \simeq
\barBch(\cA^!)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main})
identifies the target.

Part~(iii): the first composition factors through the
bar-cobar counit $\varepsilon \colon
\Omegach(\barBch(\cA)) \xrightarrow{\sim} \cA$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:higher-genus-inversion} on the Koszul
locus), which is a quasi-isomorphism by Theorem~B.
The second composition factors through the analogous
counit for~$\cA^!$. Both are quasi-isomorphisms because
$\cA$ and $\cA^!$ are chirally Koszul
(the Koszul dual of a Koszul algebra is Koszul;
Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-equivalences-meta}(v)$\Rightarrow$(i)).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Genus-zero binary content]
\label{rem:r-matrix-inverse-genus-zero}
Theorem~\ref{thm:r-matrix-koszul-dual-inverse} is a
genus-zero, degree-$2$ statement: both $r_\cA(z)$ and
$\{a_\lambda b\}_{\cA^!}$ are genus-zero binary data.
Higher-degree collision residues
$\operatorname{Res}^{\mathrm{coll}}_{0,k}(\Theta_\cA)$
for $k \geq 3$ encode the $A_\infty$ corrections
(the cubic shadow, the quartic resonance class, and so on).
The full inverse relationship between $\Theta_\cA$ and
$\Theta_{\cA^!}$ is Verdier intertwining
(Theorem~A\textsubscript{2}).
The $r$-matrix inversion theorem is the leading term
of this all-degree intertwining.
\end{remark}

%% =================================================================
%% § THE SPECTRAL FACTORIZATION BRIDGE
%% =================================================================

\subsection{The spectral factorization bridge}
\label{subsec:spectral-factorization-bridge}
\index{factorization!spectral bridge|textbf}
\index{Yangian!spectral factorization bridge}
\index{Drinfeld class!spectral|textbf}

Consider a line operator $L$ wrapping the real axis in a
holomorphic-topological theory on $\bC \times \bR$. Its
self-OPE is governed by a Maurer--Cartan kernel
$r(z) \in (\cA^! \widehat\otimes \cA^!)(\!(z^{-1})\!)$: a
meromorphic $2$-body interaction on ordered
configurations of points on the line.
The question is whether this kernel exponentiates to an honest
$R$-matrix, or whether something more subtle happens.

An honest factorization quantum group (in the sense of
Latyntsev \cite{Latyntsev23}) demands a strict spectral
$R$-matrix satisfying hexagon and pentagon identities on the nose.
A dg-shifted Yangian as defined in~\S\ref{sec:modular-dg-shifted-yangian}
carries a kernel~$r(z)$ and a twisted coproduct
$\Delta_z$, but no a priori reason for the hexagon to hold
strictly. The deformation lives in a \emph{spectral Drinfeld
class}, a filtered cohomology class measuring
exactly how far the Yangian is from being honestly factorizable.
When this class vanishes (as it does for abelian chiral algebras
and Cartan-diagonal sectors), the Yangian strictifies to an
honest $\Eone$-algebra with an $R$-matrix satisfying the full
Yang--Baxter equation. When the class does not vanish, one obtains
a \emph{quasi-factorization quantum group}: regularized holonomy
data $(R,\Phi)$ satisfying quasi-hexagon relations with a
controlled associator $\Phi(w,z)$, subject to the pentagon
relation from the Stasheff boundary of
$\overline{\Conf}_4^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$.

The results that follow make this picture precise.
The logical chain is:
\begin{center}
\begin{tikzcd}[column sep=1.8em]
\text{dg-shifted Yangian}
 \ar[r]
& \text{bar-horizontal connection}
 \ar[r]
& \text{quasi-factorization QG}
 \ar[r, "\mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}"]
& \text{strict factorization QG.}
\end{tikzcd}
\end{center}

%% ================================================================
%% Bar-horizontal strictification and the KZ connection
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Bar-horizontal strictification}

The first step is to pass from the $A_\infty$ data of the
dg-shifted Yangian to a flat connection on ordered configuration
spaces. The bar complex $B(Y) = T^c(s^{-1}\bar{Y})$ is a
dg coalgebra, and the MC kernel~$r(z)$ acts on it as a
coderivation; the resulting operator is a connection form whose
flatness is equivalent to the $A_\infty$ MC equation.

\begin{definition}[Bar-horizontal strictification]
\label{def:bar-horizontal-strictification}
\index{bar-horizontal strictification|textbf}
Let $Y$ be a residue-bounded complete dg-shifted Yangian
(Definition~\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}) with MC kernel
$r(z) = \sum_{n \ge 1} r_n z^{-n}$.
A \emph{bar-horizontal strictification} of $Y$ is a complete
filtered cochain complex $(V,d_V)$ quasi-isomorphic to the
completed bar coalgebra $\widehat{B}(Y) = \widehat{T}^c(sY)$,
together with continuous degree-zero endomorphisms
\[
 \Omega_{ij}(u) \in \operatorname{End}(V^{\widehat\otimes n})(\!(u^{-1})\!)
 \qquad (1 \le i < j \le n)
\]
satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $[d_V, \Omega_{ij}(u)] = 0$;
\item $[\Omega_{ij}(u), \Omega_{kl}(v)] = 0$
 whenever $\{i,j\} \cap \{k,l\} = \varnothing$;
\item for every triple $i < j < k$, the \emph{spectral
 Kohno relation}
 \[
 [\Omega_{ij}(u), \Omega_{ik}(u+v)]
 + [\Omega_{ij}(u), \Omega_{jk}(v)]
 + [\Omega_{ik}(u+v), \Omega_{jk}(v)] = 0.
 \]
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

Condition~(iii) is the spectral lift of the Kohno infinitesimal
braid relation; its role is to make the following operator
square to zero.

\begin{theorem}[Derived additive KZ connection;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-derived-additive-kz}
\index{KZ connection!derived additive spectral}
Let $(V,\Omega)$ be a bar-horizontal strictification. On the
ordered configuration space
$\Conf_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1) = \{z_1 < \cdots < z_n\}$,
define the total differential
\[
 \bD_n
 \;:=\;
 d_V + d_{\mathrm{dR}}
 - \sum_{1 \le i < j \le n}
 \Omega_{ij}(z_j - z_i)\,d(z_j - z_i).
\]
Then $\bD_n^2 = 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $A_n = \sum_{i<j} \Omega_{ij}(z_j-z_i)\,d(z_j-z_i)$.
Since $d_V^2 = d_{\mathrm{dR}}^2 = 0$ and
$[d_V, \Omega_{ij}(u)] = 0$, the mixed terms vanish:
$[d_V + d_{\mathrm{dR}}, A_n] = 0$
(using $d_{\mathrm{dR}}(f(u)\,du) = 0$). Hence
$\bD_n^2 = A_n \wedge A_n$. Disjoint-pair contributions
vanish by condition~(ii). For each triple $i < j < k$, set
$u = z_j - z_i$ and $v = z_k - z_j$; then every wedge product
from that triple is a multiple of $du \wedge dv$ with
coefficient equal to the spectral Kohno relation, which
vanishes by~(iii).
\end{proof}

The flat connection $\bD_n$ is the KZ connection seen from
the bar side. At the level of the propagator identification
$r(z) = \tau|_{\deg 2}$
(Propositions~\ref{prop:free-propagator-matching}
and~\ref{prop:affine-propagator-matching}), the operators
$\Omega_{ij}$ recover the bar-transported $r$-matrix
insertions on those benchmark surfaces, so the additive KZ
connection is read there as the bar-side realization of the
usual KZ operator on ordered configurations.

\begin{remark}[MZV content of the Drinfeld associator]%
\label{rem:drinfeld-associator-mzv-content}%
\index{Drinfeld associator!MZV content}%
\index{multiple zeta values!Drinfeld associator}%
The parallel transport of $\bD_n$ from $0$ to $1$ on
$\Conf_2^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1) \cong \bA^1 \setminus \{0\}$
yields the Drinfeld associator
$\Phi(A, B) = 1 + \sum_w I(w) \cdot w \in
\hat{\mathcal{U}}(\mathrm{Lie}(A, B))$,
where the coefficient $I(e_0^{a_1-1} e_1 \cdots
e_0^{a_k-1} e_1) = (-1)^k \zeta(a_1, \ldots, a_k)$
is a multiple zeta value (Le--Murakami convention).
The Lie series $\log \Phi$ has coefficients:
\begin{align*}
\text{weight } 2{:}\quad &
\zeta(2) \cdot [A, B], \\
\text{weight } 3{:}\quad &
\zeta(3) \cdot \bigl([A, [A, B]] - [B, [A, B]]\bigr), \\
\text{weight } 4{:}\quad &
\tfrac{\zeta(4)}{4} \cdot
\bigl([A, [A, [A, B]]] + [B, [B, [A, B]]]\bigr) + \cdots
\end{align*}
The group-like property $\Delta(\Phi) = \Phi \otimes \Phi$ and
the pentagon equation are formal consequences of the flatness
$\bD_2^2 = 0$ and the FM compactification structure.
In the shadow obstruction tower language: the associator is the holonomy
datum of the genus-$0$ shadow connection, and its MZV
coefficients encode the shadow obstruction tower invariants in the
Lie-theoretic (weight/depth) coordinates on the space of
periods of~$\cM_{0,n}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-mzv-dictionary} of
Chapter~\ref{chap:arithmetic-shadows}).
The weight-$2$ coefficient $\zeta(2)$ corresponds to~$\kappa$;
the weight-$3$ coefficient $\zeta(3)$ to the cubic shadow~$S_3$;
the weight-$4$ coefficient $\zeta(4)/4$ to the quartic
shadow~$S_4$. For Heisenberg
(class~$\mathbf{G}$, $r(z) = \kappa/z$):
the bar transport is abelian and the associator reduces to
$\Phi^{\mathrm{Heis}} = \exp(\zeta(2) [A, B])$, with all
higher-weight contributions vanishing.
For affine Kac--Moody at level~$k$ (class~$\mathbf{L}$):
the full associator appears, but the shadow obstruction tower terminates
at degree~$3$, so only $\zeta(2)$ and $\zeta(3)$ contribute
from the intrinsic algebra data (higher weights arise from
the representation theory via the Casimir insertion).
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% Boundary residue theorem
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Boundary residue and FM extension}

The next step is to extend the flat connection to the
Fulton--MacPherson compactification, where collision of points
is permitted. The condition is that the connection form have
at worst logarithmic singularities.

\begin{theorem}[Boundary residue theorem; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-boundary-residue}
\index{boundary residue!spectral connection}
\index{Fulton--MacPherson!logarithmic extension}
Assume that each $\Omega_{ij}(u)$ has at most a simple pole at
$u = 0$:
\[
 \Omega_{ij}(u) = \frac{r_{ij}}{u} + \Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{reg}}(u).
\]
Then the connection form $A_n$ of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:spectral-derived-additive-kz}} extends
logarithmically to the FM compactification
$\overline{\Conf}_n^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$. The residue along
the boundary divisor $D_S$ parametrizing collision of a subset
$S \subset \{1,\ldots,n\}$ is
\[
 \operatorname{Res}_{D_S}(A_n)
 = \sum_{\substack{i < j \\ i,j \in S}} r_{ij}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Near $D_S$ introduce coordinates $z_i = z_* + t\xi_i$ for
$i \in S$, where $t = 0$ cuts out the boundary and the
$\xi_i$ are pairwise distinct. Then for $i,j \in S$,
\[
 \Omega_{ij}(z_j - z_i)\,d(z_j - z_i)
 =
 \Bigl(\frac{r_{ij}}{t(\xi_j - \xi_i)} + \text{reg.}\Bigr)
 \bigl((\xi_j-\xi_i)\,dt + t\,d(\xi_j-\xi_i)\bigr)
 =
 r_{ij}\,\frac{dt}{t} + \text{log.}
\]
Pairs not entirely in $S$ remain regular in~$t$. Summing
over $i < j$ in $S$ gives the residue formula.
\end{proof}

%% ================================================================
%% Transfer of flat connections
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Transfer of flat spectral connections}

Homotopy transfer from the bar level to cohomology (or a minimal
model) preserves flatness.

\begin{theorem}[Transfer of flat spectral connections;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-transfer-flat}
\index{homotopy transfer!flat spectral connections}
Let
\[
 (H,d_H)
 \xrightarrow{\;i\;}
 (V,d_V)
 \xrightarrow{\;p\;}
 (H,d_H)
\]
be a filtered strong deformation retract with homotopy~$h$
satisfying $pi = \mathrm{id}_H$ and
$ip = \mathrm{id}_V + d_V h + h d_V$.
Suppose $V \otimes \Omega^\bullet(\Conf_n^{\mathrm{ord}})$
carries the flat total differential
$\bD_V = (d_V + d_{\mathrm{dR}}) - A_V$.
Then the homological perturbation series converges and yields
a flat transferred differential
\[
 \bD_H = (d_H + d_{\mathrm{dR}}) - A_H,
 \qquad
 A_H = p\,A_V(1 - h\,A_V)^{-1}i
 = \sum_{m \ge 0} p\,A_V\,(h\,A_V)^m\,i.
\]
In particular, every flat bar-level spectral connection
descends functorially to cohomology.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Tensor the strong deformation retract with
$\Omega^\bullet(\Conf_n^{\mathrm{ord}})$; since
$d_{\mathrm{dR}}$ commutes with $i,p,h$, the same data form a
retract for the base differential $d_V + d_{\mathrm{dR}}$.
Take $\delta = -A_V$ as the perturbation. Because $\delta$
lowers the filtration, the standard perturbation lemma converges
and the transferred total differential squares to zero
($(d_V + d_{\mathrm{dR}} + \delta)^2 = \bD_V^2 = 0$).
Replacing $\delta$ by $-A_V$ gives the stated formula.
\end{proof}

%% ================================================================
%% The quasi-factorization theorem
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{The quasi-factorization theorem}

The regularized holonomy of the flat connection from
Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-derived-additive-kz} produces
an $R$-matrix at $n = 2$ and an associator at $n = 3$.
The central result is that these data form a
quasi-factorization quantum group.

\begin{definition}[Regularized holonomy data]
\label{def:regularized-holonomy-data}
\index{holonomy!regularized spectral}
Assume that the flat connections of
Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-derived-additive-kz} are
pronilpotent at the boundary. For $n = 2$, let
\[
 R(u) \in 1 + F^1 A^{\widehat\otimes 2}
\]
be the regularized holonomy from the positive tangential
basepoint at collision to the interior point with difference
$u = z_2 - z_1$. For $n = 3$, let
$\Phi(w,z) \in 1 + F^2 A^{\widehat\otimes 3}$ be the
regularized parallel transport between the two tangential
basepoints corresponding to the bracketings $(12)3$ and
$1(23)$ in $\overline{\Conf}_3^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$.
We call $(R,\Phi)$ the \emph{spectral quasi-factorization
datum}.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Quasi-factorization theorem;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-quasi-factorization}
\index{quasi-factorization quantum group|textbf}
Every residue-bounded complete dg-shifted Yangian equipped
with a bar-horizontal strictification canonically determines a
spectral quasi-factorization quantum group. More precisely,
the regularized holonomy data $(R,\Phi)$ of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:regularized-holonomy-data}} satisfy:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item quasi-hexagon relations on
 $\overline{\Conf}_3^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$; and
\item the pentagon relation on the codimension-one Stasheff
 cell complex of $\overline{\Conf}_4^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The boundary strata of
$\overline{\Conf}_3^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$ for the
bracketings $(12)3$ and $1(23)$ admit collar neighborhoods
in which the regularized holonomy factors as the ordered
product of two-body holonomies. The comparison between
these two collar factorizations is the comparison holonomy
$\Phi(w,z)$, yielding the quasi-hexagon.
For $n = 4$, the codimension-one boundary strata of
$\overline{\Conf}_4^{\mathrm{ord}}(\bA^1)$ form the
Stasheff pentagon. Flatness of $\bD_4$ implies that the
total regularized transport around its boundary is the
identity, which is the pentagon relation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[CG interpretation]
\label{rem:spectral-bridge-cg}
In the CG framework of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:ainfty-yb-consistency}, the
quasi-factorization theorem says: the MC element
$\tau \in \operatorname{Conv}(\bar B(Y), Y^!)$ is an
\emph{infinitesimal} factorization datum. Its
exponentiation to holonomy is the passage from the
convolution algebra to the factorization quantum group.
The quasi-hexagon defect $\Phi$ is the image of the
$A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter defect under this exponentiation.
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% Spectral Drinfeld class and strictification
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{The spectral Drinfeld class}

The obstruction to strictifying a quasi-factorization quantum
group into an honest one lives in a filtered cohomology theory.

\begin{definition}[Spectral cochain complex and Drinfeld class]
\label{def:spectral-drinfeld-class}
\index{Drinfeld class!spectral!definition}
Define the spectral cochain groups
\[
 C^2_{\mathrm{spec}}(A) = \{g(u) \in A^{\widehat\otimes 2}\},
 \qquad
 C^3_{\mathrm{spec}}(A) = \{\phi(w,z) \in A^{\widehat\otimes 3}\},
\]
with linearized spectral differential
\[
 (\delta g)(w,z)
 =
 1 \otimes g(z)
 + (\mathrm{id} \otimes \Delta_z)g(w)
 - (\Delta_w \otimes \mathrm{id})g(z)
 - g(w) \otimes 1.
\]
Denote the resulting cohomology by $H^3_{\mathrm{spec}}(A)$.
If
$\Phi(w,z) = 1 + \phi_n(w,z) \pmod{F^{n+1}}$
with $\phi_n$ the first nontrivial term, its class
\[
 \mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}(A,\Omega)
 := [\phi_n]
 \in H^3_{\mathrm{spec}}(\mathrm{gr}^n A)
\]
is the \emph{spectral Drinfeld class}.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Strictification by spectral cohomology;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-strictification-cohomology}
\index{strictification!spectral cohomology}
Suppose $\Phi(w,z) = 1 + \phi_n(w,z) \pmod{F^{n+1}}$ with
$n \ge 2$. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\phi_n$ is a $3$-cocycle in the spectral complex;
\item under a spectral twist
 $G_n(u) = 1 + g_n(u) \pmod{F^{n+1}}$, one has
 $\phi_n \mapsto \phi_n + \delta g_n$;
\item if $[\phi_n] = 0$ in
 $H^3_{\mathrm{spec}}(\mathrm{gr}^n A)$, a twist
 kills $\phi_n$ modulo $F^{n+1}$;
\item if $H^3_{\mathrm{spec}}(\mathrm{gr}^n A) = 0$ for all
 $n \ge 2$, there exists a filtered twist~$G$ making
 $\Phi^G = 1$, and the quasi-factorization datum
 strictifies to an honest spectral factorization $R$-matrix.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand the pentagon relation in the first nontrivial filtration
degree. All nonlinear terms lie in higher filtration, so
$\phi_n$ satisfies the linearized pentagon and is a cocycle.
The twist formula for the quasi-associator at degree~$n$
yields addition by $\delta g_n$. Killing the leading term
and iterating recursively proves~(iii) and~(iv).
\end{proof}

The Yangian-to-factorization bridge is a filtered obstruction problem: the passage
\[
 \text{dg-shifted Yangian}
 \;\longrightarrow\;
 \text{spectral quasi-factorization QG}
 \;\overset{\mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}}{\longrightarrow}\;
 \text{strict factorization QG}
\]
is canonical in the first arrow and obstructed by a concrete
spectral cohomology class in the second.

%% ================================================================
%% Triangle localization: universal coefficient 1/2
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Low-filtration localization: universal
coefficients $\frac{1}{2}$ and $\frac{1}{3}$}

The first two filtration sectors where the spectral Drinfeld
class can be computed explicitly are the adjacent-root triangle
(filtration~$2$) and the root-quadrilateral (filtration~$3$)
sectors. Both yield universal rational coefficients.

Let $i \sim j$ be adjacent simple roots in a type-$A_2$ Levi.
Write $E_{ij} = [E_i, E_j]$ and $F_{ij} = [F_j, F_i]$, and
on three tensor factors define the left triangle vector
$T_{ij}^L = E_{ij}^{(1)} F_i^{(2)} F_j^{(3)}$.

\begin{theorem}[Triangle localization; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-triangle-localization}
\index{triangle localization|textbf}
\index{universal coefficient!1/2@$1/2$}
Let
$S_{12}(w) = \rho_i(w)\,E_i^{(1)}F_i^{(2)} + \cdots$ and
$S_{13}(w+z) = \rho_j(w+z)\,E_j^{(1)}F_j^{(3)} + \cdots$.
The projection to the oriented left triangle sector of the
commutator $\frac{1}{2}[S_{12}(w), S_{13}(w+z)]$ is
\[
 \tfrac{1}{2}\,\rho_i(w)\,\rho_j(w+z)\,T_{ij}^L
 \;-\;
 \tfrac{1}{2}\,\rho_j(w)\,\rho_i(w+z)\,T_{ji}^L,
\]
with the analogous formula on the right. Under the rational
ansatz $\rho_\alpha(u) = c_\alpha/u$ with
$c_i = c_j = c_{ij} = 1$, the adjacent-root rigidity equations
\textup{(}equating coproduct and product contributions in the
hexagon\textup{)} are uniquely solved by the universal triangle
coefficient
\[
 \boxed{\;\lambda_{\mathrm{tri}} = \tfrac{1}{2}.\;}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The only nonzero commutators landing in the triangle sector
are $[E_i^{(1)}F_i^{(2)}, E_j^{(1)}F_j^{(3)}] =
E_{ij}^{(1)}F_i^{(2)}F_j^{(3)}$ and its orientation reversal.
Projecting the hexagon defect to this sector and matching
coproduct contributions from the composite-root generator
$X_{ij}$ yields the displayed rigidity equations, which in the
normalized rational ansatz give $\lambda = c_i c_j / (2 c_{ij})
= 1/2$.
\end{proof}

For the next filtration, let $i \sim j \sim k$ be a chain
of simple roots of type~$A_3$ with $i$ not adjacent to~$k$.
Define $E_{ijk} = [E_{ij}, E_k] = [E_i, E_{jk}]$ and the
corresponding lowering operators, and set
$Q_{ijk}^L = E_{ijk}^{(1)} F_i^{(2)} F_j^{(3)} F_k^{(4)}$.

\begin{theorem}[Quadrilateral localization; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-quadrilateral-localization}
\index{quadrilateral localization|textbf}
\index{universal coefficient!1/3@$1/3$}
The projection of
$\log\bigl(e^{X_i^{12}(u)}\, e^{X_j^{13}(u+v)}\,
e^{X_k^{14}(u+v+t)}\bigr)$
to the left quadrilateral sector is
\[
 \tfrac{1}{3}\,\rho_i(u)\,\rho_j(u+v)\,\rho_k(u+v+t)
 \;Q_{ijk}^L.
\]
The universal coefficient $\frac{1}{3}$ arises from the
class-$3$ ordered BCH formula: in a class-$3$ nilpotent Lie
algebra with $[X,Z] = 0$, the multilinear $XYZ$-part of
$\log(e^X e^Y e^Z)$ is $\frac{1}{3}[X,[Y,Z]]$. Under the
rational ansatz with $c_i = c_j = c_k = c_{ijk} = 1$, the
quadrilateral rigidity equations are uniquely solved by
\[
 \boxed{\;\lambda_{\mathrm{quad}} = \tfrac{1}{3}.\;}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since $i$ and $k$ are nonadjacent, $[X_i^{12}, X_k^{14}] = 0$.
Lemma~\ref{lem:class3-bch-spectral} below gives the
multilinear $XYZ$-part as $\frac{1}{3}[X,[Y,Z]]$. Computing
$[Y,Z] = \rho_j(u+v)\,\rho_k(u+v+t)\,E_{jk}^{(1)}
F_j^{(3)} F_k^{(4)}$ and then
$[X,[Y,Z]] = \rho_i(u)\,\rho_j(u+v)\,\rho_k(u+v+t)\,Q_{ijk}^L$
gives the localization formula. Matching with the four-body
coproduct projection and using the rational ansatz yields
$\lambda = 1/3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Class-$3$ ordered BCH coefficient; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:class3-bch-spectral}
In a class-$3$ nilpotent Lie algebra with $[X,Z] = 0$,
\[
 \operatorname{mult}_{XYZ}\log(e^X e^Y e^Z)
 = \tfrac{1}{3}[X,[Y,Z]].
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write $U = \log(e^X e^Y) = X + Y + \frac{1}{2}[X,Y]
+ \frac{1}{12}[X,[X,Y]] + \frac{1}{12}[Y,[Y,X]]$.
Then $\log(e^U e^Z) = U + Z + \frac{1}{2}[U,Z] + \cdots$,
and extracting the multilinear $XYZ$-part gives
$\frac{1}{4}[[X,Y],Z] + \frac{1}{12}[X,[Y,Z]]
+ \frac{1}{12}[Y,[X,Z]]$.
When $[X,Z] = 0$, Jacobi gives $[[X,Y],Z] = [X,[Y,Z]]$ and
the sum reduces to $\frac{1}{3}[X,[Y,Z]]$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Shift transport, not shift invariance]
\label{rem:spectral-shift-transport}
\index{shift transport!spectral}
A naive ``shift-invariance'' statement at mixed-root level is
false if interpreted coefficientwise. The shift changes local
coefficients by explicit ratios of shift characters at different
spectral arguments. What is invariant is the
\emph{obstruction class} after transport by the shift cocycle.
In particular, the shifted triangle transport coefficients
are uniquely determined by
\[
 \kappa_{ij}^{L,\mu}(w,z)
 =
 \frac{\chi_i^\mu(w)\,\chi_j^\mu(w+z)}{\chi_{ij}^\mu(w)}
 \;\kappa_{ij}^{L,0}(w,z),
\]
and the analogous quadrilateral law holds at filtration~$3$
\ifannalsedition\else
(cf.\ Remark~\ref{rem:transport-not-invariance}
in the source material)
\fi. No new independent obstruction class
appears in filtrations $2$ or~$3$.
\end{remark}

%% ================================================================
%% Cartan shift theory and exact Drinfeld class
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Cartan shift theory and exact Drinfeld class}

The Cartan-diagonal sector admits an explicit computation
showing that the spectral Drinfeld class is exact: the
associator defect is a coboundary.

\begin{theorem}[Cartan-diagonal Drinfeld class is exact;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-cartan-diagonal-exact}
\index{Drinfeld class!Cartan-diagonal exactness}
\index{Cartan shift!cocycle}
Let $H$ be a completed commutative primitive Cartan bialgebra
with primitive generators $h_1, \ldots, h_\ell$, and let
$\phi_i(u) = \log H_i(u)$ be the shifted Cartan currents.
Define the formal bicharacter
\[
 F_\mu(u)
 = \exp\!\Bigl(\sum_{i=1}^\ell \phi_i(u)\,h_i \otimes h_i\Bigr).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $F_\mu(u)$ satisfies the cocycle identities
 $(\mathrm{id} \otimes \Delta)F_\mu = F_\mu^{12} F_\mu^{13}$
 and
 $(\Delta \otimes \mathrm{id})F_\mu = F_\mu^{13} F_\mu^{23}$
 \textup{(}since $\Delta h_i = h_i \otimes 1 + 1 \otimes h_i$
 and the $h_i$ commute\textup{)}.
\item The Cartan gauge twist
 $G_{\mu,n} = \exp(-S_{\mu,n})$ with
 $S_{\mu,n} = \sum_{a<b} \sum_i \phi_i(z_b - z_a)\,
 h_i^{(a)} h_i^{(b)}$
 transforms an unshifted derived KZ connection $\bD_n^0$
 into the shifted connection
 $\bD_n^\mu = G_{\mu,n}\,\bD_n^0\,G_{\mu,n}^{-1}$,
 which has connection form
 $A_n^\mu = A_n^0 + \sum_{a<b} \sum_i
 \phi_i'(z_b-z_a)\,h_i^{(a)}h_i^{(b)}\,d(z_b-z_a)$.
\item On a Cartan-diagonal line $L_\lambda$, the three-body
 quasi-hexagon defect is
 \[
 \Phi_{\mu,\lambda}^{\mathrm{sh}}(w,z)
 =
 \frac{R_{\mu,\lambda}^{\mathrm{sh}}(w+z)}
 {R_{\mu,\lambda}^{\mathrm{sh}}(w)\,
 R_{\mu,\lambda}^{\mathrm{sh}}(z)},
 \]
 whose logarithm
 $\sum_i \lambda_i^2\bigl(\phi_i(w+z) - \phi_i(w) - \phi_i(z)
 \bigr)$
 is manifestly a coboundary. Hence the Cartan-diagonal
 contribution to the spectral Drinfeld class is exact.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part~(i) follows from the splitting of the exponent under
the cocommutative coproduct. Part~(ii) is a direct gauge
computation using the commutation hypothesis on the Cartan
sector. Part~(iii): the defect $\phi_i(w+z) - \phi_i(w)
- \phi_i(z)$ is by definition $\delta(\phi_i)$ in the
spectral complex.
\end{proof}

The first genuine shifted examples (the framed $A_1$ shifted
Yangian and the staircase shifted Yangians of finite type~$A$,
relevant to the DK-4 frontier of
Remark~\ref{rem:modular-yangian-dk}) all have
Cartan-diagonal sectors in which the shift produces a visible
three-body logarithmic defect but no cohomological obstruction.

%% ================================================================
%% Abelian strictification and residue-bounded completion
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{Abelian strictification and completion}

Two cases where the spectral Drinfeld class vanishes
automatically deserve separate statements.

\begin{theorem}[Abelian strictification; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-abelian-strictification}
\index{strictification!abelian}
If all coefficients of the suspended kernel
$\widetilde{r}(z)$ supercommute, $m_k = 0$ for $k \ge 3$,
and the underlying coproduct is cocommutative, then
\[
 R(z) = \exp_\star(\widetilde{r}(z))
\]
converges and defines an honest spectral $R$-matrix on the
completed bialgebra underlying~$Y$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The infinitesimal coassociativity identities exponentiate
because all coefficients commute, yielding the hexagon.
Cocommutativity gives almost cocommutativity automatically.
\end{proof}

This covers the free/$\beta\gamma$ propagator matching of
Proposition~\ref{prop:free-propagator-matching}: the abelian
kernel $r(z) = \mathbb{1} \otimes \mathbb{1}/z$ strictifies
immediately.

\begin{theorem}[Residue-bounded completion; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-residue-bounded-completion}
\index{residue-bounded completion}
Let $Y = \varprojlim_N Y_N$ be residue-bounded and complete,
with each $Y_N$ quadratic-Koszul and the inverse system
$\{H^m(\bar B(Y_N))\}_N$ Mittag--Leffler. Then the completed
coderivation $D = d_B + I_{\widetilde{r}}$ converges
continuously on $\widehat{B}(Y)$, satisfies $D^2 = 0$, and
the completed cobar comparison
\[
 \Omega\widehat{B}(Y) \;\longrightarrow\; Y
\]
is a quasi-isomorphism.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Residue-boundedness ensures that on each filtration quotient only
finitely many residues contribute, so the coderivation converges.
The three-particle obstruction identity (the assertion that
$D^2|_{\text{length}\,3} = I_{\mathfrak{Y}_{\widetilde{r}}}$
with $\mathfrak{Y}_{\widetilde{r}}$ the $A_\infty$ Yang--Baxter
defect) implies $D^2 = 0$ quotientwise. Separatedness passes
this to the inverse limit. Koszulness and Mittag--Leffler
pass the quotientwise bar-cobar quasi-isomorphisms to the
completion.
\end{proof}

This is the completed version of
Remark~\ref{rem:completion-four-checks}: checks~(1)--(3)
of the Yangian tower completion are exactly the hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-residue-bounded-completion}.

%% ================================================================
%% Exact free transport
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{The exact free model}

The free model admits a closed-form transport formula.

\begin{proposition}[Exact free transport; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:spectral-exact-free-transport}
\index{free model!exact transport}
Let $\Theta(x,y) = \Psi(x) \otimes X(y) - X(x) \otimes \Psi(y)$
be the free two-body kernel.
Then $\Theta(x,y)^2 = 0$, so the connection
$\nabla_{\mathrm{free}} = d - \Theta(x,y)/(u + x - y)\,du$
integrates exactly with transport
\[
 T(u,u_0)
 = 1 + \Theta(x,y)\,\log\frac{u + x - y}{u_0 + x - y}.
\]
The local monodromy around $u + x - y = 0$ is
$M_{\mathrm{loop}} = 1 + 2\pi i\,\Theta(x,y)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since $\Theta^2 = 0$, the matrix exponential truncates:
$\exp(\Theta\,\log(\cdots)) = 1 + \Theta\,\log(\cdots)$.
Differentiating gives the transport equation. The monodromy
follows from the $2\pi i$ increment of the logarithm.
\end{proof}

%% ================================================================
%% Conditional strictification criterion
%% ================================================================
\subsubsection{The conditional strictification criterion}

The preceding results assemble into a single criterion for
a shifted dg-shifted Yangian to admit a full $\Eone$-chiral
realization.

\begin{theorem}[Conditional strictification criterion;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:spectral-conditional-strictification}
\index{strictification!conditional criterion|textbf}
Let $\Ydg_\cA$ be a residue-bounded complete dg-shifted Yangian
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dg-shifted-yangian}}\textup{)}.
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(C\arabic*)}]
\item\label{item:strict-C1}
 the unshifted dg object strictifies to a factorization quantum
 group with spectral $R$-matrix $R_0$
 \textup{(}i.e.\ $\mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}(A, \Omega_0)
 = 0$\textup{)};
\item\label{item:strict-C2}
 the shift is implemented by the Cartan cocycle of
 Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:spectral-cartan-diagonal-exact}};
\item\label{item:strict-C3}
 the infinitesimal logarithm of the shifted spectral transport
 agrees with the dg kernel after residue-bounded completion
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:spectral-residue-bounded-completion}}\textup{)}; and
\item\label{item:strict-C4}
 the spectral Drinfeld classes
 $\mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}(\mathrm{gr}^n A)$ vanish for
 all $n \ge 2$
 \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:spectral-strictification-cohomology}}\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the shifted dg-shifted Yangian admits a completed
$\Eone$-chiral/factorization realization whose representation
category is that of an honest spectral factorization quantum
group.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Condition~\ref{item:strict-C1} gives a strict spectral object
at the unshifted level.
Condition~\ref{item:strict-C2} transports it to a shifted
quasi-factorization datum via the Cartan gauge twist.
Condition~\ref{item:strict-C4} then allows recursive
strictification of the shifted quasi-associator
(Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-strictification-cohomology}(iv)).
Condition~\ref{item:strict-C3} upgrades finite-stage compatibility
to the full completed statement via
Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-residue-bounded-completion}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of conditions C1--C4]
\label{rem:spectral-c1c4-status}
\index{strictification!status of conditions}
For the $\mathfrak{sl}_N$ Yangian tower:
\begin{itemize}
\item \ref{item:strict-C1} holds at
 the evaluation locus by the proved DK-0/1 comparison
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:derived-dk-yangian});
 extending this to an unshifted completed strict spectral object is
 additional bridge input. B2
 (Remark~\ref{rem:completion-four-checks}) supplies the completed dg
 side of that comparison, but not by itself the full unshifted
 spectral/factorization strictification required by
 \ref{item:strict-C1}.
\item \ref{item:strict-C2} holds for all framed and staircase
 shifts by construction.
\item \ref{item:strict-C3} is the completed compatibility upgrade:
 Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-residue-bounded-completion} promotes the
 residue-bounded finite-stage compatibility to the completed
 bar/cobar statement once a completed dg model is in hand, while on
 the standard RTT lane the H-level realization/comparison packet of
 Remark~\ref{rem:completion-four-checks} supplies the dg side of that
 comparison. Thus \ref{item:strict-C3} is not identical to
 check~(4) alone.
\item \ref{item:strict-C4} is \textbf{proved for all simple Lie algebras}
 (Volume~II, Theorem~thm:complete-strictification):
 root multiplicity one forces the spectral Drinfeld class to vanish
 at every filtration, via root-space one-dimensionality and the Jacobi
 collapse lemma. In filtrations~$2$ and~$3$, the vanishing also
 follows from the triangle and quadrilateral localization theorems.
 The true remaining frontier is Kac--Moody algebras with root
 multiplicities~$> 1$, where root-space one-dimensionality fails.
\end{itemize}
Thus, once an unshifted completed strict spectral object satisfying
\ref{item:strict-C1} is supplied, the remaining new work in the
conditional strictification criterion is the completed compatibility
package \ref{item:strict-C3}; condition \ref{item:strict-C4} is
proved unconditionally for all simple types.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Relation to the DK square]
\label{rem:spectral-bridge-dk-square}
\index{Drinfeld--Kohno!DK square!spectral bridge relation}
The spectral factorization bridge provides a concrete pathway
for the B4 target of the Bridge Theorem
(Remark~\ref{rem:bridge-theorem-programme}). The DK square of
Remark~\ref{rem:dk-square-geometry} relates the $\Eone$-chiral
factorization category to the evaluation-locus quantum group.
The present construction extends this to the completed Yangian
tower: the spectral $R$-matrix from the conditional
strictification criterion is the candidate bridge datum connecting the
completed bar-cobar tower
$\Omega(\widehat{\bar B}(Y)) \xrightarrow{\sim} Y$
(Remark~\ref{rem:completion-four-checks})
to Latyntsev's factorization-quantum-group side
\cite{Latyntsev23}. Once the residual DK-4/5 extension/completion packet and the
unshifted completed strict spectral input of
Condition~\ref{item:strict-C1} are supplied, the chain
\[
 \text{$\Eone$-chiral fact.\ category}
 \;\xrightarrow{\text{DK-0..3}}\;
 \Ydg(\mathfrak{sl}_N)
 \;\xrightarrow{\text{bar-horiz.}}\;
 \text{spectral quasi-fact.\ QG}
 \;\xrightarrow{\mathfrak{D}_{\mathrm{spec}}}\;
 \text{strict fact.\ QG}
\]
becomes a concrete programme. On that conditional surface, the
remaining intrinsic strictification obstruction is concentrated in the
spectral Drinfeld class at filtration~$\ge 4$.
\end{remark}
